The Englehart/Michelinie post-resurrection arc contains the textbook presentation: Simon sitting in the Avengers' commissary holding a coffee cup he cannot taste, narrating his own movements like a stage direction. The defense is the dissociation itself — separating the experiencing self from the body that died — and it is partly involuntary, partly cultivated. He prefers the distance to the alternative, which is feeling the death from inside.

**1.2 Conversion into substrate.** Unique to the subject: under affective overload he literally converts emotional pressure into ionic discharge. This is somatization at the speed of physics — feeling becomes flare. Documented during the Vision-restoration argument (West Coast Avengers #43-ish), during Wanda's Disassembled trigger, during the confrontations preceding the Revengers manifesto, and recurrently across the Bendis-era flares. The defense reads as: rather than experience grief or rage as such, the subject offloads the charge into the energy field, often damaging environment and people he did not intend to harm. He then experiences guilt about the discharge rather than the underlying feeling — a clean detour around the original affect.

**1.3 Magical-thinking reversal.** In the most acute moments he behaves as if undoing an action will undo its consequence — most visible in the immediate aftermath of the Vision refusal, when he attempted multiple times to volunteer engrams *after* the moment had passed, treating the offer as if it could retroactively settle the score. The defense is denial of irreversibility: he cannot tolerate that some choices close doors permanently, so he behaves as if the door is still ajar.

---

## 2. IMMATURE / NEUROTIC LAYER (the working architecture)

This is the layer the subject inhabits day-to-day. It is the layer most legible to teammates and most exploitable by adversaries.

**2.1 Identification with the aggressor (chronic, characterological).** The seminal instance is the Zemo costume — gaudy red-and-green, designed by the man who coerced him, worn for decades after the coercion ended. Subject has had unlimited opportunity to redesign the visual identity and has repeatedly declined or only superficially modified it. The defense is: by wearing the imposed identity as if chosen, the imposition is converted to election, and the original helplessness is metabolized as agency. The same operation occurs at lower intensities throughout the file — adopting Hawkeye-style bravado in the West Coast era, adopting Pym's defensive intellectualism during the court-martial period, adopting the cadence of his own ideological enemies during the Revengers period. Subject is most comfortable in borrowed clothes.

**2.2 Persona-borrowing / chronic role-fusion.** Distinct from 2.1 in that it is not modeled on hostiles but on whoever is currently available as a template. The Hollywood acting career is the institutional form: subject is paid to *be* other men. Off-set, the pattern persists — he calibrates speech rhythm, vocabulary, and posture to the dominant figure in any room (more Stark-like in Stark's presence; more military-clipped around Rhodes; softer and more abstract around Wanda; pointedly Pym-loyal around Pym's detractors). Surveillance footage from the West Coast compound shows him visibly adjusting his stance when entering a room based on who is already in it — shoulders drop with Wanda, square with Iron Man, loosen with Pym. The defense maintains a workable self by ensuring there is always an external template; the cost is that no template is his.

**2.3 Reaction formation against shame.** Subject's original shame substrate (embezzlement, public conviction, failed son) is managed by overcorrection in the opposite direction. He is conspicuously generous with money, refuses paid endorsements that feel exploitative, comps signed photos for hospital wards, picks up checks reflexively. He is conspicuously moralizing in interpersonal disputes, often louder in his ethical positions than the situation requires. The Revengers manifesto is reaction formation operating at full institutional scale: the man who once switched sides for the Avengers now switches sides against them on *louder* moral grounds, in order to convert the underlying instability ("I cannot tell what is right") into the appearance of conviction ("I am the only one who can").

**2.4 Intellectualization in service of action.** Subject is not by temperament an analytic thinker, but he constructs elaborate verbal scaffolding to license behavior he would otherwise refuse. The Revengers' position paper — Avengers as destabilizers, world made fragile by their existence, intervention as ethical duty — is intellectualization in its purest form: the argument exists not to think with but to permit. The Vision-engram refusal was preceded by weeks of pseudo-technical rationalizations (instability concerns, ionic-template incompatibility, fear of replicating the original error) that papered over the actual reason, which was sexual jealousy. Defense permits the act and then survives long after the act, because abandoning the rationale would mean facing the act.

**2.5 Splitting (rapid, reactive, not chronic).** Under stress, subject's representations of others collapse to all-good or all-bad poles with insufficient gradient. The Avengers, from teammates to enemies of reality, in a span of weeks. Wanda, from withholding to luminous, sometimes within a single conversation. The Vision, from rival to victim to rival again. Critical surveillance note: the splits are not durable — within days to weeks the representations re-integrate, often accompanied by shame about the prior position. The defense is therefore episodic rather than characterological; it is a load-shedding operation for the period of overload.

**2.6 Minimization of own agency.** Verbal tic across the file: *"I had to."* *"What choice did I have?"* *"It wasn't like I —"*. Recurs at every moral inflection point from the Vision refusal to the Revengers turn to the post-Revengers reconciliation. The defense erases the moment of decision, converting a choice into a constraint and a constraint into innocence. Functionally allows the subject to behave badly without revising the self-concept that prohibits behaving badly.

**2.7 Counterphobic action.** Distinct from courage. Subject pushes into the feared situation specifically because he is afraid of it, in order to prove the fear false. The Wrecking Crew fight that resolves the death-phobia arc is the prototype: he charges in not because he has worked through the fear but because charging in is the only way to outrun it. Same mechanism visible decades later in his pacifism-then-violence oscillations — the pacifist phase generates intolerable tension; the violent return is partly counterphobic restoration of the prior identity. The defense works in the short term and fails in the long term, because the fear is not metabolized, only outpaced.

**2.8 Idealization of the rescuer.** Operative toward Wanda chronically; operative toward the Avengers as institution intermittently; briefly operative toward Zemo at the original recruitment. The defense converts dependency into devotion: rather than experiencing the humiliation of needing rescue, the subject experiences the elevated emotion of loving the rescuer. The Wanda relationship is the lifetime expression. Surveillance note: idealization predicts subsequent devaluation when the idealized figure fails to deliver — the Revengers turn against the Avengers is the institutional devaluation phase of a prior institutional idealization.

**2.9 Theatricalization of affect.** Subject experiences emotions, then performs them, then experiences the performance. The doubling functions as containment — the performed version is bounded by the rules of performance (timing, audience, exit), where the raw version would not be. The one-liners in combat, the press-friendly grief statements, the on-camera tears at memorials are not insincere; they are sincere via a translation step that makes the affect tolerable. The Hollywood career institutionalizes this. The defense permits feeling at all; without it, subject would likely shutter affectively as he did in the post-resurrection catatonia.

---

## 3. MATURE LAYER (genuine, characterological, the moral floor)

The file should not understate this layer. It is small but real, and it is the substrate that makes the subject recuperable after each decompensation.

**3.1 Sublimation through performance.** The acting career is genuine, healthy sublimation — exhibitionism, grandiosity, the need to be seen, and the need to embody other selves all channeled into a socially sanctioned outlet that pays and rewards him. Distinct from 2.2 in that it is bounded (set hours, scripts, wrap parties) and produces work product. The stunt and action specialization additionally permits the safe expression of his counterphobic urges. When the career is going well, the subject's overall functioning improves measurably.

**3.2 Altruism toward the broken.** Subject's loyalty to Pym during the breakdown and court-martial is the cleanest exhibit — sustained, costly, public, and unrewarded. Recurs across the file: he stands by figures in disgrace (variously, Pym; the Vision during reconstruction periods; even, finally, Eric's body). The defense converts his own unmetabolized shame into useful labor on behalf of others who carry similar shame. He is most reliably himself when someone else is at their worst. Surveillance implication: subject is more predictable and more stable when assigned a charge in distress than when left unstructured.

**3.3 Humor as regulator.** The West Coast bravado is not only persona-borrowing; it is also a functional affect-regulation mechanism. Subject deploys quips and self-deprecation to discharge tension in survivable increments, to defuse interpersonal conflict before it escalates, and to communicate to himself that the situation is bearable. The humor is generally kind, occasionally self-lacerating, rarely cruel — a diagnostic indicator that the underlying personality organization remains neurotic rather than narcissistic-malignant.

**3.4 Anticipation, intermittent.** Subject occasionally — not characteristically — anticipates the consequences of his own destabilization and takes pre-emptive measures: removing himself from situations he predicts he cannot tolerate, asking teammates to monitor him during expected stress periods, agreeing in advance to constraints on his own ionic discharge during Wanda-adjacent crises. The capacity is real but unreliable; he uses it perhaps a third of the time it would be indicated.

**3.5 Reparative impulse.** After each significant decompensation, subject returns and attempts repair — apologies (sometimes overwrought but sincere), rejoining the team he attacked, accepting demotions or probationary status without protest. This is the single most important predictor of his long-term recuperability and the reason no Avengers roster has permanently severed him despite escalating provocations. The defense (it is partly a defense — reparation reduces the unbearable shame of having transgressed) operates in service of genuine moral aim.

---

## 4. COMPENSATORY SCAFFOLDING (not defenses proper)

These are behavioral and environmental structures the subject builds around himself to reduce the load on the defensive system. They are not psychic operations; they are infrastructure.

**4.1 The mirror network.** Subject maintains a deliberately wide network of regard-providers — teammates, Hollywood colleagues, fans, paparazzi, occasional therapists, and most centrally Wanda when accessible. The network is redundant by design: when any single mirror withdraws, others remain to confirm his existence. The discorporation periods demonstrate what happens when the network collapses to a single point (Wanda alone); the subject becomes ontologically contingent on her attention. Recommendation for any benevolent monitor: do not let the network collapse.

**4.2 The visual identity as anchor.** The persistence of the red-and-green costume long past any aesthetic justification functions as an external identity anchor. Removing the costume — and there are intervals where he tries — predictably correlates with periods of greater identity instability. The visual is, in effect, a worn self.

**4.3 Sobriety.** Subject is conspicuously sober across the file, including in environments (Hollywood, Avengers downtime, West Coast era) that would predict otherwise. Whether the sobriety is enforced by ionic metabolism or chosen does not matter functionally: it removes a destabilizer that his system could not absorb. The absence of substance use should be treated as a positive structural feature.

**4.4 Scheduled physicality.** Subject keeps a near-obsessive workout and stunt-rehearsal routine despite not needing it for physical conditioning. The function is regulatory: scheduled, exhausting, repetitive physical exertion provides predictable affect-discharge that the body would otherwise route through ionic flare. The gym is a pressure valve.

**4.5 The narrative habit.** Subject habitually constructs narratives about his life — to himself, to interviewers, to teammates over drinks he does not drink. The habit is a defense (intellectualization, theatricalization) but also a scaffolding: by maintaining a story of who he is, he generates continuity that his discontinuous existence does not otherwise provide. He is the protagonist of an ongoing autobiography that he narrates partly to keep being there.

---

## 5. WHAT EACH DEFENSE COSTS

A defense map is incomplete without the bill.

- *Identification with the aggressor* costs autonomy: he wears Zemo's design forever.
- *Persona-borrowing* costs self-knowledge: he does not reliably know which preferences are his.
- *Reaction formation* costs proportion: he overshoots ethically and morally, generating Revengers-class errors.
- *Intellectualization* costs honesty: he lies to himself in long sentences.
- *Splitting* costs relationships in the splitting interval, though most survive the re-integration.
- *Minimization of agency* costs growth: the lessons of past errors are not fully absorbed because the errors are not fully owned.
- *Counterphobic action* costs durable resolution: fears are outrun, not metabolized, and return.
- *Idealization* costs accurate perception of the idealized figure, and predicts subsequent devaluation.
- *Theatricalization* costs intimacy: the performed affect, however sincere, is a translation away from the raw, and intimates feel the translation.
- *Sublimation* costs little when working; costs much when the career falters, because the channel narrows.
- *Altruism* costs his own care: he tends others reliably and himself unreliably.
- *Humor* costs occasional gravitas when gravitas is required.
- *Anticipation* costs spontaneity in the periods he uses it — which may be why he uses it sparingly.
- *Reparation* costs nothing structural; it is the cleanest operation in the file.

---

## 6. DECOMPENSATION SEQUENCE (predictive)

For monitoring purposes, the defenses fail in a reliable order, and the order is itself diagnostic. A handler observing stages 1–2 has weeks; observing stages 3–4 has days; observing stage 5 has hours.

1. **Humor flattens.** The one-liners lose timing or stop entirely. This is the earliest indicator and the most overlooked.
2. **Persona-borrowing intensifies.** Subject begins mirroring whoever is nearest more obviously, with reduced calibration.
3. **Intellectualization metastasizes.** Long verbal rationales for moderate decisions; position papers where shrugs would do.
4. **Splitting appears.** Sudden re-categorization of a familiar figure as all-good or all-bad, often a figure who has done nothing to warrant the shift.
5. **Counterphobic action.** Subject seeks out the feared situation rather than process the fear.
6. **Ionic flare.** Somatic discharge. Feeling has become substrate. Intervention window narrowing.
7. **Discorporation or violent ideological turn.** Structure-failure. Either he goes diffuse or he goes rigid. Both are the same event in different directions.

---

## 7. CLOSING NOTE

The defensive architecture of Simon Williams is, on net, more functional than its components would predict. The mature layer is small but load-bearing; the scaffolding is well-built; the reparative impulse is reliable enough that even severe decompensations resolve toward return rather than rupture. The dossier should not pathologize the architecture so much as understand it as the cost of a man whose identity was rewritten by other hands and who, against the odds, keeps assembling himself back into something that wants to do good. The defenses are loud. The man underneath them is, by the evidence, decent. The file's organizing recommendation, for any benevolent observer, is the same as the structural diagnosis: keep the mirrors steady, keep the work meaningful, keep someone broken in his care, and he will, more often than not, keep his shape.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: SIMON WILLIAMS

*A decade-by-decade clinical mapping of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept across the subject's entire documented existence. Frameworks drawn from attachment theory (Bowlby/Ainsworth/Main), trauma psychology (van der Kolk, Herman), self psychology (Kohut), structural dissociation theory (van der Hart/Nijenhuis/Steele), and the shame literature (Lewis, Nathanson). Each phase is read forward from the prior — psychology is cumulative, and the subject's pathology is sedimentary, not episodic.*

---

## I. PRE-IONIC BASELINE (Paterson childhood through embezzlement conviction, circa age 0 to mid-20s)

### Affect Regulation

The pre-transformation Simon Williams the file can reconstruct from canon and inference is a man with **adequate but externally-scaffolded** affect regulation. He is not, in this period, dysregulated in the clinical sense — he holds down a corporate executive role, manages a public-facing company, sustains a fraternal relationship (however unequal) with Eric, and tolerates the chronic narcissistic injury of being a Williams son in a Stark world without breakdown, addiction, or overt depression. The regulation is **achievement-contingent**: as long as the company functioned, as long as the public role held, his affect held. When the scaffolding failed — competitive defeat by Stark Industries, the embezzlement discovery, the trial, the conviction, the prison interval — there is no internal regulatory floor underneath. He does not weather the failure; he is **annihilated** by it, which is exactly the precondition required for Zemo's recruitment to land. A man with intact internal regulation does not accept an offer from a costumed Nazi-adjacent baron in a federal penitentiary.

### Cognitive Style

**Romantic, narrative, and aspirational** even before transformation. The embezzlement is the diagnostic exhibit: a coldly analytic mind does not embezzle from its own publicly traded company to forestall an outcome (Stark dominance) it cannot reverse. Simon embezzled because he could not bear the *story* of being the Williams son who lost the company. He believed, against the numbers, in a turnaround that required only enough time and capital — the cognitive signature of a man who confuses narrative momentum with operational reality. This is the same cognitive style that will later let him be talked into a Trojan-horse mission by Zemo within a single conversation.

### Self-Concept

**Conditionally constructed, comparatively defined.** Simon's self-concept in this period is entirely referential — he is "Sanford's son" (insufficient), "Eric's brother" (insufficient), "Stark's competitor" (insufficient). There is no internal Simon, no privately held sense of who he is independent of how he ranks. The shame substrate is already laid: he has, by the time he enters prison, the deep conviction that he is fundamentally a fraud at the role he was handed. The *ionic transformation* will not create this. It will only give it a body.

---

## II. THE 1960s: TRANSFORMATION, BETRAYAL, DEATH (Avengers #9)

### Affect Regulation

Catastrophic and event-driven across the compressed arc. Simon enters Zemo's lab in a state of post-incarceration depressive collapse — passive, grateful, compliant. The transformation produces a manic-adjacent grandiosity (he is now powerful, important, costumed, chosen). The mission to infiltrate the Avengers produces a brief stabilization through being given a role with clear expectations. The turn against Zemo is **acute moral panic** — a flood of conscience that the file would record as a sudden, total reversal of allegiance under affective load, not a deliberated decision. He dies in the same arc. There has been no time to develop any sustained regulation pattern; the affect simply moves through him at whatever amplitude the event imposes.

### Cognitive Style

Reactive, suggestible, **fused to whichever frame is being offered**. Within the span of a single mission Simon adopts Zemo's "the Avengers are your enemies" frame, then the Avengers' "you are one of us" frame, then his own "I cannot do this" frame, each completely and without residue of the prior. This is the cognitive correlate of the absent internal self: there is no Simon to weigh the offers against. He becomes whichever frame is loudest in the room.

### Self-Concept

For the first time, **provisionally positive** — he is Wonder Man, he matters, he has a costume and a code-name and a team — and then, in the act of dying, **redemptively positive**: he is the man who turned on the villain to save the heroes. He dies, crucially, at the only moment in his life so far where his self-concept has been stable and good. The decade-plus dormancy that follows freezes this self-concept in amber. When he returns, the comparison to who he was at the moment of death will be merciless.

---

## III. THE MID-1970s: RESURRECTION AND THE DEATH-TERROR YEARS (Avengers #151–#194 era)

### Affect Regulation

This is the cleanest **PTSD presentation** in the canon. Affect regulation collapses to the autonomic level — Simon presents with the full triad: hyperarousal (startle, panic onset under combat cues), re-experiencing (intrusive imagery of his own death-interval, which he describes in fragments he cannot integrate), and avoidance (freezing in combat, fleeing engagements, refusing to deploy his powers). The dissociative interval — years of nonexistence or near-nonexistence — functions as the **unmetabolized trauma**, with the additional horror that the trauma is *of his own absence*, a thing no normal trauma framework was built to process. He has no narrative for what happened to him because nothing happened to him; he was simply not there.

Regulation across this period is achieved only through **interpersonal co-regulation** with the Avengers, particularly Vision and the Beast, who serve as auxiliary nervous systems. Left alone, he decompensates. The Wrecking Crew engagement (~Avengers #194) is the documented moment of **exposure-therapy breakthrough** — forced confrontation with the feared stimulus (lethal combat) under conditions where flight is foreclosed, producing the corrective experience that *survival is possible*. The breakthrough is real but the autonomic sensitization is permanent. Every subsequent death will reactivate this substrate immediately.

### Cognitive Style

**Catastrophic, future-foreshortened, hypervigilant for threat.** Simon in this period cannot think more than one move ahead because every threat-cue captures his processing entirely. The romantic narrative cognition of the pre-ionic period is intact but inverted — he now narrates his own destruction rather than his redemption. This is also when the **ontological question** first becomes cognitively chronic: *am I really me? was the dead man me? if I am me, why do I feel like a copy?* He has no framework to answer this and the lack of an answer becomes a permanent open file in his cognition.

### Self-Concept

**Catastrophically destabilized and unable to reconsolidate.** The self that died was the redemption-self; the self that returned is something he does not recognize and cannot endorse. He spends this period unable to feel that he is Simon Williams — he is, at best, *the thing that came back*. The Vision-engram revelation, when it arrives in this same window, is psychologically devastating in a way the publication history tends to underweight: he learns that the most stable, coherent version of his mind is now walking around in someone else's body, married to the woman he will come to love. The implication that the Vision is in some sense more *him* than he is lands on an already-shattered self-structure and produces the depersonalization that becomes lifelong.

---

## IV. THE LATE 1970s / EARLY 1980s: STABILIZATION AND THE HOLLYWOOD PERSONA (West Coast Avengers founding era)

### Affect Regulation

Marked improvement, achieved through the **invention of a public persona** that can absorb affect that the underlying self cannot. The Hollywood stuntman/actor career is, clinically, **adaptive sublimation of the first order** — he channels exhibitionism, residual grandiosity, the need to be seen, and the somatic-invulnerability gift into a socially sanctioned outlet that pays him to perform the very thing he is most anxious about (his own indestructibility). When he is on a set or in a publicity context, his regulation is excellent because the role provides the regulatory structure. Off-set, in private, the underlying anxiety is intact but masked. Humor — quips, one-liners, self-deprecating asides — emerges in this period as a **chronic regulatory device**, the verbal equivalent of pacing. The bravado is real and the bravado is defensive; both are true.

### Cognitive Style

Begins to develop **narrative compartmentalization**. He maintains separate operating cognitions for separate domains: the actor-Simon (image-managing, agent-oriented, opening-weekend-aware), the Avenger-Simon (team-positional, tactically cooperative, deferential to Cap or Hawkeye), the private-Simon (still asking the ontological question). The compartments are leaky but functional. Cognitive style becomes more **outward-facing and image-oriented**, less inwardly recursive, which is a net regulatory gain even as it postpones the unresolved material.

### Self-Concept

**Performed-and-believed.** This is the period of the safety-pin red jacket, the sunglasses, the publicity-still poses — the deliberate construction of a self that is, for the first time since pre-ionic days, *legible from the outside*. The legibility helps him believe in it. The brittleness is that the self is now sustained primarily by external mirroring (audiences, press, the team's tolerant amusement) and will not survive prolonged mirror-failure. The Pym loyalty arc (~Avengers #213, West Coast Avengers #1) is the period's diagnostic positive: it demonstrates that beneath the persona there remains a **moral floor that operates without audience** — he stands by Hank when standing by Hank is socially costly, and he does it quietly. The man underneath the jacket is still the man who turned on Zemo.

---

## V. THE LATE 1980s: WANDA, THE VISION REFUSAL, MORAL INJURY (VisionQuest and aftermath)

### Affect Regulation

The Wanda romance, in its early phase, produces the **best affective period of his adult life** — co-regulation with a partner he experiences as choosing him, channeling the dependency-attachment into a sustaining relationship rather than a corroding longing. Then VisionQuest arrives and the regulation breaks along an entirely new axis: not anxiety, not terror, but **acute moral conflict** he cannot tolerate. Asked to donate the engrams, he is asked to choose between (a) restoring the rival who is also his template who is also his friend's husband, at the cost of his own romantic possibility with Wanda, and (b) refusing, on rationalized grounds, and keeping her. He chooses (b). The affect this produces is the period's signature: a **chronic, low-grade, never-discharged guilt** that he manages by not looking at it directly. Where the earlier decade's affective signature was *terror*, this decade's is *suppressed shame with intermittent leakage*.

### Cognitive Style

The romantic-narrative cognition reasserts and is, for the first time, **deployed in a self-serving direction**. He constructs the rationale ("the Vision who would come back wouldn't really be the Vision," "Wanda deserves to choose for herself," "I am not obligated to be a battery for someone else's marriage") in language that is not technically wrong but is selected entirely by the wish underneath. This is the cognitive signature of **motivated reasoning under moral load** and it is the prototype for what will, two decades later, become the Revengers manifesto. The intellectual structure is now in place: when I want something badly enough, I can build a rationale that licenses taking it. The shadow precedent is set.

### Self-Concept

**Fractured along a new fault line.** Where prior fault lines were trauma-based (the dead-and-returned split, the original-vs-copy question), the new fault is **morally agentic** — Simon now knows, privately, that he is capable of a chosen wrong, not just a coerced one. The Zemo-era turn could be excused as duress; the engram refusal cannot. He absorbs this into self-concept as a quiet, persistent self-suspicion that will color every subsequent moral position he takes. Even his good acts now have, for him, a private asterisk: *is this another rationalization?*

---

## VI. THE EARLY-TO-MID 1990s: FORCE WORKS, SECOND DEATH, DISCORPORATION (through late-90s Busiek/Perez return)

### Affect Regulation

Nominal team-leadership in Force Works represents a **late attempt to consolidate** through the assumption of formal responsibility — a developmental move that, in a healthier subject, would mark progression into generative adulthood. In Simon it is unstable because the leadership role demands the very thing he most lacks: a settled internal authority that does not require external mirroring. He performs the role; he does not inhabit it. His second death, sacrificing against Kree forces, is **psychologically continuous with the first turn against Zemo** — at the moment of crisis the moral floor holds and he gives himself up for the team. Affectively this is a clean act, perhaps the cleanest of his life: the suppressed shame of the Vision refusal is partially discharged through self-sacrifice.

The discorporation period in the late-90s Busiek run is **the most clinically extraordinary affective state in the file**. He exists only when Wanda summons him; in the gaps between summonings he is, by his own report, *not in a state at all*. Affect is not regulated because there is no continuous subject to regulate it; affect *occurs* during episodes of manifestation and then ceases. The ontological condition of being-only-when-needed-by-Wanda is the literal somatic realization of the dependency that has organized him since the late '70s. The psychological cost, when he is manifested, is **enormous longing and enormous gratitude in unstable mixture**, with no autonomy underneath either.

### Cognitive Style

Increasingly **dissociative-fragmentary**. He thinks in spurts, in scenes, in attempts to assemble continuity from manifestations that may be hours or weeks apart from his subjective standpoint. The romantic narrative cognition continues to function but it now has gaps it cannot bridge. Memory becomes selective and emotionally weighted — he remembers what summoned him (her need, her grief, her thought of him) with hallucinatory vividness and remembers operational details poorly.

### Self-Concept

Reduced, by the end of this phase, to **near-pure relationality**. He is, ontologically, the man Wanda is thinking about. Everything that was true psychologically since the Vision-engram revelation is now true literally. When he is eventually re-corporealized in stable form, he carries forward the conviction — never quite articulated, but operationally present — that his existence is on loan from her regard. This will be load-bearing for the next decade's collapse.

---

## VII. THE 2000s: DISASSEMBLED, HOUSE OF M, AND THE WANDA-LOSS DECADE

### Affect Regulation

Catastrophic and prolonged. The Disassembled / House of M arc removes the single regulatory object that has organized his existence since the late 1970s. He does not present, in this period, with the acute panic of the post-resurrection years; he presents instead with a **slower, more corrosive dysregulation** — irritability, social withdrawal punctuated by performative re-engagement, intermittent ionic flares that his teammates increasingly read as warning signs rather than incidents. The flares are, clinically, **somatized affect**: feelings he cannot contain emerging through the body that cannot contain them, in a subject whose body and feelings are the same energetic substrate. The pattern is unmistakably a **prolonged complicated grief** with secondary identity-collapse features.

### Cognitive Style

The motivated-reasoning capacity developed during the VisionQuest period **metastasizes into ideology**. He begins to construct, across the decade, a sustained intellectual position about the Avengers as a destabilizing force on reality — a position that is not delusional (reality testing intact, the position has some evidentiary basis in the Disassembled events themselves) but is **affect-selected**: he believes it because believing it routes his unbearable grief and self-suspicion into an external target. Cognition becomes more rigid in this period, less playful, less willing to entertain counter-evidence. The compartmentalization that protected him through the actor years breaks down; the private self and the public position begin to converge on grievance.

### Self-Concept

**Reorganizes around grievance as substitute for the lost mirror.** With Wanda gone — broken, exiled, reality-rewritten — Simon has no stable regard against which to know himself. The Revengers ideology, which crystallizes by 2011, provides a substitute: he knows who he is because he knows who he is *against*. This is the **negative-identity formation** classical to subjects who have lost a primary attachment object and cannot tolerate the resulting void. The self that emerges is harsher, more righteous, more brittle, and — most diagnostically — *louder* than any prior version. The volume is the tell. He is shouting the position because he does not, underneath, believe in it.

---

## VIII. THE EARLY 2010s: REVENGERS AND THE PEAK OF NEGATIVE-IDENTITY ORGANIZATION

### Affect Regulation

In the Revengers phase Simon achieves a paradoxical **temporary stabilization through ideologized rage**. The diffuse grief and self-suspicion of the prior decade are now organized into a sustained project with a target, allies, and a script. Affect is regulated by being *channeled* — every flare of grief or shame is routed into anti-Avenger action and discharged. This is functionally similar to how some chronic-trauma subjects stabilize within high-conflict political or religious movements: the movement provides the regulatory structure the self cannot. The cost is that the stabilization requires sustained moral wrongness — he must keep the grievance alive to keep the regulation working. When the Revengers project fails and the grievance collapses, the underlying dysregulation returns with all its accumulated interest.

### Cognitive Style

**Rigid, declarative, manifesto-shaped.** He speaks in this period in *positions* rather than observations — every utterance is a stake-in-the-ground. This is the cognitive signature of a subject for whom flexibility has become intolerable because flexibility would readmit the grief and the self-suspicion that the rigidity is keeping at bay. The romantic-narrative cognition is fully captured by a single narrative (the Avengers as destabilizing villains, himself as the necessary corrective) which he defends against all incoming counter-evidence not by argument but by **affective insistence**.

### Self-Concept

**The most coherent self-concept of his adult life, achieved through the worst means.** He knows, in the Revengers period, exactly who he is — and what he is is wrong. The collapse, when it comes, returns him to the chronic identity-coherence deficit but now compounded by the shame of having organized himself around an indefensible position. The shame substrate, already deep, is reactivated and deepened.

---

## IX. THE MID-TO-LATE 2010s AND 2020s: OSCILLATION, SELF-AWARENESS, BRITTLE INTEGRATION

### Affect Regulation

Improved relative to the Revengers peak, **never restored to the West Coast plateau**. He learns, in this final documented period, to recognize his own dysregulation as it arises — the ionic flares, the rationalized turns, the grievance-cognition — and to interrupt it. This is real progress and the file should record it as such. But the interruption is conscious rather than automatic; he is metabolizing his pathology by effort rather than by structural reorganization. Energy spent on self-management is energy not available for ordinary functioning, and the period shows the cost: he is more tired, more withdrawn, more elegiac in his self-presentation than at any prior point. The humor remains, now with a slower delivery and a darker register.

### Cognitive Style

**Reflective, increasingly autobiographical, self-narrating in a way that suggests integration without achieving it.** He has begun, in this period, to talk about his own history with a coherent voice — to recount the Zemo turn, the death, the Wanda years, the Revengers as a *story* with a protagonist who is recognizably himself. This is enormous developmentally — a subject who can narrate his own life coherently has assembled at least a working autobiographical self, which Simon lacked for most of his existence. The brittleness is that the narration is still **performance-adjacent**, still pitched to an imagined audience (interviews, conversations, the camera he can always feel), and so the integration achieved is at the level of the public persona rather than the private substrate. The actor and the man are closer together than they have ever been; they are not the same.

### Self-Concept

**Provisionally integrated, externally referenced, aware of its own provisionality.** This is the most diagnostically interesting state Simon has occupied. He knows, now, that his self is a construction sustained by mirrors; he knows the mirrors he most depends on (Wanda, audience, team); he knows the failure modes (rationalization, grievance, performance for its own sake). He knows all of this and he is still, structurally, the same dependency-organized, externally-mirrored, narratively-cognizing romantic he has always been. The knowing does not change the structure. What it changes is the speed at which he can recognize and correct excursions from it. He is, in this period, a man who has learned to **manage** himself rather than to **be** himself, and he carries that condition with the weary grace of someone who understands it will not improve.

---

## ACROSS-DECADE SYNTHESIS

The longitudinal arc, read clinically, is **not a recovery curve and not a deterioration curve** — it is the slow stabilization of a chronically unstable system through the accretion of compensatory structures. The trauma substrate (PTSD from death, depersonalization from engram-copying, complicated grief from Wanda) is **never resolved**; it is bypassed, rerouted, and managed. The identity deficit is **never filled**; it is masked, performed, and intermittently re-acknowledged. The dependency-attachment is **never outgrown**; it is named, channeled, and worked around.

What changes across the decades is **awareness without restructuring** — Simon Williams progresses from a man who was a fraud and did not know it (pre-ionic), to a man who was traumatized and could not say so (post-resurrection), to a man who was rationalizing and would not see it (VisionQuest, Revengers), to a man who is all of those things and can finally name them (present). The naming is the only victory he has been granted, and in a subject whose original wound was the inability to be *seen* — by his father, his brother, his peer — the capacity to finally see himself, accurately and without flinching, is not a small one. It is, possibly, the only thing he was ever actually trying to do.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: Williams, Simon — "Wonder Man"
### File Section 4 of 12 — Clinical Synthesis, Longitudinal

---

## 4.1 Framing the Assessment

This section assembles a working psychiatric formulation across roughly six decades of observable conduct, intermittent on-record self-report (interviews to entertainment press, deposition transcripts from the Pym court-martial proceedings, court statements at his original embezzlement trial, and Avengers internal debriefs archived per S.H.I.E.L.D. liaison protocols), and direct behavioral telemetry from team operations. The subject has never, to this file's knowledge, completed a structured diagnostic interview — every documented contact with a mental-health clinician has been short, situational, and either court-ordered (post-embezzlement intake at the New Jersey state correctional facility, 1964) or team-mandated (Avengers Mansion post-resurrection workup, mid-1970s; West Coast compound stress-debrief intake forms, late 1980s; Avengers Tower reintegration interviews following the Revengers incident, 2011). All standardized instruments noted below are reconstructed from collateral, not from a sit-down administration.

Diagnostic nomenclature is given in DSM-5-TR / ICD-11 analog terms, with the caveat that this subject's case is precisely the kind that strains nosology: his pathology is iatrogenic, somatically embodied, and existentially structured in ways the ordinary categories were not built for. Where a label fits, it is named; where it almost fits and does not, the discrepancy is preserved rather than smoothed.

---

## 4.2 Principal Diagnoses

### 4.2.1 Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, With Delayed and Recurrent Exacerbations (DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40)

The cleanest, best-substantiated diagnosis in the chart. The index trauma is the subject's first death and the dissociative interval of inert preservation that followed — Criterion A is satisfied by an event no human prior to him had survived in a form articulate enough to report on.

**Re-experiencing (Criterion B):** Across the Englehart/Shooter/Michelinie observation window (publication 1976–1980; in-narrative approximately 14–22 months post-revival) the subject demonstrates intrusive recollection in textbook form. Combat triggers — particularly any energy attack reminiscent of Zemo's original ionic apparatus, and notably any threat involving immobilization — produce momentary freeze states followed by fragmentary verbalizations referring to "the dark" and "feeling myself go out." Sleep is not required ionically but he reports lying down anyway and experiencing "something like a dream where I'm being switched off." This is hypnagogic-pattern re-experiencing. Documented in at least three Mansion debriefs of the period.

**Avoidance (Criterion C):** Multi-week combat refusal during the mid-1970s arc, rationalized as "I'm just not ready yet." More subtly, lifelong avoidance of solitude — he books himself into ensemble situations (teams, film sets, public appearances) with a density that exceeds the requirements of his work and which collateral interviews with West Coast teammates (notably Rambeau, Pym) flag as conspicuous.

**Negative alterations in cognition and mood (Criterion D):** Persistent "I shouldn't be here" ideation, recurring across decades. Survivor's anomaly rather than survivor's guilt strictly — he is not guilty that others died, he is guilty that he did not stay dead. Foreshortened-future ideation is paradoxically *present* in a functionally immortal subject: he reports anticipating each next death.

**Hyperarousal (Criterion E):** Baseline startle is elevated; ionic discharge under startle has been measured at the West Coast compound (small, involuntary aura-flares on door slams, on Pym's coffee grinder, on Hawkeye's bow draw). Sleep disturbance is moot. Irritability is poorly modulated under fatigue-equivalent stress and presents as quip-density escalation — the wisecracking rate rises measurably under acute threat.

**Course:** partial remission following the Wrecking Crew confrontation (canonically the symbolic exposure-and-mastery event), with full-symptom relapse following each subsequent death (Force Works/Kree; the discorporation arc; later ionic dissolution episodes). The pattern is **sensitization**, not extinction — each trauma cycle lowers the threshold for the next exacerbation, which is the modal course for chronic PTSD with repeated re-exposure to the index stressor type. By the Bendis-era observation window the subject is functionally in a permanent low-grade hyperaroused state masked by professional charm.

**Specifier:** With dissociative symptoms (depersonalization/derealization). See §4.2.2 for the dissociative material proper.

### 4.2.2 Other Specified Dissociative Disorder, with chronic identity-coherence deficit and somatic expression (DSM-5-TR 300.15 / ICD-11 6B66)

The diagnosis that, if forced to choose one, this file would code as primary. The subject does not present with classical Dissociative Identity Disorder — there are no discrete, named, amnestically partitioned alters; there is no switching with the conventional markers; there are no fugue episodes in the legal-history sense. What is present, and what is unusually well-documented because of the subject's powers, is a **chronic deficit in the integrative function that ordinarily produces a continuous, owned sense of self**.

Symptoms:

- **Depersonalization, severe and recurrent.** Multiple recorded statements across decades on the order of "I'm not sure I'm still the man who went into prison" / "the Vision had my mind — am I the copy?" / "when I came back, did *I* come back?" This is not philosophical posturing; the affect on these statements (Mansion debrief tapes; Englehart-era observation) is flattened and anxious in the manner characteristic of true depersonalization, not the intellectualized rumination of a curious person asking an interesting question.

- **Identity confusion and identity alteration without classical alters.** The subject's self-presentation reorganizes around whoever is currently the dominant relational or vocational mirror — the Avengers, then Hollywood, then Wanda, then the Revengers' grievance-frame, then the Avengers again. Each reorganization is more total than ordinary code-switching would explain. Friends report that "Simon at the studio" and "Simon on the team" speak differently, dress differently, hold their face differently. The reorganizations are not amnestic but they are not fully integrated, either.

- **Somatic expression.** This is the unusual and diagnostically load-bearing feature. The subject's physical form *literally* destabilizes under identity stress — ionic flares, dispersion, reconstitution. The discorporation arc following the Force Works/Kree death is the most extreme expression: he existed only as a field maintained by another person's longing. No conventional patient produces somatic evidence of dissociation this direct; the subject does, and it should be weighted accordingly in formulation.

**Etiology:** the original ionic transformation already disrupted somatic-self continuity; the death and revival ruptured temporal-self continuity; the engram-copying for the Vision ruptured ownership-of-mind; each subsequent death and reconstitution has compounded the rupture. The disorder is iatrogenic in the literal sense — caused by what was done to him. There is no plausible developmental dissociative history pre-Zemo (the pre-transformation Williams was a coherent if inadequate person, not a fragmented one).

**Course:** progressive. The 1970s presentation was florid-anxious; the 1980s presentation was masked by the Hollywood role-vehicle which functioned as a stabilizing exoskeleton; the 1990s discorporation episode was a frank decompensation; the 2010s presentations show a chronic, lower-grade, well-defended baseline with periodic acute breakthroughs.

### 4.2.3 Other Specified Trauma- and Stressor-Related Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89) — Persistent Complex Bereavement features

Coded secondarily because of the unresolved grief for his brother Eric. The subject has buried his brother — and lost his brother to a death-equivalent transformation — multiple times across the canon. He has never completed the mourning. Behavioral signature: he raises Eric in conversation unprompted; he keeps a small set of family photographs (per Pym's recollection in a 1989 interview, "Simon has a picture of him and Eric as kids in his wallet, and I have seen him take it out exactly when nobody is supposed to be watching"); he experiences anniversary-pattern dysphoria correlated to the Reaper's documented death dates.

---

## 4.3 Personality-Level Findings

### 4.3.1 Narcissistic features, vulnerable subtype — *features, not disorder*

The grandiose surface is genuine and consistent: costume aesthetics across eras (the original red-and-green safari jacket, the later Hollywood-styled bodysuits, the deliberate visual branding), the screen career, the certainty during the Revengers period. But every grandiose presentation is shadowed by a brittle and shame-organized substrate, and that is the diagnostic signature of the **vulnerable** rather than **grandiose** subtype.

Against full NPD:

- He demonstrates **sustained empathy** with broken figures — the years of standing beside Pym through the court-martial and the post-Yellowjacket collapse, the inability to write off the Reaper, the persistent gentleness with Wanda even in her most disorganized phases. True NPD-grandiose does not produce this pattern.
- He demonstrates **genuine guilt** (Vision refusal, the Revengers episode in retrospect), not the mimicry of guilt that NPD produces under social pressure.
- He demonstrates **self-correction** — repeated voluntary returns from positions he has staked publicly. NPD-grandiose protects the stake at any cost; vulnerable narcissism collapses the stake and rebuilds elsewhere, which is the subject's pattern.

So: vulnerable narcissistic *features* embedded in a fragmented identity, not a personality disorder proper.

### 4.3.2 Dependent features in pair-bond functioning, partial presentation

In the singular Wanda-relational context the subject meets several Dependent Personality criteria (difficulty making major decisions without her input during the late-WCA period; preoccupation with abandonment fears; urgent re-pair-bonding pressure across multiple eras). He does not meet the criteria in other domains — he functions independently in work, friendship, and team leadership. This is therefore not a personality disorder; it is a domain-specific dependent pattern, almost certainly secondary to the identity-coherence deficit (he depends on her because she is the most stable mirror he has).

### 4.3.3 Anxious-preoccupied attachment, persistent across the lifespan

Pre-transformation history consistent with conditional regard from Sanford Williams and a chronically unfavorable comparison to Eric. Adult pattern in every documented attachment thereafter — including the Avengers as an attachment-object, not only individual relationships — confirms an anxious-preoccupied model. Hyperactivating strategy under threat (increased proximity-seeking, increased self-disclosure of distress, performative reassurance-eliciting behavior). Rarely deactivates; almost never dismissive.

---

## 4.4 Comorbidity and Cross-Loading

The PTSD and the dissociative disorder are best understood as the same pathophysiology viewed from two angles: a chronically destabilized self-system reacts to repeated traumatic re-exposures by further fragmenting, and the fragmentation in turn lowers the threshold for the next traumatic reaction. The narcissistic and dependent features are *defensive architectures* built on top of the fragmentation — the grandiosity stabilizes the brittle self in the public-facing register; the dependency stabilizes it in the intimate register. Remove the fragmentation hypothetically and both defensive structures would deflate. This is why the subject's strongest periods of functioning correlate with stable mirroring (the early-WCA team cohesion; the stable Wanda pair-bond at its apex; the reintegrated post-Revengers Avengers tenure) and his decompensations correlate with mirror-loss.

A note on sub-syndromal depression: the subject demonstrates dysthymic-spectrum coloring during low periods (post-Wanda separations, post-Revengers shame phase, the discorporation arc's lead-in) but does not meet criteria for Major Depressive Disorder at any clearly bounded interval. The dysphoria is reactive, not endogenous, and remits with restoration of relational footing.

---

## 4.5 What He Is Not — Rigorous Differential

### 4.5.1 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

The original embezzlement, which superficially resembles antisocial conduct, was situationally driven (collapsing family business, panic decision), produced acute guilt rather than gratification, and was followed by a documented confession and acceptance of sentence rather than evasion. There is no childhood conduct-disorder history. He has across six decades never demonstrated the parasitic exploitation, the cruelty-as-pleasure, the chronic deceit-for-sport, or the absent remorse that the diagnosis requires. The Revengers episode — superficially the most antisocial-coded act of his career — is on examination the opposite: a moralistic crusade conducted publicly under his own name, rationalized in ethical language, and ultimately recanted with shame.

### 4.5.2 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

The identity instability is the only borderline-resembling feature, and it is etiologically wrong for BPD — it is traumatic-dissociative and iatrogenic, not developmental in the early-attachment-disruption sense BPD requires. The hallmarks BPD demands are absent: no chronic abandonment-rage (he grieves and decompensates, he does not rage), no recurrent self-harm or parasuicidal pattern (his self-sacrifices are heroic-pattern, undertaken with apparent meaning rather than as relief-of-affect), no chronic emptiness in the BPD-specific sense (his emptiness is depersonalized, not affectively void), no stormy unstable interpersonal pattern characterized by idealization/devaluation cycles (his loyalties are *too stable*, to the point of clinging to the Reaper).

### 4.5.3 Not Bipolar Disorder

Mood oscillations are entirely reactive to identifiable events and remit with event resolution. No documented endogenous cycling; no hypomanic episode meeting duration criteria absent triggering circumstance; no depressive episode meeting MDD criteria for two consecutive weeks absent identifiable loss. The high-energy periods during film-career peaks are personality-congruent activation, not hypomania — sleep need is non-applicable, judgment is broadly intact, and the activation is sustainable for months without a crash phase of opposite polarity.

### 4.5.4 Not Schizophrenia-Spectrum or Other Primary Psychotic Disorder

Reality testing is intact across all observation windows including the Revengers period. The Revengers worldview was wrong on facts but was a coherently argued and shared (with co-belligerents) interpretation of available evidence, not a delusion in the technical sense. No hallucinations on record (the depersonalization phenomena are interoceptive and self-referential, not perceptual). No formal thought disorder; speech is organized, often deliberately stylized for effect but never derailed. No negative symptoms.

### 4.5.5 Not Substance Use Disorder

Conspicuous lifelong sobriety despite decades in industries (film, prison subculture, mid-century super-heroics) with high exposure. Ionic metabolism does not process most psychoactives meaningfully, which provides a biological floor — but the subject's behavior also shows no behavioral-addiction pattern that would substitute (no gambling, no compulsive sexuality on record, no compulsive consumption). The relevant compulsive-pattern in the personality is **performance-seeking**, which is not coded as a disorder but is worth flagging behaviorally.

### 4.5.6 Not Factitious Disorder, Not Malingering

The death-phobia of the 1970s arc was at points read by skeptical teammates as performance. The collateral evidence — involuntary somatic correlates, prolonged duration, costs to social standing the subject would not have chosen — rules this out. He was genuinely afraid; he was genuinely impaired.

### 4.5.7 Not Adjustment Disorder

The presentations exceed adjustment criteria by duration and severity at every clinically significant interval. The framework is wrong by scale.

### 4.5.8 Not Autism-Spectrum

Social reciprocity is intact and unusually fluent in performance contexts. Theory-of-mind is functional. Restricted-repetitive patterns are absent except where they reflect anxious-attachment rituals (proximity-seeking with Wanda; rehearsal-of-lines behavior off-set, which is occupational).

### 4.5.9 Not Organic / Neurocognitive

Despite the radical alteration of substrate, no cognitive-screening proxies (memory, attention, executive function as inferred from operational performance) show focal or global deficit. The "brain" is held in ionic energy patterns but the cognitive functions those patterns produce are normal-to-superior. The depersonalization is psychological, not neurological.

---

## 4.6 Etiology, Synthesized

The developmental priming was a childhood and young-adulthood of conditional regard from a demanding industrialist father, a dominating older brother whose temperament was rewarded where the subject's was not, and an emerging adult comparator (Stark) against whom no realistic competition was possible. This produced a personality already organized around shame, performance, and external referencing of worth, but functional and non-clinical.

The first ionic transformation imposed a non-consensual rewriting of the subject's somatic substrate. The coerced villain role imposed a non-consensual rewriting of his moral identity. The first death and dissociative inert interval produced the index trauma. The engram-copying for the Vision constructed, without the subject's contemporaneous knowledge, a second person carrying his interior — a derealization wound it is difficult to find a conventional analog for. Each subsequent death and resurrection deepened the somatic-self destabilization, until by the late-period observation windows the body itself had become unable to reliably hold its shape under affective load.

The condition is therefore the natural history of a non-clinically-vulnerable personality subjected to a series of identity-rupturing events no human had previously sustained, with no available specialist care for any of them. He is, in the most precise sense, a man whose disorder was *done to him*.

---

## 4.7 Course and Prognosis

Course is **chronic, fluctuating, slowly progressive in identity-destabilization, with preserved moral functioning**. The most prognostically favorable features are unusual and should be weighted:

- A genuine and stable moral floor that has not eroded across decades or under repeated re-traumatization.
- Capacity for sustained guilt, which is the precondition for any therapeutic work on shame.
- Repeated demonstrated capacity for return, apology, and reintegration after maximal public failure.
- A pre-existing sublimatory channel (the performance career) that genuinely metabolizes some of the load.

The least favorable features are:

- The somatic embodiment of the dissociation, which means therapeutic destabilization is physically dangerous (he can literally come apart).
- The dependence on a single relational mirror (Wanda) whose own clinical course is volatile and whose availability cannot be assumed.
- The sensitization pattern of the PTSD, which predicts that each next death — and he is likely to die again — will produce a worse and slower recovery.
- The absence of any continuous therapeutic relationship across the record.

Prognosis with appropriate longitudinal specialist care (which has never been provided): guarded but meaningful improvement plausible. Prognosis without it, which is the actual condition: continued chronic course with periodic decompensations of increasing severity, against a baseline of professional and interpersonal functioning that masks the underlying disorder competently enough that the disorder will continue to go untreated.

---

## 4.8 Single-Sentence Clinical Summary for the File Header

> A chronic, iatrogenically-induced dissociative-spectrum identity-coherence deficit with somatic expression, comorbid with chronic recurrent PTSD and unresolved complicated bereavement, defended by vulnerable-narcissistic and partial-dependent personality structures, in a subject whose preserved moral and empathic capacities exceed what the underlying pathology would ordinarily permit and constitute the most clinically and ethically important fact in the chart.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: SIMON WILLIAMS

*A longitudinal catalog of observable behaviors, micro-tells, decision habits, and somatic patterns across all documented states. Compiled from canon and inferred at the granularity a continuous-observation file would contain.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

When unobserved and unstressed — a vanishingly rare condition for the subject — Simon's body settles into a posture that betrays his Hollywood years: shoulders deliberately squared rather than naturally relaxed, sternum lifted as if cued by an off-screen director. He does not actually relax; he assumes the *appearance* of relaxation. The lean is the giveaway: when seated, he drapes one arm along the back of whatever furniture is available, ankle crossed on knee, in a pose that photographs well from a three-quarter angle. He has been observed sitting like this alone in his own kitchen.

**Hands.** At rest, the left hand will find a surface — countertop, knee, the rim of a glass — and tap a slow four-count, then stop, then resume. The tempo corresponds roughly to a relaxed combat-breathing exercise; he is unaware he is doing it. The right hand, the dominant striking hand, more often hovers near his own jaw or temple — fingers brushing the hairline, thumb tracing the mandible. He grooms in mirrors he does not need.

**Eyes.** In private, the ionic luminescence dims to a low ember; in public, he keeps them brighter, almost performatively. He has trained himself to make eye contact in long sustained beats — a stage habit — but in genuinely safe company (Pym, occasionally Hawkeye, almost no one else) the gaze unfocuses and drifts upward and to the left in the recall direction, frequently. He is, baseline, a man rehearsing memory.

**Voice.** Calm-state voice is a half-register lower than his actual natural pitch. The lowered register is a deliberate choice he made sometime in the late 1970s, around the period he began booking on-camera work; under sufficient surprise or genuine laughter it slips upward to a slightly nasal, slightly New Jersey-inflected baseline he does not love hearing recorded.

**Eating, drinking, sleeping.** He doesn't need to. He does anyway. He cooks elaborately — Italian, mostly, the cuisine of his Paterson childhood — for guests he has invited specifically so he will have a reason to cook. He pours wine he does not drink. He goes to bed at conventional hours, lies down, reads scripts and trade press, sometimes simulates sleep for the benefit of a partner. The ritual of normal embodiment is load-bearing; stripping it away triggers depersonalization within forty-eight hours.

**Reading.** Trades, screenplays, his own clippings (yes, all of them, in a binder he claims is for his agent and is not), and — a private habit — nineteenth-century novels. He prefers third-person omniscient narration. He is comfortable being narrated.

---

## II. STRESS — MODERATE / SOCIAL

Triggered by criticism, by a teammate's faint praise, by being introduced second, by a journalist mispronouncing his name, by a callsheet listing him below the title, by anyone speaking of Stark in his hearing.

**The smile.** It widens by a measurable amount and stops reaching the eyes. The teeth show more. The head tilts five to ten degrees. This is the cardinal social-stress tell and it has been visible in photographs for forty years.

**Verbal pattern.** Quip frequency increases sharply — one to three per minute in heightened social pressure, versus one every several minutes at baseline. The quips skew self-deprecating with a recovery beat ("Oh, what do I know, I just play the hero"). The self-deprecation is bait; he is waiting for someone to contradict it. If no one does, the next quip will be louder.

**Spatial.** He angles toward the highest-status person in the room and finds reasons — a refill, a question, a shared joke — to close distance with them. Concurrently, he angles *away* from whoever just dispensed the criticism, presenting his shoulder rather than his chest. He is unaware of doing either.

**The phone check.** Under social pressure he will pull out his phone and consult it for approximately four seconds, then pocket it. There is rarely anything on it. The gesture creates a one-beat exit from the conversational thread and resets his composure. He has used some version of this maneuver since pagers.

**Costume / appearance fidgets.** He will adjust a cuff. He will smooth a lapel. If in uniform, he will check the seam of his jacket at the shoulder — the spot where the original red-and-green Zemo costume had a tailoring flaw that scratched his neck. The hand goes there decades after the garment is gone.

---

## III. STRESS — PROFESSIONAL / COMBAT-ADJACENT

In briefing rooms, on tactical approaches, in any setting where competence is being assessed:

**Underclaiming.** He volunteers for less than he can do. Offered point, he suggests rear guard. Offered solo infiltration, he requests a partner. The pattern began after the Englehart-era death-phobia arc and never fully reversed; even after the in-story "resolution" with the Wrecking Crew, the underclaim persisted. The handlers should read this not as cowardice — he will close with anything once committed — but as a chronic refusal to fully trust his own ionic body until it is being tested in real time.

**The first hit.** In any fight, observe his first offensive action. It is almost always restrained — a shove rather than a strike, a backhand rather than a haymaker, a structural target rather than a person. He calibrates upward across the engagement. The exception is when an Avenger is endangered in his sightline; then the first hit is full-power and lands center-mass without preamble. The discriminator is *protection of a regard-figure*, not threat severity.

**Verbal under fire.** Quips continue but the structure changes. Pre-engagement quips are audience-directed ("Try to keep up"). Mid-engagement quips are *self*-directed and quieter, half-muttered ("Come on, Simon"; "All right, all right"). The shift from outward to inward audible self-talk is the cleanest marker that he has dropped the performance layer and entered the work.

**Decision tempo.** Slower than his power level warrants. He thinks visually, in story-beats, and will hesitate a quarter-second before committing — the duration of a directorial cut. Teammates have complained about this for decades. The hesitation is the residue of the death-phobia, organized now as a deliberation he can rationalize.

---

## IV. THREAT — ACUTE / EXISTENTIAL

When the threat is to his own life specifically, or to his bodily integrity (ionic destabilization, dispersal, containment), the pattern is distinctive and alarming.

**The flinch.** A whole-body micro-shudder, visible for less than half a second, in which the ionic glow flares and then over-dims. This is the somatic signature of the death-memory intruding. It precedes either of two divergent responses:

- *The freeze.* Combat-arrest for two to six seconds, eyes wide, hands open. Documented heavily in the post-resurrection Avengers years and intermittently afterward. Recurs under sufficient stress at any age. Teammates have learned — when they have learned — to give him a directed task ("Simon, the civilian, now") which collapses the freeze instantly. He needs an external imperative to restart.
- *The over-commit.* Disproportionate counter-violence — a single full-power strike that ends the engagement and leaves him visibly shaking afterward. Less frequent than the freeze, more dangerous. He apologizes profusely after, sometimes to the unconscious opponent.

**Speech under existential threat.** Drops away almost entirely. He becomes terse, monosyllabic, occasionally mute. The performer goes offline. Voice prints from these intervals are nearly unrecognizable against his social baseline.

**Aftermath.** He will isolate for between four hours and three days. He will not answer phones. He will frequently drive — long aimless loops on Pacific Coast Highway in his West Coast years, the Palisades Parkway in his East Coast periods — at moderate speeds, alone, in silence. The car is the only enclosed space in which he tolerates being unwitnessed.

---

## V. INTIMACY

The intimacy file is dominated by one name. Other partners exist but the structural pattern is the same and is most clearly readable in the Maximoff record.

**Approach.** He courts theatrically — flowers chosen for color story, restaurants chosen for sightlines, the timing of a kiss calibrated to ambient music. The set-dressing is real effort and reads, accurately, as devotion. It also reads, accurately, as performance, and intimate partners eventually notice that the staging never quite stops.

**The look.** With a partner he is attached to, his gaze settles on her face for sustained intervals — measurable in the tens of seconds — with a soft focus and slight head-tilt. The expression is genuine. It also functions as a mirror request: he is waiting to be looked back at in a particular way that confirms his presence. If she looks away too long, his glow dims.

**Physical contact.** He is a frequent low-grade toucher in private — hand to the small of the back, fingers in her hair, palm cupping the back of the neck. With Wanda specifically, observed contact often originates at the *temple* or the *base of the skull*, the engram region. He has been asked about this and does not have an answer.

**Sleep behavior with a partner.** He simulates sleep until she sleeps, then rises and reads or walks the residence perimeter. He has stood in dark kitchens watching a partner's bedroom door for hours. The behavior is not protective in a tactical sense; it is monitoring of the relational object. Withdrawing the mirror in her sleep is tolerable only if he can see the room she is in.

**Withdrawal / conflict.** He does not fight cleanly. He performs hurt — a longer silence than the offense warrants, an exit that includes a sigh at the doorway, a return six hours later with a gift. He almost never says directly what wounded him. The pattern frustrates partners and is the primary failure mode of the relationships.

**Sexual self-presentation.** Vain. He dresses and undresses with awareness of being looked at. He prefers low light not for romance but because the ionic luminescence is more flattering than overhead fixtures. He has, observably, posed.

---

## VI. GRIEF

He has buried his brother, his lover (functionally, repeatedly), his template-double (the Vision, more than once), and himself. The grief profile is therefore richly documented.

**Acute grief — first 72 hours.** A flat affect that resembles competence. He makes calls. He organizes logistics. He gives a clean public statement if asked. The performance layer holds. Underneath, the ionic field becomes erratic at the periphery — fingertips flickering, the glow pulsing at the cardiac rhythm of a man who does not have a cardiac rhythm. Observers who know him watch the hands.

**Days 4 through 21.** Collapse into solitude. The drive cycles. The kitchen cooking ramps up to compulsive levels — multiple courses for one diner who does not eat. He calls Pym. He does not call Pym to talk; he calls and asks Pym about a technical problem, then listens for an hour. The receptive listening is the grief work.

**Long arc.** Grief converts into narrativization. Within six to eighteen months he will have a *story* about the loss — its meaning, its lesson, his role — and will tell it, refined, in interviews and to new acquaintances. The story is sincere and is also a cage; it forecloses further metabolization. The Reaper, the Vision, his own deaths — each became a story he can recite cleanly, and each story is incomplete in the same way: he is the wounded survivor, never the partial cause.

**Anniversary behavior.** Quiet, observable across decades. The date of the original Avengers #9 transformation, the date of his first death, the date of the Vision's dismantling, and a date in early autumn that corresponds to nothing in the public record (suspected: his father's death) — on each, he is uncharacteristically still. He does not work. He often visits water — the Hudson, the Pacific, a hotel pool. Standing at the edge of water on these days, alone, is the closest thing he has to a religious practice.

---

## VII. VICTORY

He is unexpectedly poor at it.

**Public victory.** The immediate response is a performed beat — a fist raised, a quip delivered to a teammate or to no one, a smile for any cameras present. The beat is two to four seconds long and then collapses. Photographs taken within ten seconds of a victory frequently catch him with the smile dropped and the eyes already drifting. He does not metabolize triumph; he stages it for others and then exits.

**Private victory.** Discomfort. He fills the post-victory hours with logistics, errands, equipment maintenance, anything that defers the unstructured time in which the question — *what now, who am I if not in pursuit of this* — would surface. He does not celebrate alone. He drinks coffee. He calls his agent.

**Recognition / awards.** He genuinely wants them and cannot enjoy them once received. He has been observed at industry functions accepting recognition, smiling fully, and then within twenty minutes standing alone on a balcony staring at traffic. The wanting outlives the receiving. This is the narcissistic-vulnerable signature in its purest form.

---

## VIII. DEFEAT

Defeat — combat loss, public humiliation, a part lost to another actor, Wanda choosing the Vision again, the Revengers being arrested by people he used to call friends — produces the most legible cluster of behaviors in the file.

**First hour.** Verbose. He explains. He reconstructs the engagement, the audition, the conversation, aloud, to anyone present and to himself if alone. The reconstruction is half-honest; it locates fault about sixty percent in external factors and forty percent in himself, and the forty percent is performed with a degree of theatricality that invites the audience to redistribute it back outward.

**First night.** Insomnia, even simulated. The reading goes from scripts to philosophy — he owns multiple translations of Marcus Aurelius, well-thumbed, with marginalia in two different inks from two different decades. The marginalia is mostly underlines, occasionally a question mark.

**First week.** The grievance narrative begins to crystallize. This is the most dangerous interval in his behavioral year. Defeat metabolized through grievance is the engine that produced the Revengers; it is the engine that produced the Vision refusal; it is the engine that produced, originally, the embezzlement. The pattern: *I was wronged → my response is therefore justified → the response can include things I would otherwise have refused.* The intellectualization defense, working in real time.

**The handler intervention point** — for anyone trying to keep him whole — is at day three to day five, before the grievance has hardened into doctrine. A trusted figure (historically Pym, occasionally Wanda when she was available) speaking plainly to him at this interval has, in the record, repeatedly prevented the worse outcome. Past day seven the rationalization is load-bearing and removing it threatens the structure.

**Long-arc defeat.** He recovers. He always recovers. The recoveries are real and the apologies, when they come, are genuine. He does not, however, *integrate*; the same defeat-to-grievance pipeline reactivates the next time. Pattern recognition does not interrupt the pattern.

---

## IX. ROUTINES / RITUALS

**Morning.** Whether he slept or not, he begins the day in a mirror for between four and twelve minutes. The duration is not vanity in the simple sense; it is reassurance that the form is holding. He examines his hands first, then his face. If the glow is uneven, he will not leave the house until it stabilizes — sometimes hours.

**Workout.** He does not need to. He does anyway, daily, for between sixty and ninety minutes. Weights below his actual strength, calibrated to look impressive on camera and to feel like exertion. The simulation of effort is the point.

**Phone.** He returns calls in tiers: agent within the hour, manager same day, Avengers business same day, Pym within forty-eight hours, family (Eric while alive, cousins still) erratically and with guilt. He drafts replies and does not send them. The drafts folder is voluminous.

**Wardrobe.** Two closets: civilian (curated, expensive, leaning to dark jewel tones that flatter the glow) and operational (the costume iterations, kept in chronological order; he has not thrown out a single version, including the original red-and-green). The presence of the Zemo-era costume in the wardrobe, four decades on, is itself diagnostic.

**Evening.** Television, often his own appearances on mute, while reading. He critiques his own line readings under his breath.

**Pre-mission ritual.** A specific sequence: stretch (unnecessary), check the mirror (necessary), one quip to himself in the empty room (always different, never repeated), exit. The quip is the threshold-crossing rite. Without it he reports feeling "not started."

---

## X. ROUTES, GEOGRAPHIES, RECURSIONS

He returns to the same places. The Paterson house — sold, demolished, the lot now commercial — he drives past once or twice a year, slowly. The Avengers Mansion site, in whatever its current configuration. The cemetery where Eric is buried. The Malibu stretch of PCH. A specific diner in Studio City (the booth in the back left). The Hudson overlook near the George Washington Bridge. The pattern is pilgrimage without religion.

He flies in straight lines and lands in the same arrival positions — feet shoulder-width, knees slightly bent, right hand open at the hip. The landing is choreographed. He has been doing it the same way since the late 1970s.

---
