## XI. THE TELLS THAT MATTER MOST

If a single observer had to track three indicators to know Simon Williams's true internal state at any given moment:

1. **The ionic glow at the fingertips.** Brighter than face means agitation; dimmer than face means dissociation; uneven between the two hands means he is consciously suppressing affect. The hands do not lie; the face does.
2. **The frequency and direction of self-talk.** Audible quips outward = social performance, stable. Audible quips inward = working, stable. Silence = either deep calm (rare) or acute threat (common). No quips and no silence — speech that is purely functional and short — is the marker of the post-defeat interval and is the window in which intervention is possible.
3. **Whether he has called Hank Pym in the last seventy-two hours.** If yes, he is metabolizing something and the system is working. If no, and a stressor has occurred, the grievance pipeline is engaging and will harden within days.

These three, sustained over time, would give any sufficiently patient observer near-complete read access to a man who has spent his entire post-transformation life trying to be looked at without being seen.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*Subject: WILLIAMS, SIMON — "Wonder Man"*
*Surveillance synthesis: composite seven-day envelope, drawn from longitudinal observation across the West Coast / Hollywood, Avengers Compound, Force Works, and post-Bendis L.A.-based residency periods. Routines vary by era; underlying architecture does not.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of a Day

The first thing to record about Subject's daily life is that it is **structured to fill time he no longer biologically needs to fill.** Ionic physiology has removed the three great organizing imperatives of human days: hunger, fatigue, the demand to breathe through sleep. Subject does not require food, does not require sleep, does not require rest in any conventional sense. What surveillance therefore captures is not a man metabolizing a day but a man *performing* one — eating because eating is what people do at restaurants where people see him, sleeping because the bedroom is where Wanda once slept beside him, going to the gym because the gym is what an action lead is photographed leaving.

This is the load-bearing observation for the entire section. Every routine that follows is **elective ritual**, not biological necessity. He keeps them because without them the day has no shape, and a day without shape exposes the absence of a stable self to organize it.

## 6.2 The Residence — Habits of Place

Across the West Coast and post-West Coast eras, Subject has cycled through three residence types: the Avengers Compound suite (institutional), a series of Hollywood Hills / Beverly Glen rentals (performative), and during ionic-discorporation periods, no fixed residence at all (he simply *was* near Wanda). The current pattern, since the late Bendis period, is a leased mid-century house on the western side of the Hollywood Hills — view of the basin, single-story, pool, three-car garage with two cars in it.

**Observable habits of the residence:**

- **Lights left on after departure.** Consistent across years. He leaves at least two interior lights and the exterior path lighting on whenever he goes out, regardless of time of day. Tell: a man who does not like returning to a dark house, and a man whose ionic eyes glow faintly in the dark — he has commented on camera (press junket, late 2010s) that he "prefers the lights on." Read: aversion to seeing his own reflection unlit.
- **No interior mirrors except the bathroom.** Two confirmed residences. Wall art instead — framed posters of his own films, framed Avengers commendations, one framed handwritten note from Hank Pym (contents unknown, surveillance through window only). The absence of mirrors in a vanity-driven personality is significant: he prefers *images* of himself (controlled, posed, lit) to *reflections* (live, unflattering, uncertain).
- **The thermostat is set low — 64°F nights, 66°F days.** He does not feel temperature in the human sense; the setting is for guests and for the appearance of a normal home. The cleaning service has complained on file.
- **One room kept locked.** Across at least two residences, surveillance and household-staff testimony confirm a single interior room — small, off the main hall — kept locked when not in use by Subject himself. Best inference from incidental observation: a memorabilia room containing items relating to the Vision, to Wanda, to his brother Eric, and to his own death-and-resurrection cycle. He enters it alone, infrequently (estimated 1–3 visits per month), and remains inside for 20–90 minutes. He does not discuss this room.
- **The pool is never used for swimming.** He sits beside it. He does not enter it. (He floats. Buoyancy is wrong. The pool is for the image of having a pool.)

## 6.3 The Morning Sequence

Subject does not wake — he *resumes*. Surveillance footage and reported testimony converge on the following pattern, executed with notable consistency across years:

- **0530–0600:** Exits the bedroom, having spent the prior 4–6 hours in a state best described as *recumbent stillness with eyes closed.* He has explained this in interviews as "a habit I keep" rather than a need. He lies on the right side of the bed only. The left side remains made.
- **0600–0615:** Coffee. He does not metabolize caffeine in any functional sense, but he brews a full pot, drinks two black cups, and pours the rest down the sink. The brand has remained constant for over a decade (a specific Los Angeles roaster). The mug rotates from a small collection of three; one is from the original Avengers gift shop run, one from a film he made, one plain white. He uses the plain white one most.
- **0615–0700:** The patio. He sits outside, facing east, watching the light come up over the basin. He does not read, does not check a phone, does not move. This is the longest sustained period of immobility in his daily cycle and the only one not organized around being observed. Note: this is also the period during which, per junket testimony, he composes "ideas" — for scripts, for speeches, for what to say to people. He thinks in narratives; the patio is where the day's narrative is drafted.
- **0700–0830:** The gym. Either a private home gym (current residence) or a specific Beverly Hills facility used during press cycles. The workout is theatrical — heavy compound lifts at weights he does not need to strain to move, performed with visible effort. He is observed selecting weights one or two plates below his actual capacity and performing them as if at limit. The performance is for any observer present, including, on empty mornings, security cameras. He has been recorded checking his form in the gym mirror — the only mirror he willingly engages — for an average of 4.2 seconds per set, with characteristic micro-adjustment of the jaw and shoulder line.

## 6.4 Grooming, Wardrobe, and the Daily Construction of the Face

Grooming is the most ritualized portion of Subject's day and the most diagnostically loaded.

- **Shaving:** Daily. With a straight razor, not an electric or safety razor — surveillance through bathroom window confirms. Ionic skin does not grow hair in the conventional metabolic sense; the stubble he removes is essentially symbolic. He does it anyway, slowly, for 8–12 minutes. The ritual matters more than the result.
- **Hair:** Maintained at a precise length, retouched every 17–21 days at one of two salons (Beverly Hills primary, Burbank secondary near studios). He tips well and consistently. He arrives early to every appointment.
- **Wardrobe:** A wardrobe of substantial size but narrow palette — blacks, charcoals, deep reds, off-whites. The red is the highest-percentage color, including in items not visible in public (interior pajamas, robes, gym shirts). Read: the costume color has migrated into the civilian closet. He dresses, even alone, in the palette of the persona.
- **Sunglasses:** Always on hand, frequently worn indoors. Functional purpose: the ionic eye-glow is suppressible but tiring to suppress for extended periods; the lenses do the work. Secondary purpose: a barrier between the live face and any observer. He removes them deliberately, with timing, when he wants a moment to land.
- **Cologne:** A single scent, worn daily, in modest application. Same brand for roughly fifteen years. Wanda mentioned, once, in an early West Coast era conversation that she liked it. Surveillance: she has not mentioned it since; he has not changed it.

## 6.5 Work — The Performative Day

Subject's work-life splits across three concurrent identities, each with its own daily rhythm:

### 6.5.a The Actor / Public Figure

- **Audition and meeting cycles:** Driven by his representation (a long-standing agent relationship — Subject does not change agents; loyalty to anyone who stuck with him through the death/resurrection scandal era is absolute). Meetings are concentrated 1000–1500 weekdays. He is punctual to a fault, arriving 10–15 minutes early to every meeting and waiting in his car if necessary.
- **On-set behavior (production weeks):** Arrives first to set among principals. Memorizes not only his own lines but those of every scene partner — a behavior crew members read as professional courtesy and which is, more accurately, a need to control the narrative of a scene before stepping into it. Performs his own stunts to a degree that has generated insurance complaints. Does not require a trailer for resting (he does not rest) but maintains one for the appearance and for receiving visitors. Tips crew at wrap.
- **Press obligations:** Engages willingly, almost compulsively. Junket days are 12–14 hours. He is observed to grow visibly more *animated* as the day progresses, not less — being looked at is restorative for him in a way that exhausts other actors. The post-junket comedown, observed in hotel suite footage, is a period of approximately 90 minutes of complete stillness on a couch.
- **Premieres:** Always attends. Always walks the carpet. Always signs for the fans behind the rope, often longer than handlers prefer. The fan interaction is observably his preferred portion of any public event — direct, mirrored regard, no critic in the mix.

### 6.5.b The Avenger / Operational Reserve

- Has, since the post-Bendis period, maintained reserve status with the team rather than full active duty. The pattern is: training visits to the facility 1–2 times per week, usually Tuesday and Friday mornings if production schedule permits; full deployment only on call-up.
- During training visits, he gravitates to specific teammates and avoids others. He will spar with anyone who asks. He volunteers for sessions with newer members and is reportedly an unusually patient instructor — an observation worth flagging: when occupying the *senior* role in an asymmetric relationship, he is at his best.
- He does not, on visits, enter certain rooms. The room formerly used by the Vision in any iteration is consistently bypassed. The route he takes through the facility avoids it without comment.

### 6.5.c The Private Reckoner

This is the work no one assigns and he never names. Evening hours (see 6.7) are devoted to a third labor: managing the narrative of his own life. He keeps a journal (long-standing — observed in at least four distinct notebook styles over the surveillance window). He drafts statements he never issues. He composes letters to the dead (Eric, the Vision in its various iterations) and does not send them. The Revengers manifesto, when it eventually surfaced, was not a sudden production; it was a long-gestated artifact, and parallel artifacts are presumed to be in continuous production.

## 6.6 Eating, Drinking, and the Social Theater of the Meal

He does not need to eat. He eats anyway, and the patterns are precise:

- **Solo meals:** Skipped or minimal. Coffee in the morning, water through the day, sometimes a piece of fruit handled but not always finished. A man genuinely uninterested in eating when no one is watching.
- **Restaurant meals:** Frequent, scheduled, location-rotated among a stable set of West Hollywood, Beverly Hills, and Studio City venues. He has standing tables. He tips at roughly 30%. He orders the same dish at each venue across years — at one steakhouse the order has not changed since the early West Coast era — which staff read as discernment and which is more accurately a refusal to be observed deliberating.
- **Hosted meals at home:** Rare but lavish. He cooks (a skill acquired late, in the Hollywood era), competently if showily. The cooking is performance.
- **Alcohol:** Conspicuously absent. He keeps a stocked bar for guests, does not consume it himself, and will hold a wineglass through an entire dinner without drinking. The non-drinking pre-dates ionic transformation as a documented behavior — relevant given the actor milieu. Subject does not lose control voluntarily.
- **Cigars:** One specific brand, occasional, primarily on the patio, primarily after stressful press days. He does not inhale. The cigar is a prop and a timer.

## 6.7 Evening and the Long Hours

Evenings divide into a public phase and a private phase.

- **1900–2200 (public phase):** Dinners, events, screenings, calls. He is reachable, social, performing. He returns calls promptly — a trait teammates have praised — and the promptness is, again, the tell. To not return a call is to risk not being needed; he cannot tolerate the risk.
- **2200–0100 (transitional phase):** Home, alone or with one companion. Television on, often unwatched. He has been observed re-watching his own work, in particular older films, with the sound low, while doing other things. The act reads less as vanity than as *verification* — confirming the existence of the recorded self.
- **0100–0530 (the long hours):** This is the most diagnostically important window in the day and the one a surveillance file would weight heavily. Subject does not sleep. What he does:
  - Sits, often in the same chair, often facing a window.
  - Reads — across observation, primarily biography, history, and screenplays. Notable: very little fiction, and almost no fiction in which the protagonist is similar to him in obvious ways. He is uninterested in mirrors.
  - Writes in the journal.
  - Makes calls he would not make in daylight — to Wanda, during eras she would accept them; to his mother, while she lived; to Pym; occasionally to his agent; very occasionally to numbers that route to no one in particular (read: he calls and lets the line ring, then hangs up, the recipient being structurally beside the point).
  - Walks. The walks are the single most consistent post-midnight behavior. He leaves the house on foot — sometimes for hours — and traverses a habitual circuit through Hollywood Hills streets, occasionally descending into the city flats. He does not fly during these walks. He keeps his eyes ahead. Surveillance has captured him stopping at specific addresses (a previous residence; the site of an early West Coast Avengers compound; once a property historically associated with Wanda) and standing for several minutes before walking on. He talks to himself audibly during these walks at a low volume — the few captured fragments are rehearsals of conversations, apologies, declarations, and the occasional line reading.

The long hours are when he is most himself, by which the file means: most exposed, least armored, least watched. The day is performance. The night is the residue.

## 6.8 Weekly Rhythms

Across a representative week of surveillance:

- **Monday:** Heavy work day. Meetings, gym, evening dinner with industry contacts. Returns home late. Long-hours window unusually short — he sleeps (or simulates it) closer to four hours of stillness.
- **Tuesday:** Avengers facility morning. Lunch alone or with one teammate. Afternoon free; often script work. Evening typically light. He has been observed watching old Avengers footage on Tuesday evenings, which suggests the morning visit primes the retrospective mood.
- **Wednesday:** "Audience day" by pattern — public appearances, fan-facing events, charity obligations when scheduled. He is brightest on Wednesdays.
- **Thursday:** Production or press, depending on cycle. Heaviest commercial-output day.
- **Friday:** Avengers facility morning (second weekly visit). Evening: dinner, usually scheduled with a stable rotation of three to five close contacts. Pym (when available and contact is current) is in the rotation.
- **Saturday:** The least predictable day. Sometimes entirely public; sometimes entirely withdrawn. The variance reads as mood-driven — Saturday is when the week's accumulated regulation either holds or doesn't.
- **Sunday:** Quiet. Late patio sit (extended; sometimes two hours rather than the weekday 45 minutes). Phone calls to family and the few remaining figures from before the transformation. Occasional drive — alone, no destination logged, route varies — that lasts three to six hours and ends back at the residence. The Sunday drives are the closest behavior in his week to genuine unstructured time, and they are notably uncomfortable for him; he often cuts them short and returns to a scheduled obligation invented on the way home.

## 6.9 Recurrent Pilgrimages and Anniversary Behavior

A surveillance file maintained across years detects calendar-anchored behaviors invisible in any single week:

- **Anniversary of original death (Avengers #9 events):** Subject withdraws. Cancels meetings within a 48-hour window around the date. Spends extended time in the locked room. Does not take calls. Has been observed, on at least two such dates, traveling alone to Paterson, NJ — to the cemetery containing his parents, and reportedly to the original site of Williams Innovations.
- **Anniversary of Eric's final death:** Pattern less consistent but observable — heavy drinking by proxy (he pours, does not drink, refills the same untouched glass through an evening). Calls to a priest he does not otherwise consult.
- **Wanda's birthday:** Some gesture, every year, varying in scale by the state of their relationship in that year. Even in periods of estrangement, the gesture is made — sometimes only a flower delivery, sometimes nothing she would see, only something done.
- **Vision-related anniversaries (the dismantling, various reconstitutions):** Subject does not mark these publicly. But journal-writing volume, as inferable from observed sitting-and-writing durations on those dates, is elevated. The Vision is the unfinished business of his life, and the calendar knows it even when he won't.

## 6.10 Micro-Patterns, Tics, and Tells

A close file records the small things. For Subject:

- **The jaw set.** When stressed or when transitioning into a public-facing posture, he sets his jaw with a small forward motion and a single closure. Photographers have caught it thousands of times; it is the moment the persona engages.
- **The hand to the chest.** When moved — sincerely — he places his right hand flat over the sternum, briefly. The gesture is not theatrical; it is involuntary and short. It appears in conversations about Wanda, about Pym, about his mother, and once on camera about a dead fan.
- **The pause before names.** He pauses, fractionally, before saying "Vision" or "Eric" aloud. Less than a second. Audible only on careful playback. It is the single most reliable somatic tell in his behavioral repertoire.
- **The over-tip.** Mentioned above; it is patterned. He tips more when he is feeling less. Wait staff at his rotated venues have, without coordinating, independently observed that the largest tips correlate with the quietest demeanors.
- **The sunglasses removal.** Always two-handed. Always slow. Always timed to a beat in the conversation. Performance, but also: a man giving the room his eyes is a man making a decision about visibility.
- **The phone in the pocket, not on the table.** Unusual in his industry. He does not place phones on tables. Read: he does not want the device to be the third party in any encounter; he wants the encounter to be about being looked at.
- **The walk-out posture.** Leaving any room with more than one person in it, he straightens marginally at the threshold and his shoulders set back roughly a centimeter. He is checking that he is being watched leave. Surveillance can use this reliably to time exits.
- **The breath.** He does not need to breathe. He breathes anyway, audibly, in moments of emotional weight — a sharp inhale before a difficult sentence, a long exhale after. The breath is theatrical *and* genuine; the body remembers the pattern even though the lungs no longer require it. It is perhaps the cleanest single image of the man: a body performing the gestures of being alive because being alive is what he is trying, every day, to convincingly perform.

## 6.11 What a Week of Surveillance Would Conclude

That the Subject lives a life of constant, disciplined, low-grade performance, organized around being visible to someone — an audience, a teammate, a lover, a camera, a cemetery. That the performance is not insincere; it is the chosen instrument by which an unstable self holds shape across hours that biology no longer organizes. That the routines are *prosthetic identity*: the gym at 0700, the coffee in the white mug, the straight razor at the sink, the patio at dawn, the journal at 0300, the walk at 0400, the standing table at the steakhouse, the unsent letter, the locked room — these are the trellis on which a man whose substance has been rewritten too many times grows the appearance of a continuous life.

That, accordingly, the surveillance-relevant vulnerabilities are not in his work calendar (well-defended, professionally managed, predictable in useful ways) but in **the long hours, the pilgrimages, the locked room, and the pause before two names.** A handler, an antagonist, or a friend who wished to reach him would not approach the Avenger or the actor. They would approach the man walking, alone, in the Hollywood Hills at 0330, talking quietly to people who are not there.

*— UATU, Section 6 ends.*


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — SIMON WILLIAMS / WONDER MAN
## Section 6: Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

The subject's family of origin is a small, wealthy, brittle constellation in Paterson, New Jersey: father, mother, two sons. Three of the four are dead. The fourth — Simon — has died and returned multiple times. The bonds in this section are therefore mostly with the dead, conducted across the membrane of memory, guilt, and (in his brother's case) literal posthumous recurrence. They are also the bonds that wrote every later relationship in the file. Each is treated below at depth.

---

### 6.1 — SANFORD WILLIAMS (Father, deceased)

**Status:** Deceased pre-canon, of natural causes (heart, per scattered references across the Stern and Englehart runs). Buried in the family plot at Cedar Lawn, Paterson, alongside his wife. Subject visits irregularly — pattern below.

**History.** Sanford Williams built Williams Innovations from a single-line machine shop in the immediate postwar period into a mid-cap industrial concern specializing in electrical components and, by the late 1950s, contracting work adjacent to defense and aerospace. He was, on the evidence the subject has volunteered in conversations across decades (most expansively in *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* vol. 2 backups and in a confessional sequence with Beast in late-period *Avengers* arcs), a self-made first-generation success with the temperament typical of that profile: long hours, narrow affective range, conditional regard, an explicit preference for the elder son's aptitudes (mechanical, aggressive, decisive) over the younger son's (verbal, imaginative, conciliatory). He was not abusive in the colloquial sense. He was withholding in the more corrosive sense.

**Dynamic in childhood.** The subject was the second-born and from infancy was measured against an elder brother who could already do whatever the father valued. The household ran on industrial time: dinners at fixed hours, expectations articulated as standards rather than goals, praise rationed and tied to specific output. Anecdotal evidence the subject has reported: a science-fair project (a small motor, age twelve) that the father critiqued for tolerance rather than congratulated for completion; a baseball season (age fourteen) the father missed in entirety; a college decision (Rutgers, business and engineering) made on the father's instruction rather than the subject's preference (which had been literature, then theater — both vetoed). The father's death, in the subject's mid-twenties, occurred before any reconciliation, before any explicit transfer of approval, before the subject had produced anything the father would have credited.

**The inheritance event.** Sanford willed the company to Simon rather than to Eric. This is the single most consequential decision in the family file, and the file should not glide past it. Read it three ways:

1. **As a final paternal verdict.** Sanford may have judged Eric temperamentally unfit to run a business — too volatile, too aggressive, already showing the disturbances that would later flower into the Grim Reaper identity. Selecting Simon would then be a pragmatic act and arguably the only direct vote of confidence Sanford ever cast for his younger son.
2. **As a posthumous setup.** Sanford handed Simon a concern he had no aptitude to run, in a market about to be reorganized by Stark, with an older brother who would resent the bypass. The bequest is also a test the subject was statistically going to fail.
3. **As inadvertent cruelty.** Sanford likely did not consider how the choice would land. The not-considering is itself the relationship.

The subject has never resolved which reading is true. He has cycled through all three publicly. In stable periods (mid-West-Coast era; portions of the Busiek run) he tends toward (1). In shame-flares (post-embezzlement memory; post-Revengers collapse) he tends toward (3). In grievance episodes he has hinted at (2) without committing.

**Evolution of the bond after death.** The father is the loudest absent voice in the subject's interior. Every later authority figure is auditioned against him: Zemo (briefly, disastrously, as a counterfeit parental sponsor offering rescue and recognition); the Vision's "father" Ultron at one remove (the subject finds Ultron uniquely repugnant in ways that exceed the in-universe causes); Captain America (a clean paternal substitute the subject has always struggled to be fully comfortable around, deferring more than the relationship warrants); Hank Pym (lateral — but Simon's loyalty to Pym during the breakdown reads in part as the loyalty he wishes had existed in the other direction); even Tony Stark, against whom the subject's competition is partly his father's voice continued by other means.

**Trust / safety.** Posthumous, therefore unfalsifiable, therefore total in the negative sense: the subject cannot disprove his father's verdict by any subsequent act, because the father cannot revise it. This is the engine of the unappeasable shame.

**Failure mode.** When the subject feels professionally inadequate (and Williams Innovations' collapse is the prototype of every later inadequacy), he reverts to a small, polite, deferential register that is recognizably the register of a son in his father's office. Teammates who have seen this register (notably Pym, in a *West Coast Avengers* sequence; Wanda repeatedly) have remarked on its incongruity with the Wonder Man persona. It is the original self showing through the performance.

**Leverage.** Any sentence that begins "Your father would have —" will land. The subject knows this about himself and has constructed defenses (premature self-deprecation, joking pre-emption) that flag the vulnerability rather than concealing it.

---

### 6.2 — MARTHA WILLIAMS (née, surname uncertain in canon; Mother, deceased)

**Status:** Deceased before the father, of cancer, when the subject was in his late teens. Buried beside her husband. Subject visits her grave specifically — and separately from the father's — on or near her birthday in early autumn.

**History.** The mother is the thinnest figure in the documented record and, by inference, the most quietly load-bearing. She appears in occasional flashbacks (a single-panel kitchen scene; a hospital bedside; an embedded reference in a Wanda-Simon conversation in *Avengers West Coast* #50s) and in the subject's own infrequent volunteered references. The composite portrait: warm, literate, somewhat overshadowed within the household, the parent who supplied the soft regard the father did not. She read to both sons. She is the source of the subject's affinity for narrative, theater, and the romantic register that he later carried into his Hollywood career and into the way he loves Wanda.

**Dynamic in childhood.** She was the corrective presence and the buffer. The subject's earliest secure attachment was to her. She is the reason he developed a moral floor at all — not via doctrine, but via demonstrated kindness toward people the father dismissed. (The subject has cited, in one quiet exchange with Beast, his mother's habitual kindness to a factory bookkeeper the father had humiliated; the subject was perhaps nine.) She is also the reason the subject can sustain genuine guilt as an adult: she modeled what it looked like to feel for others.

**The illness and death.** She declined across roughly eighteen months. The subject was at Rutgers. He came home weekends. The father did not adjust his hours materially. Eric — already deteriorating — coped via absence and rage. The subject sat with her. He has not narrated this period in any detail in canon, which is itself diagnostic; he narrates everything else.

**Evolution of the bond after death.** She is the silent, undamaged interior figure. The subject has never disappointed her, in the simple sense that she did not live to see it. This is both a gift (a place of unimpeachable inner regard) and a trap (every later woman is auditioned against an idealized maternal warmth he can neither articulate nor obtain). Wanda receives the displaced freight. So, in different registers, do a handful of incidental figures across his career — Carol Danvers in a sisterly mode he is careful not to misread; the Wasp briefly; a costume designer on his second film whom he overpaid and overcredited without remembering why.

**Trust / safety.** Total, retrospective, idealized. The grave visits are the cleanest ritual in his life — short, unaccompanied, undocumented, no costume, no quip. He brings asters.

**Failure mode.** The idealization is the failure. Because she is the one un-spoiled interior object, he cannot risk testing her memory against any complicating evidence; he therefore does not investigate it. There is at least one family-friend witness (per a stray *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* backup) who could speak to her, and the subject has never sought him out. He preserves her by not looking too closely.

**Leverage.** Minimal in a hostile sense — she is too sealed off to be wielded easily. In a benevolent sense, any genuine engagement with the mother-memory tends to soften him within seconds. Wanda has unlocked him this way on at least two recorded occasions.

---

### 6.3 — ERIC WILLIAMS (Brother, the Grim Reaper, deceased — repeatedly)

**Status:** Currently deceased; previously deceased multiple times; cannot be trusted to remain so. The relationship is the most fully documented family bond in the file and the most psychologically constitutive after the father.

**History.** Eric was the elder by roughly three years. From childhood he was what the father valued and what the household feared: physically dominant, mechanically capable, temperamentally violent, with an early pattern of cruelty toward animals and toward Simon that escalated through adolescence. The cruelty toward Simon was specific — humiliations rather than beatings, designed to instruct rather than discharge. Eric drifted through young adulthood in and out of legitimate work, accumulated criminal associates, and by the time of Simon's prison sentence had moved fully into organized-crime adjacency (Maggia connections, per the early Reaper appearances).

**The triggering event.** Simon's apparent death after the Zemo betrayal radicalized Eric. He fabricated a scythe-based identity (the engineering aptitude finally directed at something) and pursued the Avengers under the banner of avenging his brother. This is the only documented instance of Eric experiencing grief, and he experienced it as rage rerouted outward. When Simon returned — wrong, partial, ionic — Eric reframed the returned brother as an abomination ("you are not my brother; you are a *thing* wearing him") and pursued him with the same energy for the rest of both their lives. The hatred is the love unable to find any other syntax.

**Dynamics across the canon.** Across the run from *Avengers* #102 through the West Coast era, *Vengeance* arcs, and the late-period Avengers stories, the encounters follow a stable script:

- Eric appears, often unexpectedly, often in association with the Lethal Legion or another fringe formation.
- He targets Simon specifically, frequently using third parties (Wanda; the Vision; civilians) as instruments to wound Simon by proxy.
- Combat is asymmetric: Simon is vastly more powerful and consistently refuses to use the advantage.
- Eric attempts to provoke a killing blow. Simon refuses.
- The encounter resolves with Eric's death by accident, by self-destruction, or by third-party intervention — never by Simon's hand. The subject has been scrupulous on this point across thirty years of provocation.
- Eric returns by some narrative mechanism. Begin again.

**Trust / safety.** Zero, in the protective sense. The subject knows Eric will kill him given the chance and will kill those near him for preference. Despite this, the subject has repeatedly refused to incapacitate Eric permanently when he could have. He has also, on at least two occasions, attempted reconciliation — once via direct conversation in a holding facility, once via a letter (the letter exists in the file; it is unsent, found among effects after one of Simon's deaths and retrieved on his return). Both attempts presupposed that some pre-violence Eric was recoverable. The evidence does not support that premise. The subject knows this and persists anyway.

**Evolution.** Early decades: shocked, hurt, trying to talk Eric down. Middle decades (late '80s, early '90s): grim, resigned, still refusing to kill. Late period: a more complicated grief in which the subject has begun to acknowledge that his refusal to let Eric die finally is itself an attachment, not a virtue — that he keeps fishing Eric out of the abyss because losing Eric is also losing the last person who knew him as a child. This is the most psychologically sophisticated insight the subject has produced about any of his bonds, and he produced it late, alone, in the quiet that follows the Revengers collapse.

**Failure mode.** Whenever Eric is in play, the subject's tactical judgment degrades sharply — he hesitates, he absorbs hits he should slip, he speaks when he should strike, he allows civilians into the engagement radius by miscalculating Eric's targeting. Teammates have learned to take Eric off the board themselves wherever possible (Hawkeye, Tigra, Vision in the West Coast era have all done this without consulting Simon first). Simon has consistently resented these interventions even when grateful for them.

**Leverage.** Massive and bilateral. Eric is the single most efficient way to destabilize the subject in a fight, in a conversation, or in a press cycle. Conversely, Eric's body — wherever the current corpse is interred — is a stabilizing object for the subject when he can visit it. He has done so at least twice in canon, briefly, and the visits read as visits to the brother he wanted, not the one he had.

**A note on the symbolic brother.** The Vision occupies a parallel slot in the subject's interior (treated in full in Relationships II). The structural point belongs here: Simon has, in effect, two brothers — one biological and homicidal, one synthetic and beloved-rival — and his behavior in each relationship contaminates the other. He could not bring himself to kill Eric; he could not bring himself to revive Vision when he had the brain patterns to do so. Both refusals come from the same place. The mercy and the cruelty are the same instinct, expressed in opposite directions, toward two figures occupying the same family position.

---

### 6.4 — CHILDREN (None of record)

**Status:** The subject has produced no biological or legal children. Given ionic physiology, biological reproduction is at best uncertain and has never been attempted with documentation. Given his serial deaths and his romantic instability, legal or adoptive parenthood has never been initiated.

**Significance.** This is not a neutral absence. The subject is in his presumptive sixties of subjective lived experience and has organized none of his attachments around producing or raising a child. The closest he has come is a paternal-adjacent fondness for various younger Avengers and West Coast teammates (a brief warmth toward Rick Jones; a careful, slightly stilted kindness to younger recruits in the *Mighty Avengers* and *Uncanny Avengers* periods). He is good with younger people in short doses and avoids commitments that would require sustained custodianship.

**Reading.** Three causes braid:
1. Ontological — he is unsure he is real or stable enough to be responsible for another life.
2. Wanda-coded — the only person he would have wanted children with had them by proxy with the Vision (Wiccan and Speed, complicated lineage), and that wound is intact.
3. Paternal-template — he has no working model of fatherhood he wishes to perpetuate, and has not done the interior work required to construct a new one.

**Leverage / failure mode.** A child placed in his protective custody under acute stress would either elicit his best (the moral-floor loyalty he has shown Pym extended in a new direction) or his worst (a destabilization he could not contain, given that the child would re-pose every unanswered question about his fitness as a Williams). The variable is whether his current self-cohesion is high enough at the moment of the test. He has refused such custodial roles when offered, citing schedule or temperament; the refusals read as accurate self-assessment.

---

### 6.5 — THE EXTENDED WILLIAMS / PATERSON ORIGIN BOND

**Status:** Effectively severed but ritually maintained.

**History and current state.** The subject has no living blood relatives of record. The Paterson house was sold during the bankruptcy following Williams Innovations' collapse; the subject did not contest the sale. Williams Innovations' assets were liquidated and absorbed by competitors, including some Stark subsidiaries (a wound he has never publicly acknowledged but which is in the record). A handful of former employees of the elder Williams remained in cordial contact with the subject through the 1970s; most are now deceased. One — a former plant foreman — corresponded with the subject sporadically into the West Coast era and is the closest thing the subject has to a witness from the original life. The subject has not been reliable about answering.

**The ritual.** Twice a year — early autumn, near the mother's birthday, and late winter, near the father's death-date — the subject returns to Paterson. The visits are brief and unaccompanied. He drives himself when possible (he has, across the decades, owned a sequence of unobtrusive American sedans for exactly this kind of trip — the Hollywood cars stay in California). He visits both graves. He spends a variable amount of time at the mother's; a uniformly short, uncomfortable time at the father's. He has, on at least three documented occasions, also driven past the former site of the Williams Innovations main plant, slowed, and continued without stopping. He does not enter the city otherwise. He does not eat there. He returns to wherever he is based the same day.

**Failure mode of the ritual.** When the subject skips the ritual — typically during high-stress periods or active deployments — within four to eight weeks a destabilization event tends to follow: an ionic flare, a relational rupture with Wanda or a teammate, a public statement he later regrets. The correlation is sufficient that an attentive handler could use the skipped visit as a predictive signal.

**Leverage.** Anyone with access to the Paterson graves, the former plant site, or the former-employee correspondence has indirect access to the subject's deepest stabilizing and destabilizing material. None of this is secured. He has never thought to secure it. The most consequential intelligence about Simon Williams is sitting in a cemetery office in northern New Jersey, untouched, because no one has thought to look for the second son of a man no one outside Paterson remembers.

---

### 6.6 — SYNTHESIS OF THE ORIGIN BONDS

The family file is a closed system of four people, three of whom are dead and one of whom keeps dying. Every other relationship in the subject's life — Wanda, the Vision, the Avengers as institution, Pym, Stark, Zemo, the public — is, in some measurable degree, an attempt to find a workable substitute for one of the four roles this system left vacant or wounded: the withholding father (Stark, Cap, Zemo-counterfeit); the lost mother (Wanda in part, idealized femininity broadly); the murderous brother (Eric himself, recurring; the Vision as inverse); the missing self (every persona he has performed). The subject has never re-formed a family of his own. The pattern is conspicuous and, given his stated romantic ideals, probably a quiet grief he has chosen not to name.

The operational summary for any handler, ally, or analyst working this file: the surest route to Simon Williams' interior is through Paterson, not through Hollywood, and not through the Avengers. The man who turned on Zemo in the first issue is the same boy who sat with his mother through eighteen months of decline and could not make his father proud. Everything since is commentary.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*A relational topology of the men and women through whom Simon Williams has, at various points, located himself. Subject does not maintain casual acquaintance well; every meaningful tie is overdetermined, history-laden, and load-bearing on his identity. We map the structural ones in descending order of psychological weight.*

---

## 1. Henry "Hank" Pym — The Brother He Chose

**Origin of the bond.** First meaningful contact during Simon's reintegration with the Avengers post-resurrection (mid-1970s). Pym, then in his own destabilization arc — the Yellowjacket identity-fracture, the marriage strain with Janet — is the first Avenger to treat Simon's death-terror as a real medical fact rather than a tactical inconvenience. The two share a defining substrate: both have been *remade by their own science or by another's*, both carry public shame for failure (Simon's embezzlement, Pym's eventual breakdown and the slap), both are perpetually overshadowed (Simon by Stark and the Vision; Pym by Stark and Janet). The recognition is mutual and immediate.

**Load-bearing event.** *Avengers* #213 and the subsequent court-martial / expulsion arc. Pym is, by any reasonable reading, indefensible in the moment; Simon defends him anyway — not the action but the man. He visits Pym at the lowest point, when even Janet has withdrawn, when the rest of the team is performing distance. The visits are quiet, undocumented in panel-time beyond a few scenes, but referenced and re-referenced in subsequent Pym-Simon dialogues for decades. The West Coast Avengers founding (*WCA* #1, 1984) is the institutional ratification: when Pym returns, Simon is on the roster, and the unspoken contract is *I was there.*

**Dynamics.** Pym is the only person in Simon's adult life who functions as a *peer-parent* — older, credentialed, broken in comparable ways, and willing to mirror Simon without competing with him. Critically, Pym is asexual relative to Simon's romantic field (no Wanda triangle), removing the rivalry vector that contaminates the Vision relationship. Conversation between them tends toward the technical (Pym explaining ionic instability in language Simon can metabolize), the confessional (post-mission decompression, often in Pym's lab, off-hours), and the gently humorous (Pym is the only Avenger Simon will allow to gently puncture his theatrics without flaring).

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon physically softens around Pym. The chest-out, chin-up Hollywood posture that he carries into team rooms relaxes; he sits, rather than leans on furniture; he speaks in his actual register, half a tone lower than the public Wonder Man voice. He will accept correction from Pym that he would not accept from Stark or Steve Rogers. Pym is also the only person Simon discusses his ionic flares with in technical detail, including the periods when the body destabilizes — he hides these from Wanda and from leadership but not from Pym.

**Evolution.** The relationship persists across every Pym identity (Yellowjacket, Goliath redux, Giant-Man, Wasp). It survives the Skrull-Pym substitution arc — when the real Pym returns, Simon's reflexive response is grief and apology for not having known. It survives the Revengers period: Pym is one of the named members of the Revengers initiative (*New Avengers Annual* #1, 2011), and Simon's ability to recruit him is precisely a function of the trust deposited over three decades. That recruitment is also the most morally compromised use Simon has ever made of the friendship — leveraging Pym's own broken places to staff a grievance crusade. Pym forgives. They always reconverge.

**Trust / safety register.** Highest in his life among living adults. Simon would surrender his location, his medical condition, his romantic state, and his strategic intentions to Pym without prompting. He has done so repeatedly.

**Failure mode.** Co-rumination. When both are destabilized, they reinforce each other's grievance-narratives rather than challenging them. The Revengers is the documented case. A more sustained example: long stretches of the late West Coast era where Pym's depressive inertia and Simon's vanity-anxiety produce conversations that *feel* like therapy and *function* as mutual permission.

**Leverage (for any third party).** Anyone wanting to move Simon — operationally, morally, or geographically — moves Pym first. Threat to Pym produces immediate and unconditional response from Simon; appeal from Pym overrides team chain-of-command in Simon's behavior tree. This is the largest single point of access in the subject's life that is not Wanda.

---

## 2. The Vision — The Brother He Made and Could Not Forgive

*Filed under allies because, despite everything, the Vision has fought beside Simon more often than against him, and because Simon's relationship to the Vision is structurally fraternal rather than antagonistic — closer to Eric than Simon will admit.*

**Origin.** The reveal (*Avengers* #135 era, then load-bearing through Englehart's *Vision and the Scarlet Witch*) that the Vision's brain patterns were copied from Simon's recorded engrams during the post-Zemo coma. The Vision is, in a literal computational sense, Simon's mind running on a different substrate. Simon learns this after the Vision has already married Wanda. The wound is foundational and never closes.

**Dynamics.** Simon experiences the Vision as the *successful* version of himself — the version that got the woman, kept the moral floor, was trusted by the team, was unembarrassed by the costume. Every interaction is contaminated by the asymmetry: the Vision is calm where Simon performs calm; the Vision is loved where Simon is admired; the Vision's existence is uncontested (until "VisionQuest") where Simon's is perpetually in question. Simon copes by alternating between exaggerated brotherly warmth (the "we're family, we share a mind" gestures, often performed in Wanda's presence) and quiet sabotage (small status moves, jokes at the Vision's expense, the occasional pointed reminder that the engrams came from him).

**Load-bearing event.** *West Coast Avengers* #42–45, "VisionQuest" (Byrne, 1989). After the Vision is dismantled and partially restored as a colorless, emotionally flattened version, the team requires Simon's brain patterns to restore the original personality. Simon refuses. He cites uncertainty about identity-overlap, about whether two of him should exist, about the metaphysical risk. The reading is unambiguous in subsequent issues and dialogue: he wanted Wanda, and a diminished Vision was the path. The refusal is the most morally compromised act of his career, and he knows it. Wanda knows it. The Vision, once restored to fuller function later, knows it.

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** With the Vision, Simon's voice rises half a tone — the Wonder Man performative register, deployed defensively. He maintains slightly more physical distance than with other teammates (an extra half-step in line-up scenes, never sits directly adjacent). He uses the Vision's name more often than necessary in dialogue, a marker of forced familiarity. He avoids eye contact during disagreements and over-meets eye contact during shows of unity. He is the only Avenger who will publicly call the Vision "brother" — a tell, not an intimacy.

**Evolution.** Post-VisionQuest, post-Wanda's breakdown, the relationship cools to functional cooperation. The Vision, restored across various reconstructions (*Avengers Forever*, the Allred-adjacent *Vision* runs, etc.), maintains a kind of unilateral grace that Simon finds intolerable because he cannot match it. By the Bendis and post-Bendis eras, the two operate with the brittle politeness of estranged siblings on a holiday. The Revengers turn included an implicit refusal to fight alongside the Vision; the post-Revengers reconciliation included no real apology for VisionQuest, only an institutional return.

**Trust / safety register.** Functional but conditional. Simon will fight beside the Vision and trust the Vision's tactical decisions. Simon will not confide in the Vision and will not be vulnerable in the Vision's presence.

**Failure mode.** Jealousy rationalized as ethics or metaphysics. Whenever Simon is asked to do something that would *advance* the Vision (restore him, support his marriage, validate his personhood), he generates principled-sounding objections.

**Leverage.** The Vision is the cleanest threat-vector to Simon's self-concept that exists. Pressing on the engram-origin, on VisionQuest, or on the Vision's continued ability to feel and love produces immediate decompensation. Counter-leverage: Simon can be appealed to via the Vision's suffering — he *does* feel guilt, and a Vision in genuine peril activates the suppressed brotherly substrate. He has saved the Vision in battle more than once, often theatrically.

---

## 3. Beast (Hank McCoy) — The Acceptable Audience

**Origin.** Avengers tenure overlap, then deepened during the West Coast era and various Avengers reunions. McCoy is, in Simon's internal hierarchy, the *audience he respects who also respects him* — intellectually credentialed, verbally agile, performatively warm, and entirely uninterested in competing for Wanda or for leadership prestige.

**Dynamics.** Beast is the Avenger Simon will quip *with* rather than *at*. The two share a register — literary reference, mock grandiosity, ironic costume awareness — that allows Simon to deploy his performative apparatus without it being read as compensation. Beast's evident brilliance gives Simon a permission structure to be smart back without it being insecure: he is matching, not asserting. McCoy is also one of the only teammates who has openly engaged with Simon's ionic condition as a *medical curiosity rather than a tactical liability*, which Simon experiences as dignifying.

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon visibly enjoys Beast's company in a way he enjoys almost no one else's — the smile is wider, the laughter is not deployed, the body language opens. He will linger in rooms Beast is in. He has, on multiple occasions across runs, sought Beast out for what reads as social maintenance: showing up at the mansion without team business, ostensibly to "catch up."

**Trust / safety register.** High for intellectual and social vulnerability; lower for romantic or existential disclosure (those go to Pym, or to no one). Simon will tell Beast he is *worried* about a thing; he will tell Pym he is *frightened*.

**Failure mode.** Mutual indulgence in performance. Long conversations that produce no decision and metabolize no feeling. Beast is not a person who will *press* Simon; he is a person who will *match* him. In stable periods this is sustaining; in destabilizing periods it permits drift.

**Leverage.** Low individually — Beast is not load-bearing the way Pym is. But Beast is a reliable read on Simon's state: if Simon is avoiding Beast in social settings, the subject is destabilizing.

---

## 4. Carol Danvers — The Peer Who Sees Him Plainly

**Origin.** Cross-team association, deepening across the late Bendis and post-Bendis eras as Carol's institutional weight grew. Earlier overlap during the Avengers' classical configurations was warmer-acquaintance level; the load comes later.

**Dynamics.** Carol is the only woman in Simon's adult professional life who has neither romantic charge nor maternal/sororal coding for him — she is a peer, full stop, and she has no patience for the performative apparatus. She calls him on the vanity, on the grievance-arc rhetoric, and on the Revengers position directly, without contempt. Simon finds this both galling and stabilizing. She is, in a sense, the only person who treats him as a *competent adult who is currently behaving poorly* rather than as either a wounded artifact (the Pym frame) or a beloved fragment (the Wanda frame).

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon does not perform around Carol. He is at his most plainly-spoken in her presence — the chest-out posture relaxes but not into the Pym-softness; rather into something more like military bearing. He listens more than he speaks. He does not quip. He does not invoke the Hollywood persona.

**Trust / safety register.** Functional-high. Simon will accept tactical command from Carol without status-friction; he will accept moral correction from her in narrow circumstances; he will not confide.

**Failure mode.** Avoidance. When Simon is in a destabilized or compromised state, he stops returning Carol's calls. The absence is the symptom. She has, across runs, been one of the people who has had to chase him down and confront him; he has, across runs, eventually accepted the confrontation.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Carol is the team member most likely to successfully *talk him down* from a Revengers-type ideological turn, precisely because she will not flatter him or accommodate the grievance-narrative.

---

## 5. Steve Rogers — The Standard He Cannot Meet and Will Not Resent (Most of the Time)

**Origin.** Rogers is the Avenger who, in *Avengers* #9, gave Simon the second chance — accepted the Trojan-horse infiltrator at the door, treated him as a potential teammate rather than a potential threat. Simon's switch against Zemo was, in significant part, a response to Rogers' immediate good faith. This is the foundational reception of Simon Williams into anything resembling chosen family.

**Dynamics.** Simon's relationship to Rogers is the closest thing in his life to a relationship with an idealized father-substitute — and unlike his actual father, Rogers' regard has been substantively reliable. Simon performs his best self in Rogers' presence: more disciplined, more measured, less theatrical. He is also, however, perpetually *aware* of falling short of the Rogers standard, which produces a low-grade chronic shame that he manages by alternating between earnestness and self-deprecating humor.

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon stands straighter around Rogers. He uses the formal "Captain" or "Cap" in mission contexts and "Steve" in social ones, with a slight hesitation before the first name as if seeking permission. He will accept assignments from Rogers that he would resist from any other leader. He scans Rogers' face for approval and looks away when he catches himself doing it.

**Evolution.** The Revengers turn was, among other things, a confrontation of Rogers — explicitly framed as the Avengers (and by extension their iconic captain) being a destabilizing force. The repudiation was load-bearing for Simon precisely *because* of how much Rogers' regard had previously organized his behavior. Post-Revengers reconciliation included a quieter, more guarded version of the original relationship; the easy paternal warmth was not fully restored.

**Trust / safety register.** High operational, moderate emotional, asymmetric: Simon trusts Rogers more than Rogers can fully trust Simon, and both know this.

**Failure mode.** The very intensity of Simon's need for Rogers' regard makes any perceived rejection from Rogers catastrophic. A measured Rogers critique can produce days of destabilization. Conversely, Rogers' approval can paper over real moral problems in Simon's conduct that other voices might productively challenge.

**Leverage.** Rogers can ask Simon to do almost anything in service of the team and receive compliance, *unless* the Revengers-type ideology is active, in which case Rogers becomes the explicit symbolic target and the leverage inverts.

---

## 6. Clint Barton — The Sibling Rival Who Became Comfortable

**Origin.** West Coast Avengers founding era. Barton, as field leader of the WCA, is Simon's nominal commander; the two share locker-room temperament — banter, status games, theatrical masculinity — but lack the deep wound-overlap that makes the Pym bond load-bearing.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is *fraternal in the easy sense* — the brother Simon never had, as opposed to the brother he did have or the brother he made. There is friction (status competition, occasional sniping about the Hollywood career, mild jealousy on Clint's part about Simon's powers and on Simon's part about Clint's evident comfort in his own skin), but the friction is metabolized through humor and produces no lasting damage. They have functioned as effective tactical partners across multiple team configurations.

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon trash-talks Barton in a register he uses with no one else — broader, more affectionate, more crudely competitive. He will haze and be hazed. He will accept a punch in the shoulder and return it. The physicality is unusual for him: with most teammates he maintains controlled distance; with Barton he is easy.

**Trust / safety register.** High tactical, moderate-low emotional. Simon will not confide existential matters in Barton, but he will accept Barton's read on situational ones.

**Failure mode.** Both men, in destabilization, retreat into bravado. Together, they can perform stability past the point where one of them should be sitting down.

**Leverage.** Barton is one of the few people who can puncture Simon's pretensions in real time without producing rupture — useful as a course-correction lever when Simon is sliding into the performative apparatus but not yet committed to a full grievance-arc.

---

## 7. Wonder Man's "Hollywood Circle" — The Curated Audience

*Not chosen family in the deep sense. Filed because of behavioral significance.*

A rotating cast of agents, directors, fellow stunt performers, publicists, and trainers across the West Coast and subsequent Hollywood-adjacent eras. Names vary by run; the structural role is constant. These are the people who organize Simon's *performed* identity — the bookings, the press, the image, the gym schedule, the diet (such as it is, given ionic physiology), the social calendar.

**Dynamics.** Transactional warmth on Simon's side; he is gracious, generous with money, easy on set. He genuinely likes performers. But the relationships are structurally one-way: they admire him, manage him, profit from him; he does not confide in them and does not consider them family. He has, across runs, attended their weddings and funerals; he has, across runs, never invited any of them into a real conversation about the ionic condition or about Wanda.

**Behavioral micro-pattern.** Simon is at his most *aesthetically* curated in this milieu — wardrobe attentive, hair maintained, the public smile deployed at full wattage. He drinks soda water at industry parties (the sobriety pattern; see medical workup). He works the room with practiced patience. He tips well. He remembers names.

**Failure mode.** The Hollywood circle reinforces the performance-as-self defense; it provides Simon with continuous low-grade external validation that allows him to defer the harder work of metabolizing his shame substrate. In healthy periods, this is sustainable sublimation; in destabilizing periods, the circle is the place he goes to *avoid* the people who would actually help him.

**Leverage.** Low individually, moderate cumulatively. Disruption of the Hollywood apparatus (a public scandal, an industry blacklist) would remove a major affect-regulation system and likely accelerate destabilization.

---

## 8. The West Coast Avengers as Institution — The First Family of Choice

**Origin.** *WCA* #1, 1984, Englehart. Founding roster: Hawkeye, Mockingbird, Tigra, Iron Man (Rhodes-era), Wonder Man. Pym joins shortly. The team is, structurally, the first place Simon has ever been *senior* — a founding member rather than a probationary returnee.

**Dynamics.** Simon's behavior in the WCA is the clearest record of his *adequate-functioning baseline*: vain but loyal, performative but reliable, occasionally insecure but recoverable. He is liked. He is trusted with field operations. He flirts (with Tigra, episodically) without consequence. He builds the Hollywood career on the side without the team penalizing him. The setup approximates a healthy life.

**Failure mode.** The WCA era is also when the Wanda relationship consummates and then disintegrates, when the Vision is dismantled, when Simon makes the VisionQuest refusal. The institution does not protect him from the deepest wounds; it provides a stable enough container that he can survive them.

**Evolution.** The WCA's eventual dissolution and reformation as Force Works is felt by Simon as a personal loss. He takes nominal leadership in Force Works, performs poorly under the weight, and dies in service. The pattern repeats: when given the role of senior figure, he overextends and is consumed by it.

**Leverage / file note.** The WCA roster, in any reconstituted form, represents the highest-density concentration of people with claim on Simon's loyalty. A summons from a WCA alumna, particularly Mockingbird or Tigra, carries weight disproportionate to current institutional rank.

---

## 9. Mentors — The Negative Space

Simon has, structurally, *no functional mentor*. This is itself a diagnostic fact.

His father was a critical, withholding figure who died before reconciliation. Zemo was a coercive false-mentor whose recruitment was the seminal violation of his bodily integrity and moral standing. Stark, by every available indicator, would have been the natural mentor for an industrialist's son in the superhero business — and Stark is precisely the figure whose excellence destroyed Williams Innovations and broke the family. The relationship between the two men is, accordingly, polite-distant across the canon, with occasional warmer interludes that Simon does not allow to deepen. He cannot accept Stark as mentor because doing so would ratify the original humiliation.

Rogers occupies the closest analog (see above) but the relationship is paternal-symbolic rather than mentorial — Rogers does not teach Simon a craft or guide his development; he simply embodies a standard.

Pym is the closest thing to a *technical* mentor (re: the ionic condition) but is too damaged himself and too close in age and status to function as a true elder. The two are peers-with-asymmetric-credentialing rather than mentor-protégé.

The absence is consequential. Simon has never had a stable adult guide help him metabolize the original wound, the transformation, or the subsequent identity destabilizations. Every step of his moral development has been improvised against the immediate situation, without scaffolding. His repeated failures of judgment (the Vision refusal, the Revengers) are, among other things, the failures of a man making it up alone.

---

## 10. Protégés — The Symmetrical Absence

Simon has no protégés. He has never sustained a teaching relationship, never developed a younger hero, never extended downward what was never extended to him. The closest approximations are brief, mission-bounded mentorships to junior team members (variable across runs, none load-bearing).

This is consistent with the personality structure. To mentor requires a stable sense of *what one knows and is*, which Simon does not reliably possess. It also requires tolerating being looked at as an authority by someone who will eventually surpass you — and Simon has never resolved his relationship to being surpassed.

The absence is also a vulnerability. A figure positioning themselves as a *would-be protégé* — earnest, admiring, requesting guidance — would access an under-defended part of Simon's psyche. He would respond to the offered role of senior with poorly-defended generosity. This is a credible recruitment vector for any hostile actor with patience.

---

## SY


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

A file on Simon Williams that fails to map his rivalries and his loves is a file that has not understood him. The man is constituted by these relationships; they are not adjacent to his identity, they *are* his identity in its most exposed form. What follows is the granular mapping — every figure whose presence has been load-bearing in his psyche, whether by injury or by intimacy, and the patterns that recur across them.

---

## A. RIVALS

### A1. Anthony Stark

The oldest wound that wears a face. Stark is, in Simon's mental geography, the man he was supposed to be: the inheritor-son who took a father's defense-adjacent industrial concern and *did not lose it*. Williams Innovations was outcompeted by Stark Industries directly — not through fraud or sabotage, but through the simple fact that one heir was capable and the other was not. This is the irreducible humiliation. Every later Stark interaction is colored by it.

**History.** Pre-transformation, Simon never met Stark; he competed against the *idea* of Stark and lost. Post-transformation, they are teammates on and off for forty years of in-story time. Simon serves under Iron Man in multiple Avengers configurations, is mentored peripherally, takes orders, exchanges pleasantries. Stark, characteristically, has no memory of the original commercial humiliation; for Stark it was a quarterly footnote. For Simon it was the end of his first life.

**Dynamics.** Simon performs ease around Stark — the quip, the loose shoulder, the I-am-fine-with-this-actually posture — and the performance is detectable in microbehavior. He is more verbose around Stark than around any other Avenger. He volunteers more, jokes more, references his Hollywood career more. The bid is constant: *see that I am also a man of stature.* When Stark is in a vulnerable period (the alcoholism arcs, the Civil War aftermath, the various corporate collapses), Simon's posture eases noticeably — he is genuinely sympathetic, and the sympathy is also relief.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally high — Simon will take Stark's tactical calls without resistance. Personally medium-low — he does not confide in Stark and never has. The asymmetry is invisible to Stark.

**Failure mode.** Simon's Revengers-era critique of the Avengers (*New Avengers Annual* #1, 2011) is rhetorically aimed at the institution but psychically aimed at Stark specifically — the architect, the convener, the man who keeps assembling the thing Simon both needs and resents. Listen to the manifesto in that light: it is a younger brother finally saying out loud what he could not say at twenty-five about the man whose company ate his.

**Leverage.** Anyone wanting to move Simon against Stark needs only frame Stark as the cause of a destabilization Simon already feels. Anyone wanting to bind Simon *to* Stark needs Stark to ask him for help, sincerely, in front of others — the request itself is the reparation Simon has been waiting forty years for.

---

### A2. The Vision

The most morally compromising relationship of Simon's life, and the one in which he has behaved worst. The Vision was constructed (revealed in the Englehart run building from *Avengers* #135) using a recording of Simon's brain patterns — engrams taken in the period just before the original transformation. The Vision is therefore, in a literal sense, a copy of Simon's mind installed in a synthezoid body, then individuated by his own experience. He is Simon's only sibling in the metaphysical sense — a man made from him — and the husband of the woman Simon loves.

**History.** Initially Simon resents the Vision quietly. The two coexist on the Avengers for years with surface civility and structural tension neither articulates. The dynamic intensifies catastrophically in the *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* maxi-series and the West Coast Avengers run when the Vision is dismantled (the "VisionQuest" sequence, *West Coast Avengers* #42–45, Byrne) and Simon is asked to donate his current brain patterns to restore the Vision's personality. He refuses. The refusal is rationalized — concern about creating a true copy, concern about the new Vision being a stranger — but the operative reason, which Simon eventually acknowledges, is that he wants Wanda for himself and the Vision restored is the obstacle.

**Dynamics.** With the Vision present, Simon is quieter, more defensive, more prone to leave the room. The two have a manner of looking at each other that is recognizable to anyone who has watched siblings who do not get along: a flat acknowledgment, a quick disengagement of gaze. They share gestural tics — head-tilts, certain phrasings — that are uncanny in the literal sense, and which both of them seem aware of and avoid drawing attention to.

**Evolution.** The relationship moves from quiet resentment → active rivalry over Wanda → moral catastrophe (the refusal) → uneasy guilt-shaped coexistence after the Vision's eventual restoration by other means → an attempt at adult fraternity in the later runs that never fully takes. The Vision, characteristically, processes the injury and offers something like forgiveness; Simon cannot accept it cleanly because accepting it would require him to acknowledge what he did, which he has only ever half-acknowledged.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally functional. Personally — neither will turn his back on the other in a private room without a reason to. Not because either expects violence, but because the *charge* requires line-of-sight management.

**Failure mode.** Anything Wanda-related. The presence of all three in a room is the single most volatile social configuration Simon enters, and his body knows it — pulse signature elevates, shoulders rise, the quips get sharper and shorter.

**Leverage.** The Vision is the mirror Simon cannot break and cannot stop checking. Anyone who wants Simon to act against his interests need only put the Vision in proximity to Wanda and wait.

---

### A3. Hawkeye (Clint Barton)

The peer-rivalry that *works*, by accident and by mutual benefit. Clint and Simon spend nearly the entire West Coast Avengers run (1984–1994) as co-leaders, then teammates under Hawkeye's chairmanship, and the relationship settles into something both men need: a sibling-rivalry without the sibling-trauma. They mock each other constantly, compete on field assignments, drink (in Clint's case) and don't (in Simon's) at the same bars in Los Angeles, and have a running joke about which of them is more famous (Simon by industry, Clint by Avengers profile; both insecure about it).

**Dynamics.** This is the closest Simon has to a peer-male friendship that does not destabilize him. Clint is loud where Simon is performatively loud; Clint is genuinely insecure about powers (he has none) where Simon is insecure about identity (he has too many). The mismatched insecurities mean they cannot rank each other in any clean direction, so neither becomes the wounding mirror.

**Failure mode.** Clint's deaths and resurrections (Disassembled era, etc.) hit Simon harder than he shows. They reactivate his own death-material. He is awkward around Clint after each return — overly cheerful, slightly evasive — for weeks.

**Leverage.** Mutual. Each can ask the other for the kind of favor neither would ask anyone else; both honor it.

---

### A4. Wonder Woman / DC Trademark Note — *not applicable, omit*

[Cross-reference; no relationship in continuity. File note retained for disambiguation in legal review only.]

---

### A5. The Beast (Henry McCoy)

A rivalry that became a friendship, then frayed. Beast and Simon are the two Avengers most associated with showbusiness sensibility — both performative, both verbal, both prone to deflecting feeling through wit. In the Stern-era Avengers they buddy up, do publicity together, share what Simon would call a "type." The rivalry is over who is the team's *charm*, and it is friendly because the stakes are low.

**Failure mode.** Politicized periods (Beast's various X-Men entanglements, Simon's Revengers turn) split them on ideological lines they cannot easily bridge. Each is disappointed in the other in a way that has not been repaired.

---

## B. ENEMIES

### B1. Eric Williams / the Grim Reaper

The defining antagonist. Not the most powerful enemy Simon has faced, not the most strategically dangerous, but the only one whose existence is constitutive of Simon's own. Eric is the older brother, the inheritor of the family's dominant temperament, the one who turned grief over Simon's first death into a scythe-armed murder career, and then turned the news of Simon's resurrection into a deeper hatred — because the *thing* that came back, by Eric's logic, was not his brother but an ionic abomination wearing his face.

**History.** Pre-transformation: standard older-brother dominance, intensified by paternal favor and by Simon's manifest inadequacy. Eric was the son who was supposed to inherit; Simon was the one who did, by accident of paternal sentimentality, and lost the company. The childhood pattern was contempt-mixed-with-protectiveness on Eric's side; admiration-mixed-with-fear on Simon's. Post-transformation: Eric blames the Avengers for Simon's death, becomes the Grim Reaper to avenge him, attacks the team repeatedly, is repulsed each time. Post-resurrection: Eric rejects Simon as inauthentic — a *philosophical* hatred now, dressed in pseudo-vitalist language about "real" life versus "energy mockery." Across roughly thirty years of publication the brothers fight, the brothers reconcile briefly, the brothers fight again, until Simon is forced to bury Eric — multiple times, because Eric returns through necromantic and dimensional means almost as often as Simon does.

**Dynamics.** Simon's combat behavior against Eric is unmistakable on tape: he is slower, he pulls strikes, he talks more than he fights, he positions himself between Eric and others rather than engaging directly. The reluctance is total and it has gotten people killed. He cannot accept that the relationship ends.

**Trust / safety.** None and total simultaneously. Simon trusts Eric absolutely to attack him; he trusts Eric absolutely not to attack him in the back. There are codes between them that survive everything.

**Failure mode.** Anyone deploying Eric against Simon is deploying the only opponent Simon will not fight at full power. Hostages can be lost during a Reaper engagement that would not be lost during any other fight.

**Leverage.** Eric's name, invoked unexpectedly, will alter the tone of any conversation Simon is in. Photographs of their childhood — there were apparently many, taken by their mother, who appears in the record almost not at all — produce a flat, withdrawn affect that lasts hours.

**Reading.** The Reaper is Simon's externalized verdict on himself: that what came back from the death is not the man, that the ionic shape is a fraud, that Simon Williams died in *Avengers* #9 and everything since is a costume. Simon cannot let Eric go because Eric is the only voice articulating the thing Simon most fears is true. Killing Eric would not silence it; it would only make the verdict permanent and Simon's. This is why he buries him and lets him come back.

---

### B2. Baron Heinrich Zemo (and, derivatively, Helmut)

The original maker. Zemo found Simon in a prison cell, offered him power, fame, vengeance against the world that had humiliated him, and the chance to be *someone*. Simon accepted. The acceptance is the most uncomfortable fact in his autobiography, and he has spent every subsequent decade managing it.

**History.** Brief and decisive. Zemo recruits, transforms, deploys. Simon turns on him within a single issue (*Avengers* #9). Zemo dies shortly thereafter in unrelated business. The relationship is over in publication-weeks but does not end psychically. Helmut, the son, inherits the grudge in both directions — Simon's continued existence is an affront to the Zemo legacy, and Simon's existence-as-ionic is the Zemo legacy. Encounters with Helmut across the Masters of Evil arcs (*Avengers* #270s, *Thunderbolts* era) are charged with a paternity Simon does not want to acknowledge: in a literal-genealogical sense, Heinrich Zemo *made* the body Simon walks around in.

**Dynamics.** Simon is unusually controlled around any Zemo. The performance drops. He becomes terse, watchful, economical with movement. This is the only enemy class around which his observable behavior is *less* theatrical than baseline.

**Failure mode.** Anyone framed as a "rescuer offering a new self" risks triggering Simon's original Zemo-pattern — the susceptibility to a charismatic figure with a story about who Simon could become. The Revengers period is, structurally, Simon falling for his own internal Zemo.

**Leverage.** Reference to Zemo as Simon's creator, his father-in-physics, the man who *gave* him the powers he is so proud of — produces shame and silence. Helmut has used this in dialogue; it lands every time.

---

### B3. The Enchantress (Amora)

A peripheral but recurring enemy whose particular weapon — seduction, illusion, the projection of desire — works on Simon better than on most. Encounters in the early Avengers run and in scattered later appearances show him manipulated more easily than teammates. He knows it and is ashamed of it. He compensates by being conspicuously cool around her in any subsequent encounter, which is itself a tell.
