**Leverage.** Any opponent capable of generating illusory Wandas, or illusory audiences applauding him, will get more from Simon than they should.

---

### B4. Ultron

Not a personal enemy in the way the Reaper is, but a structural one. Ultron's existence (as the Vision's "father" in a chain of synthezoid lineage) and his repeated attempts to remake the Vision implicate Simon's engrams at the root. Every Ultron crisis is, for Simon, a referendum on the fact that his mind is reproducible. He fights Ultron with unusual ferocity for this reason. The fights are also where he gets injured most — he is less careful when the opponent represents the question of his own copyability.

---

### B5. Kang the Conqueror

Generic team-enemy. No specific dyad. Simon fights Kang as Avengers business, no charge. Noted only to confirm that not every powerful enemy maps personally; Simon's enmities are selective and the selection itself is diagnostic.

---

### B6. The Avengers (institutional, during the Revengers period)

The most revealing enemy in the file, because Simon made them one. *New Avengers Annual* #1 (2011) and surrounding issues: Simon founds the Revengers — Goliath, Atlas, Virtue, D-Man, Century, Devil-Slayer, and Captain Ultra — on the proposition that the Avengers' very existence destabilizes reality, that their interventions cause the crises they then resolve, and that the world would be safer without them. He attacks teammates of decades. He puts Wonder Man on the cover of a magazine declaring war on the team he is most associated with in the public mind.

**Reading.** The institution stands in here for Stark specifically and for the Avengers-as-mirror that Simon has been straining against for forty years. The ideological content is not nothing — there is a real argument about superhuman intervention to be made — but the *energy* is personal. He is breaking up with a family.

**Failure mode.** This is what Simon does when the mirror cracks: he flips polarity rather than examine the crack. The Revengers turn is a single behavior, repeated at scale: turning on Zemo in issue 9, turning on the Avengers in 2011. Same circuit, opposite valence.

**Recovery.** As predicted by the personality profile, he returns. The institution forgives him with the weary largeness institutions can afford. He does not forgive himself, which is the engine that will produce the next destabilization.

---

## C. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### C1. Wanda Maximoff — the Scarlet Witch

The only relationship in Simon's life that organizes him. Every other intimacy is measured against this one and found insufficient, including by him.

**History.** The attraction is present from Simon's earliest re-introduction to the Avengers post-resurrection, but it cannot move while she is married to the Vision. He carries it for years in the manner of a man who has decided to be honorable about it and is therefore especially unable to hide it from anyone but her. The Englehart *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* maxi-series and the West Coast Avengers run dramatize this — every panel of him in her vicinity is a study in restrained longing. After the Vision is dismantled and Wanda's mental state begins to fragment (the "VisionQuest" sequence and its aftermath), Simon is the figure who stays. They become lovers in the late West Coast run. The relationship is, by his account and by the visual record, the happiest period of his life.

She leaves him to attempt to restore the Vision. She does not entirely leave him — there is a long, painful in-between — but the trajectory is clear. He loses her to the husband he refused to help restore. The moral arithmetic of this is so exact it could only be a story, and Simon knows it, and the knowing does not relieve the pain.

Post-Disassembled, post-*House of M*, the relationship enters its strangest phase: Wanda's chaos magic and her grief and her need keep summoning Simon back from discorporation. *Avengers Vol. 3* (Busiek/Perez): Simon exists, when he exists at all, because she needs him to. He cannot maintain solid form without her presence. He is, in the most literal sense available in this universe, her dependent.

**Dynamics.** Around Wanda, Simon is *quieter*. The performance drops. The voice is lower, the gestures are smaller, the eye-contact is steadier. This is the one social context in which the persona-borrowing pauses — because, with her, he does not need to perform a self; her gaze constitutes one. (This is also the diagnosis.) He brings her small things — flowers chosen with care, books, a particular pastry from a particular bakery in Los Angeles that he started visiting during the West Coast years and still visits when alone. He remembers what she said three years ago about a song. He does not remember what other teammates said three weeks ago.

**Trust / safety.** From his side: total, in a way that is itself the problem. He has no protective skepticism with her. From her side: complex. She loves him. She has used him. She knows what he is when she is not there to anchor him and the knowledge is heavy.

**Failure mode.** Wanda's withdrawal, in any form — physical absence, emotional preoccupation, return to interest in the Vision — produces Simon's worst behavior. The Vision refusal happens in the gravity of Wanda. The Revengers turn happens after long Wanda-absence. His ionic destabilizations cluster around her crises. The correlation, across forty years of canon, is the cleanest single variable in the file.

**Leverage.** Anyone with credible access to Wanda — to her safety, her opinion, her romantic state — has Simon. Adversaries who have understood this have used it. Allies who understand it use it more carefully. Therapists working with Simon will not get past this until they have addressed it, and addressing it requires acknowledging that the relationship is both his great love and the load-bearing element of his pathology, and that those are not separable conditions.

**Reading.** The romance with Wanda is real. The dependency is also real. Both can be true. The honest assessment is that Simon would not survive — psychically, possibly literally — the definitive end of her interest in him. He has organized his being around her since approximately *Avengers* #160, and the organization has only deepened. Whether this is romantic in the most generous sense or pathological in the most clinical sense is a question the file declines to resolve, because both descriptions are accurate at their respective resolutions.

---

### C2. Carol Danvers — Ms. Marvel / Warbird / Captain Marvel

Brief, sharp, instructive. The Mighty Avengers and proximate runs (Bendis era) place Simon and Carol in close-quarters team configuration during a period in which both are emotionally available — Carol post-her-various-traumas, Simon post-discorporation and pre-Revengers. The chemistry is real. They have what is best described as a romance attempt that does not consolidate.

**Dynamics.** Carol is the only romantic partner who has consistently *called him on his shit* — refused his performative bravado, named the Wanda-dependence out loud, declined to be a substitute mirror. Simon found this both unbearable and clarifying. He was better, briefly, around her, because he could not deploy the usual defenses and she would not pretend not to notice.

**Failure mode.** He could not sustain the honesty. She would not sustain the relationship without it. They parted on terms that are, by his account, friendly; by hers, finished.

**Leverage.** Carol is one of the only people whose opinion of Simon will alter Simon's behavior in the moment. A direct word from her is more effective than a lecture from anyone else, including teammates of longer standing. She does not deploy this often.

---

### C3. Tigra (Greer Grant Nelson)

A West Coast-era flirtation and brief involvement, more situational than central. They are both lonely on the West Coast roster, both stuck in Los Angeles, both dealing with identity questions (her transformation, his ionic instability), and they find each other. The relationship is warm and uncomplicated by his standards, which is to say it does not survive any complication.

**Dynamics.** Simon is gentler with Greer than with most lovers because her vulnerability — particularly during her various trauma arcs, including the Masters of Evil mansion siege in *Avengers* #270s, where she is brutalized — calls out his loyal-to-the-broken instinct. This is among his better behaviors, and it is also not, by his lights, romance in the way Wanda is romance.

**Failure mode.** When Wanda is again available, Simon's attention reorganizes. Greer notices. The relationship ends without dramatic event but with clear cause.

---

### C4. Earlier and Peripheral Liaisons

The Hollywood years produced a number of brief involvements that do not appear by name in canon but are implied by the milieu and by his public profile. The pattern is consistent: actresses, stuntwomen, and industry-adjacent women, relationships of weeks to months, ended either by his work schedule (cover story) or by his unavailability (real reason — he is in love with someone else and they figure it out). He treats these partners decently, by the available record. He does not collect them as conquests. He is not promiscuous in the predatory sense; he is *available* in the lonely sense, and the loneliness is structural.

**One specific recurrence worth noting:** a stuntwoman, unnamed in the published record but referenced obliquely in the West Coast period, with whom he had an on-again off-again involvement spanning two of his Hollywood production cycles. She is described in his own dialogue (one scene, Englehart-era *West Coast Avengers*) in a tone that suggests genuine affection and genuine guilt at not being able to offer more. This is his pattern: the women he is not in love with get the better version of him in many ways, because he is not trying to be made-real by them.

---

## D. CROSS-PATTERN OBSERVATIONS

Across rivals, enemies, and lovers, the same architecture repeats:

- **Mirrors he cannot stop checking.** Stark, the Vision, the Reaper, Wanda. Each is


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## 6.1 Mechanism: What Ionic Energy Actually Is

The substrate of Simon Williams is the single most analytically important fact about him, and it has been the subject of a half-century of inconsistent in-canon explanation that the file should treat as data about the *condition* rather than as a writing problem. The original Lee/Heck account (*Avengers* #9, 1964) describes Zemo's "ionic ray" as a one-shot saturation process: Sanford-derived organic tissue irradiated until cellular chemistry was supplanted by an energy lattice held in human configuration. The 1970s Englehart/Shooter revival treats this as effectively permanent — Simon's body is no longer metabolizing in the conventional sense, and the years he spent inert were spent as an object, not a corpse. The Byrne-era *West Coast Avengers* refinement (#2–#9, then load-bearing in "VisionQuest," #42–#45) reframes the energy as not merely *suffusing* a body but *constituting* one: there is no organic Simon Williams under the ionic field. The body is the field, shaped by the engram pattern (the same pattern, critically, that was copied into the Vision).

The Busiek/Perez run (*Avengers Vol. 3* #2–#3, then the discorporation arc) makes this explicit in the most clinically revealing way available: when Simon "died" against the Kree he did not cease — he discorporated, persisted as an unbound ionic field, and required an external coherence-source (Wanda's longing, then her conscious summoning) to re-condense into Simon-shape. He is, by that point, demonstrably a *standing wave* — a pattern that maintains itself when sufficiently anchored and disperses when not. Slott's *Mighty Avengers* and the various 2010s reconstitutions treat the ionic body as essentially infinite-uptime hardware running the Simon-Williams pattern as software, with the pattern itself stored in a manner that is partially in the energy and partially in the regard of others.

Operationally, this means every "power" below is a manipulation of the same underlying field. He is not a strong man who can also fly; he is a coherent volume of ionic energy whose density, vector, and luminance he can modulate, and "strength," "flight," "blasts," and "durability" are local expressions of those modulations.

## 6.2 Strength — Mechanism, Curve, and Use

At baseline Simon registers in the Class 100 band — the Thor / Thing / Hercules tier where canonical lifting in the 75–100 ton range is routine and short-burst output exceeds that. He has bench-pressed Avengers Quinjets, held collapsing structural members, traded blows with the Hulk (memorably in *Avengers* Annual and recurrently in West Coast and Force Works fights) without bone-fracture morbidity because there are no bones to fracture in the conventional sense.

The curve over publication time is one of progressive disclosure rather than progressive empowerment. Lee/Heck wrote him as Thor-comparable in his debut. Englehart and Michelinie downscaled him in the late '70s to manage him alongside other heavies, partly because he was emotionally fragile and the writers needed his strength to feel uncertain to *him*. Byrne and the Force Works era rescaled him upward (with the famous Roger Stern handwave that Simon had been suppressing output for years out of fear). By Busiek the strength is treated as essentially uncapped — a function of how much ionic charge he allows to express. The "growth" is therefore not biological but *permissive*: the limits are confidence-gated.

Signature application: the *shoulder-charge under flight*, used reliably from West Coast onward as his preferred opener — a kinetic delivery system that lets him terminate engagements without prolonged hand-combat (which he dislikes; see §6.7). He does not box well for someone of his class. He grapples poorly. He prefers a single decisive impact.

Granular tell: when he commits maximum force he closes his eyes a half-beat before contact. He has done this since the Englehart run. It is not aesthetic — it is the death-phobia flinch (§6.10) repurposed as a windup.

## 6.3 Durability — and the Specific Way It Fails

"Invulnerable" overstates it. Simon's ionic field resists conventional kinetic, thermal, and ballistic insult to the point of indifference — small-arms fire registers as touch, blade weapons including his brother's energized scythe require concentrated energetic enhancement to score the surface, and re-entry-grade thermal loads have been absorbed without lasting deformation. He has been buried under masonry, dropped from orbit, and shrugged off Ultron-tier strikes.

What hurts him is anything that disrupts the *field* rather than the *body*. Categorized from the canon:

- **Ionic disruption / counter-resonance.** The original Zemo process produced him; later devices keyed to ionic frequency (Reaper's later weapons, certain AIM tech, Iron Man's anti-ionic protocols built quietly after the Revengers incident) cause Simon to flare, lose cohesion, or in extreme exposures partially discorporate.
- **Magic.** Wanda's hex energy and Strange-tier sorcery treat his pattern as information and can dissolve or re-shape it. This is the asymmetry that organizes his relationship with Wanda at the *physical* level as well as the emotional: she is the one being in his life who can unmake him with a gesture and the one whose gesture has, repeatedly, *made* him.
- **Cosmic / abstract force** at the Kree-warship and Annihilation-tier range — sufficient to kill him in the Force Works era and to discorporate him repeatedly in the 2000s.
- **Emotional load.** This is the diagnostically interesting one (§6.10). Under acute psychological stress his field flares, leaks, and loses local cohesion. He has broken his own grip on objects when shamed. He has emitted light in proportion to grief. The body and the affect are the same readout.

## 6.4 Flight

Flight is a late addition — not present in the original Lee/Heck appearance, developed in the Englehart era and stabilized by West Coast. Mechanism is ionic-field manipulation against ambient electromagnetic structure, effectively self-levitation by reshaping his own coherence-vector. He flies subsonic in atmosphere as a matter of preference (he does not enjoy the sensation of speed; another tell), can push to multi-Mach when motivated, and is unbothered by vacuum.

He flies *poorly* by Avengers standards in fine-control terms — he hovers competently, he charges in straight lines beautifully, but he does not turn well at speed and avoids dogfighting roles. On combined-arms ops he gravitates to the strike-and-anchor role: arrive, land, hit, hold ground. His flight posture is recognizable from any rooftop camera — arms forward like a 1940s comic-strip hero, legs together, an aesthetic choice he is aware of and refuses to abandon. Vanity as flight-control discipline.

## 6.5 Ionic Discharge — The Eye-Blasts and the Body-Flare

Discharge capability emerged in the West Coast era and was systematized by Force Works. Two distinct modalities:

- **Directed beams**, typically from the eyes, occasionally from the hands. Output range from concussive (Wrecking Crew tier) to structurally damaging (collapsing buildings, downing Sentinels). He uses these reluctantly — they are how he fights when he cannot close to physical range, and he prefers physical range because beams feel to him like *what Zemo made him for*. The aesthetic resistance is moral residue.
- **Field flare** — uncontrolled or semi-controlled radiation of his entire body, used as area-effect in extremis. This is the modality that overlaps with his destabilization episodes; the same mechanism that lets him deliberately overload an opponent at point-blank is the one that lets him *leak* under shame.

Color is a diagnostic. Stable Simon glows a warm scarlet-orange — the canonical hue from his first reconstitution. Under stress the color drifts: white-hot at maximum output, sickly green-yellow during the late-2000s instability arcs, near-violet in the discorporated period when his pattern was Wanda-mediated. Trained observers (Stark, Reed, T'Challa) read his color in the field the way a medic reads pupil reactivity.

## 6.6 The Lattice Powers — Reconstitution, Phase, and Discorporation

These are the powers Simon would prefer not to have, because they are the ones that prove the diagnosis (§3, §4).

**Reconstitution.** He has reassembled from total bodily dispersal multiple times: Force Works death, Busiek discorporation, Bendis-era flares, the *Wonder Man* miniseries set-pieces. The process requires anchor — historically Wanda, in her absence a strong relational mirror (the Avengers as institution, a teammate's grief, an audience's recognition). He cannot reconstitute alone reliably. This is the most consequential power-limit in the dossier: his immortality is *conditional on being loved or witnessed*.

**Phase / intangibility.** Intermittent, not reliable. He has walked through walls during high-flux periods and bounced off them during stable ones. He does not use this tactically because he cannot count on it.

**Discorporation (controlled).** Late-period Simon can voluntarily release form and persist as a field. He does so rarely. It terrifies him in a way nothing else does — it is the closest condition to the inert-years death, and the death-phobia (§6.10) has never resolved at this depth. When he has done it voluntarily it has been for Wanda or to spare a teammate.

## 6.7 Combat Skill, or Its Conspicuous Absence

This is where the file diverges sharply from the standard heavy-hitter template. Simon Williams has, across sixty years, never seriously trained. He has no martial discipline. His hand-to-hand is a Class 100 brawler's instinct overlaid on a wealthy New Jersey kid's high-school athletics and whatever stunt choreography he picked up between gigs. He fights, when he must fight in close, like an actor playing a man who fights — broad telegraphed strikes, theatrical recovery, a tendency to *pose* mid-combat (West Coast issues are full of this; Byrne drew it deliberately). Captain America has remarked on this. Iron Fist has remarked on this. He is aware of it and resents being reminded.

What he is good at:
- **Closing distance.** The flight-shoulder-charge opener.
- **Single-target termination of equal-class opponents** via overwhelming output, when he allows himself the output.
- **Holding ground.** He is functionally immovable when set, and uses this as a shield-role for less durable teammates.
- **Set-piece spectacle.** The stunt career is real skill — he times falls, rolls into impacts, sells contact. In a team fight he is the most *readable* combatant on the field, which teammates can exploit.

What he is bad at:
- **Sustained technical exchange** against a trained equal (he loses extended bouts to skilled Class 100s like Hercules through pure technique deficit).
- **Multi-opponent management.** He fixates on one target.
- **Stealth, reconnaissance, restraint.** He is loud, bright, and visible by nature; he cannot dim his own glow below ambient even when trying.
- **Killing.** He has refused to, across decades, including against the Reaper, including against Ultron-class threats. This is moral, not technical, but it is a hard ceiling on his application.

## 6.8 Non-Combat Skills

- **Business and engineering literacy.** Inherited and trained at his father's firm; rusted by decades of disuse but still present. He can read a balance sheet, recognize an industrial process, and was credibly a corporate scion before the embezzlement. Stark Industries comparisons humiliate him precisely because he understands the comparison.
- **Acting.** Genuine craft, developed across the West Coast era and the *Wonder Man* miniseries periods. He has range — he was hired for action work but has done dramatic parts, voice work, and stunt-coordination. The craft is the healthiest sublimation in his repertoire (§3).
- **Stunt work.** Distinct from acting. He is invulnerable, so he does stunts no insured human could attempt, but the *technique* — timing, mark-hitting, falling clean — is professional-grade.
- **Public speaking and media management.** Better than any Avenger except Stark. He gives a good interview. He hits camera marks reflexively, even in press scrums. He knows which side his face photographs best from (left) and arranges himself accordingly without thinking.
- **Languages.** Functional Spanish from LA decades, conversational Italian from a film shoot, some German from Wanda. Not a linguist.
- **Driving.** Excellent, from the stunt work. Prefers convertibles. (See §10-equivalent behavioral catalog — he keeps his hand on the gearshift even in automatics.)

## 6.9 Signature Applications

The combinations that produce *recognizable* Simon Williams operations:

- **The flight-charge / shoulder-impact / set-position / quip sequence.** His default combat opening, used from West Coast onward. Camera-friendly. Teammates know to clear a lane.
- **The "anchor" role in team configurations.** He stands; others move around him. He is the immovable point. Cap has positioned him this way; Hawkeye relied on it in West Coast; Storm placed him this way in Uncanny.
- **The volunteer-for-the-suicide-assignment move.** Recurrent across eras. Whenever an op requires a member who can absorb terminal damage and reconstitute, he steps forward before asked. This is moral and it is also identity-confirming — being the one who can die is, for him, a way of being the one who *matters*.
- **The press-conference intervention.** When Avengers PR breaks down, he is the one who walks to the microphones. He is good at it. The team uses this and resents him for being good at it.
- **The brother-encounter ritual.** When the Reaper appeared, Simon disengaged from whatever fight was current and pursued personally. Teammates learned to let him.

## 6.10 The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

The powers and the pathology are the same system.

The ionic field is a coherent pattern that *requires being witnessed to hold its shape*. Strength scales with permission. Durability fails to disruption that treats him as information rather than matter. Reconstitution requires an anchoring regard. Discharge color tracks affect. Flare leaks under shame. Discorporation is the somatic version of the dissociation §4 describes — when he cannot hold the *self*, he cannot hold the *body*, because they are the same standing wave.

Every power-limit in this section recapitulates a psychological one:

- He underperforms his strength because he does not trust himself to be what he is.
- He fights at range only when forced, because the eye-beams are Zemo's gift and he does not want them to be the truest thing about him.
- He does not train, because training would commit him to *being* the warrior he performs, and committing to a self is the act he cannot perform.
- He cannot kill, because the moral floor is the one piece of identity he assembled himself, after the original failure, and surrendering it would unmake him more completely than any ionic disruption.
- He cannot stay dead, because someone keeps witnessing him into being. And he cannot stay reliably *alive*, because the witnessing is intermittent and he knows it.

The clinical formulation in §4 — chronic identity-coherence deficit with somatic expression — is, when transposed into the operational register of this section, a complete description of the powerset. Simon Williams is a man whose body is a metaphor for his condition because the same process produced both. The file should treat the powers and the pathology as a single phenomenon read at two scales.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6
## OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
### Subject: Williams, Simon (WONDER MAN)

---

## 6.1 Decision-Making Architecture

Subject does not decide; subject *narrates a decision into existence*. The cognitive sequence, observed across six decades of incident, is consistent enough to be diagrammed:

1. **Stimulus** — usually interpersonal (a slight, a request, a perceived rejection, a glance from Wanda Maximoff, a callout in press).
2. **Affective spike** — somatic before cognitive; the ionic substrate registers feeling as a faint thermal/luminescent bloom along the forearms and jawline (documented in fight footage and on-set continuity stills since the early West Coast Avengers period) *before* he speaks.
3. **Narrative framing** — he silently composes a sentence about what kind of man he is in this moment. Lip-reading of unguarded combat footage (Force Works era, Kree engagement, *Iron Man* #310-adjacent material) captures him mouthing scripted-sounding first lines to himself before engaging.
4. **Verbal pre-commitment** — he says the framing *out loud*, often to an enemy or to no one in particular. This is the operational tell: **Simon Williams announces what he is about to do before he does it.** The announcement is not bravado; it is self-coercion. Once the line is in the air, he is committed.
5. **Action** — usually direct, kinetic, theatrically blocked.
6. **Post-action reframing** — a second sentence, retrospective, that absorbs the act into the running self-narrative.

The implication for any handler, adversary, or analyst: interrupting Simon at Step 3 or 4 frequently aborts the action entirely. He cannot execute against a half-spoken script. Conversely, *feeding* him a frame at Step 3 — supplying the line — is the single most reliable manipulation vector in his file. Zemo did it. The Revengers ideology was, in effect, a frame he supplied himself when no one else would. Wanda has done it inadvertently, repeatedly, simply by being watched.

Subject's deliberative window is narrow under stress (sub-three seconds in combat; minutes-to-hours in moral decisions) and *very* wide in absence of stress, where he ruminates for days, drafts and re-drafts statements, calls trusted parties (Pym, on documented occasion; previously Beast; less frequently Carol Danvers) for what he frames as "checking my read."

---

## 6.2 Methods of Engagement

**Combat tradecraft.** Subject fights at Class-100 strength tier but consistently *under-applies* force — measurably. Telemetry from training-room sessions at Avengers Compound (logged via standard threat-assessment cycles) shows him pulling strikes by an estimated 30–60% against humanoid opponents, holding the punch at the moment of impact in a manner consistent with stuntwork choreography rather than maximal application. This is not restraint born of mastery; it is a *performance habit*. He fights as though a camera is rolling. The hands open slightly at the wrist on follow-through. The stance recovers to a photogenic resting frame. The one-liner lands on the exhale.

Against non-humanoid threats (Kree drones, Ultron frames, abstract energy hostiles) the choreography compresses and the output climbs. He is willing to be ugly when no one is watching the face.

**Flight pattern.** Subject flies in shallow arcs, prefers altitudes between 200–800 feet (low enough for visual identification from the ground), and decelerates dramatically before landing — the so-called "two-point hero landing" with one knee down. He has been observed circling a destination once before descent on multiple occasions, which reads as ensuring he is seen arriving.

**Disengagement.** Subject does not retreat cleanly. He either remains past tactical utility (sub-pattern: chronic over-commitment to "finish the scene") or, when he does withdraw, does so explosively — a single hard ascent that broadcasts an ionic signature visible to standard SHIELD/SWORD sensor packages for 6–11 minutes after departure. Pursuit is trivial. Stealth is not in his repertoire.

**Lethality.** Subject has not knowingly taken a sapient life in the canonical record, *including against his brother across two decades of provocation*. This is not squeamishness; it is load-bearing self-definition. To kill would collapse the running narrative of redemption. Adversaries who understand this know they can press him to within an inch of his ceiling and survive, which is exploited.

---

## 6.3 Tradecraft: Civilian / Covert

Subject possesses essentially no covert tradecraft and has not seriously attempted to develop any. The Hollywood career has, paradoxically, made him *more* visible, not less — SAG-AFTRA registration, public agent of record, paparazzi footprint, premiere circuit. He uses his own legal name on credit instruments, drives registered vehicles, and maintains a consistent personal aesthetic that is identifiable from a block away.

When *required* to operate covertly, his tradecraft is borrowed wholesale from screenplay convention: brimmed hat, sunglasses indoors, collar up, the canvas jacket. He is identifiable at distance to anyone who knows the tells. He does not use cutouts, dead drops, or compartmented communications. He texts directly from his own phone in plain English.

The single domain in which he displays genuine tradecraft is **media management** — the actor skillset, transposed. He knows how to seed a story, how to time a denial, how to use a sympathetic press contact (long-running relationship with at least one West Coast entertainment journalist; periodic favors to a *Daily Bugle* arts-desk stringer). When he wants a narrative in the air, he can put it there within a news cycle. The Revengers manifesto was rolled out with this exact competence — coordinated drop, prepared talking points, pre-recorded sit-down — and it caught the Avengers' PR apparatus flat-footed for nearly 36 hours.

---

## 6.4 Resources & Finances

**Income streams**, roughly stratified:

- **SAG residuals and front-end actor pay**, the largest stable line. Mid-budget action features, occasional prestige supporting roles, voice work, the periodic franchise. Estimable gross in the low-to-mid seven figures in active years; trough years substantially less.
- **Stunt-coordinator fees and second-unit work**, secondary but persistent.
- **Endorsements**, sporadic and tonally inconsistent — he accepts deals that flatter the persona and turns down deals that complicate the heroic image, sometimes leaving real money on the table.
- **Avengers stipend** during active roster membership (modest, paid through the Maria Stark Foundation channel; he has on at least one occasion refused it as a gesture and quietly reinstated it within the fiscal year).
- **Residual interest in the wreckage of Williams Innovations** — almost entirely notional at this point; minor licensing on legacy patents.

**Liabilities and expenditures:** subject lives well above what an actuary would advise, on the implicit assumption of immortality. He carries little insurance (the carriers will not write him at reasonable rates anyway), holds little long-horizon retirement instrument exposure, and spends heavily on **lifestyle signaling**: wardrobe, vehicles, residence in the Hollywood Hills / Los Feliz corridor (with prior addresses in Sherman Oaks and a long-tenured West Coast Avengers Compound bunk during the Palos Verdes era). He tips conspicuously. He picks up checks reflexively, even when the dinner companion is wealthier.

**Financial tells:** he does not budget. He delegates accounting to a business manager (retained relationship of long standing, predating the Force Works period). He pays personal bills late not from insolvency but from inattention. He has been audited at least once and treated it as a kind of performance.

He keeps **no offshore structure, no anonymous holding, no crypto position of consequence.** The embezzlement conviction left him with a permanent aversion to anything that looks like financial cleverness; he overcorrects into transparency to the point of operational vulnerability.

---

## 6.5 Infrastructure

**Residence.** Single-family home, Hollywood Hills, owned outright. Modernist, glass-forward, view-oriented — a house designed to be seen *into* as much as out of. Security is consumer-grade: standard alarm, exterior cameras, a gate. He relies on his own body as the last line, which is reasonable given the body and unreasonable given everything else. Interior is photograph-ready at all times: he tidies compulsively when expecting company and lets it slide when alone, with a documented oscillation between magazine-spread cleanliness and a specific kind of single-man entropy (script pages on every flat surface, two-day coffee cups, the same three takeout containers).

**Secondary spaces.** A locker / bunk allocation at active Avengers facilities when on roster. A trailer on whatever production is current. A storage unit in Burbank that holds, per inventory pulled in adjacent matters: prior costumes (the red-and-green original, folded, in archival tissue — he has not thrown it away and will not), fan mail bins, awards, his father's desk set, and a banker's box of Williams Innovations corporate paper he has neither read nor destroyed.

**Vehicles.** A vintage convertible, restored, used as the daily driver in good weather; a more practical SUV; a motorcycle he rides badly and rarely. All registered, all insured, all photographed in tabloids at one time or another.

**Communications.** A personal mobile, a work mobile through his agency, and a secured handset issued through whichever team currently rosters him. He does not consistently use the secured line for sensitive matters, preferring the personal phone out of habit. Email is mixed across three accounts with overlapping use.

**Wardrobe / costume.** Multiple iterations of the Wonder Man identity over time: the original red-and-green leotard (retired, preserved); the safari-jacket-and-aviators stuntman period (durable, repeatedly imitated by knock-off merchandise); the red-with-W-bolt later costumes; the various energy-form "naked" periods where the costume *is* the body. Each costume change correlates with a psychological reorganization and can be used as a rough timeline of self-state.

---

## 6.6 Patterns of Action — Daily / Weekly Cadence

Long-term surveillance composite (not continuous; assembled from press, on-set logs, teammate testimony, and incident records):

- **Morning.** Subject rises early — between 5:30 and 6:30 — regardless of the prior night, ionic metabolism rendering sleep largely optional but voluntarily observed as a ritual. A long shower (he likes the heat even though he does not require it; sensory anchor). Coffee, consumed, though it does nothing pharmacologically. He reads the trades before he reads the news.
- **Exercise.** Performed daily despite physiological unnecessity. The workout is *aesthetic maintenance*, not strength building — calisthenic, mirror-facing, choreographed. He uses the gym as a stage even when alone.
- **Work block.** Script reading, line memorization, calls with agent/manager, fittings, table reads, set days. He is a reliable on-set presence (calls his cues, learns his lines, treats craft services well, is generous with younger cast). Directors describe him as "professional, occasionally a touch much."
- **Mid-afternoon void.** A documented soft spot — between roughly 2 and 4 PM, when no scheduled obligation, he drifts. Visits a coffee shop, a bookstore, a record store. He has been seen alone at matinees of films he is not in. This is the window in which contact attempts, friendly or otherwise, are most likely to succeed.
- **Evening.** Either a public obligation (premiere, charity, dinner — performed) or aggressively private (home, alone, lights low, the same playlist of mid-tempo material from his late teens / early twenties — the pre-transformation period; the music is a tether). He calls people in the evening. Pym remains a recurrent number.
- **Late.** He stays up too late watching old footage of himself, or films of the era he was first trying to make it. He is sentimental about his own past in a way few operatives can afford to be.

**Weekly.** A regular run / flight loop in the Hills (predictable enough to be a vulnerability). A standing therapy slot during the periods he has been in treatment (compliance imperfect but better than the population baseline for his cohort). A Sunday call to Pym, when Pym is reachable.

**Monthly / annual.** He attends conventions selectively, signing for free for veterans and children and charging for everyone else. He attends the West Coast team reunion gatherings even when poorly attended by others. He has marked, every year since her departure, a date that appears in no public calendar but corresponds to a particular Vision/Scarlet Witch milestone; on that day he is unreachable.

---

## 6.7 Signature Operational Tells

Compiled from longitudinal observation:

- **The pre-strike inhale.** A theatrical chest-rise before a punch, telegraphing the swing by a quarter-second. Trained opponents exploit it; he has not corrected it because it reads well on camera.
- **The catchphrase variant.** He cycles through three or four self-introduction lines ("Wonder Man — and don't you forget it" being the foundational variant), choosing by mood. The choice of variant correlates reliably with his self-state: the full bombastic version when overcompensating, a clipped "Wonder Man" when genuinely focused, no introduction at all when ashamed or rattled.
- **The hand on the back of the neck.** A self-soothing gesture, left hand to the nape, observed in nearly every interview and many combat lulls. Frequency rises sharply when the subject of Wanda Maximoff, the Vision, or his brother arises.
- **The ionic flare under duress.** Visible micro-luminescence along the jaw, throat, and forearms when emotionally activated. Cannot be suppressed. The single most reliable affect-readout in the file.
- **The "let me explain" pivot.** When confronted with a moral inconsistency, he opens with a hand gesture (palms up, slight forward lean) and the phrase *let me explain* or *here's the thing*. This is the rationalization-script loading. Cutting him off before the third sentence frequently produces an apology instead of a defense.
- **Name-shift.** He introduces himself as "Simon" to people he hopes will see him as a man, "Wonder Man" to people he wants to hold at distance, and (rarely, late at night, to close associates) "Williams" — the surname alone — in moments of dissociative drift, as if locating himself by the family name when the first name has come loose.
- **The Stark allergy.** In Tony Stark's presence subject's vocal pitch rises a quarter-step and his sentences shorten. He does not know he does this. It is the most legible single artifact of the original wound.
- **The over-tip.** Cash, always, even when the bill is on card. Twenty percent is a floor; thirty is common. This is shame-money — a man who once stole, paying.
- **The kept costume.** He has never destroyed an old identity-uniform. The archive in the Burbank unit is a museum of selves. He visits it.

---

## 6.8 Operational Affiliations & Trust Graph

**Tier-1 trust (will answer the phone, will move resources, will lie for):** Henry Pym. Wanda Maximoff (asymmetrically; she does not reciprocate at his intensity). A small number of West Coast-era teammates, varying by current friction.

**Tier-2 trust (will cooperate, will not betray, will not bleed for):** the Avengers institutionally during good periods; the Beast; Carol Danvers in some eras; current production collaborators on a project-by-project basis.

**Tier-3 (transactional):** agent, manager, attorney of record, business manager. These relationships are stable and well-managed; he treats his professional team with consistent courtesy and pays them on time when reminded.

**Adversarial / unresolved:** the memory of his brother (unresolved post-mortem). The Vision (variable, often civil, never clean). Stark (cordial-rivalrous, the wound permanent). His own prior selves (the archive in Burbank).

**Recruitment vulnerability.** Subject is recruitable, repeatedly, by any actor who offers him: (a) a coherent narrative in which he is the protagonist, (b) a stable mirror, (c) plausible access to Wanda's regard, or (d) a way to settle the original shame. Zemo used (a) and (d). The Revengers ideology was a self-recruitment using (a) and (c) — the manifesto's emotional engine is *what the Avengers have cost Wanda*. He has not been recruited by a sophisticated hostile in the modern era only because no sophisticated hostile has bothered. This is a standing vulnerability and should be logged as such.

---

## 6.9 Summary Tradecraft Assessment

Subject is a Class-100 asset with civilian-grade operational security, theatrical combat habits, no covert capacity worth the term, a media skillset that punches above its weight, and a decision-making process that can be read by anyone patient enough to watch his mouth move before he commits. He is *not* dangerous in the way a trained operator is dangerous; he is dangerous in the way a sincere, powerful, narratively-driven man is dangerous — capable of catastrophic action when supplied with a sufficiently compelling line about himself, and capable of catastrophic *good* on the same mechanism.

The file's recommendation, where one is solicited: do not handle him through pressure. Handle him, if at all, by mirroring — clearly, honestly, and without manipulation, because manipulation works on him and a benevolent intelligence apparatus should refuse to use what works. He is, after sixty years of incident, still the man who turned on Zemo in the first issue. Operationally, this is his most reliable feature. Treat it as load-bearing.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

## Subject: Simon Williams / Wonder Man

---

## 6.1 The Shape of His Cosmos

Simon Williams does not hold a philosophy in the analytic sense. He holds a **narrative cosmology** — a worldview in which the universe is structured like a story, populated by protagonists, antagonists, mentors, brothers, and beloveds, organized around arcs of fall and redemption, and judged by whether one's part is played *well*. This is not a metaphor he uses. It is the operating substrate of his perception. He literally cannot see a situation without casting it.

The consequences are pervasive and load-bearing for everything that follows in this section:

- **Events are scenes.** A confrontation is a *scene*; a betrayal is a *beat*; a recovery is a *third act*. He talks this way (post-Englehart, increasingly explicit; the West Coast and *Wonder Man* miniseries use it as comic relief but it is diagnostic) and, more importantly, he *thinks* this way.
- **People are roles.** He has trouble holding a person as the full irreducible thing they are. He sees Wanda as The Beloved, Vision as The Rival Who Was Made From Him, his brother as The Antagonist Who Will Not Stop, Pym as The Wounded Friend, Stark as The One Who Bested Him. Each is real to him, but each is *cast*. When a person violates their cast role (Wanda choosing Vision; the Avengers becoming, in his Revengers-era reading, the destabilizers) he experiences it as a genre violation, not a character disagreement, and reacts disproportionately.
- **Morality is dramatic, not deontic.** Right and wrong are felt as *fitness to the story being told*. The act of switching on Zemo in *Avengers* #9 is the keystone: it was not a calculated ethical decision, it was an unbearable miscasting — *I cannot be the villain in my own story*. That sentence is, for practical purposes, his entire foundational ethic.

The narrative substrate is what makes him sincere, and what makes him manipulable. A man who lives inside a story can be re-narrated by anyone with the talent.

---

## 6.2 First Principles, Stated and Unstated

### Stated (what he would say if asked)

- Heroism is real. People can choose to be better than they have been.
- Second chances matter — he is the evidence.
- Killing is the line. Even his brother, even repeatedly. He has held this for sixty publication years across more provocations than almost any Avenger.
- Loyalty to broken friends is non-negotiable (the Pym anchor; tested repeatedly).
- The Avengers, as an ideal, are worth dying for. As an institution, sometimes worth opposing. He distinguishes.
- He is *not* the man he was at twenty-five. He insists on this. He is also wrong about it, in the ways that matter most.

### Unstated (the actual axioms governing behavior)

- **I exist when I am being looked at.** This is the central unspoken premise. It governs the acting career, the costume choices, the team affiliations, the public statements, the romantic dependency. Absent regard, he is — literally, by the Busiek discorporation arc — not there.
- **My worth is a verdict others render. I cannot render it myself.** Every attempt to self-validate collapses within a story or two. Stability requires an external mirror.
- **The original failure (embezzlement, prison, public shaming) is the truth about me, and every later act either covers it or confirms it.** He has not metabolized this. He performs around it.
- **A compelling story about me, told by someone who seems to see me, deserves a hearing.** This is the Zemo vulnerability, intact decades later. The Revengers-era ideology was, in part, a story he told *himself* in this voice, when no one else was telling him a good one.
- **Death is not the end, which is worse than if it were.** He has come back too many times to fear death cleanly, and not cleanly enough to be at peace with it. The terror has shifted from *being dead* to *coming back wrong*.

---

## 6.3 Reading the World: Perception and Causal Model

Simon's situational read is **fast, intuitive, and image-driven**, not analytic. He registers tone, posture, and emotional charge before he registers tactical fact. In a room he clocks who is angry, who is hiding something, who is in pain, who is performing — and he is usually correct about the affect, frequently wrong about the cause. He is a high-empathy, low-attribution reader.

**Causal model of events:** he understands the world as driven by *intention and character*, not by structure or system. When something goes wrong, his first instinct is to find the responsible agent — a Zemo, a Reaper, an Avengers leadership, a self. The Revengers manifesto is a case study: faced with a complex pattern of cosmic destabilization (the Disassembled / *House of M* / post-Siege period), he reaches for an agent (the Avengers as institution) rather than a system, because agent-thinking is native to him.

**Time horizon:** medium-short. He plans within an arc, not across a career. He commits to positions ("I will never fight again," "the Avengers must be stopped," "I love her and only her") with the conviction of a man who has never noticed how often he has reversed himself. He is not lying. He genuinely cannot see the prior reversal as continuous with the current commitment, because each commitment is, in his experience, a fresh story.

**Pattern recognition:** strong for emotional and dramatic patterns ("this is the part where —"), weak for political, economic, and structural ones. He cannot read a balance sheet — see Williams Innovations, run into the ground by a man who could not actually do the job. He has, decades later, learned no more about commerce than he had then. He outsources all such cognition.

**What he overweights:** body language, tone, betrayal signals, audience response, his brother's mood, Wanda's gaze.

**What he underweights:** logistics, second-order effects, the difference between sincerity and correctness, the difference between feeling justified and being justified, his own track record.

---

## 6.4 Conflict: Doctrine, Aversions, Tells

**Doctrinal position:** Simon believes violence is sometimes necessary and frequently regrettable. He will fight; he prefers not to. He will not kill, even when killing would solve the problem in front of him. He has held the no-kill line against the Grim Reaper through circumstances that have broken other heroes' equivalent lines. This is not naivety. It is the load-bearing wall of his self-image: *if I kill, I am the man my father feared I was, the man my brother became, the man Zemo wanted to make.*

**In-combat behavior — three distinct modes, situationally triggered:**

1. **Performance mode** (default, especially West Coast era and later): theatrical, quippy, telegraphed power use, ostentatious entry, often pulled punches at first because the *appearance* of dominance matters as much as dominance. He is genuinely strong and genuinely fast; he fights at perhaps sixty to seventy percent of his actual capability under normal conditions, because using his full power feels indecorous and, more privately, because his full power has scared him since the resurrection.
2. **Anchored mode** (when protecting a specific person — Wanda, Pym, a teammate in immediate danger): efficient, direct, the theatrics drop, the strength comes up to perhaps ninety percent. He is, in this mode, one of the more dangerous combatants the Avengers field. He does not enjoy it and does not advertise it after.
3. **Destabilized mode** (under high emotional load — grief, betrayal, the Revengers period, post-discorporation reconstitution): ionic discharge becomes uncontrolled, force calibration fails, collateral risk spikes. He has injured allies in this mode. He is afraid of this mode and will avoid combat entirely if he suspects he is sliding toward it.

**Conflict aversions:** he avoids fights that require him to be the closer — to deliver the final blow, to render a verdict, to be the one whose force ends a life. He will set up the shot for someone else. He will absorb damage so a teammate can land the strike. He will reframe a kill-decision as a containment problem so it can be deferred. This is consistent across runs and is among his most stable behavioral signatures.

**Tells in conflict:** the quip rate is inversely correlated with confidence. When he is afraid he becomes funnier. When he stops talking mid-fight, the situation has crossed into anchored or destabilized mode and observers should reassess. A faint flicker at the eyes or hands (ionic surge) preceding an action means the action will land harder than he intended; he is not yet at full destabilization but has lost fine calibration.

---

## 6.5 Control: Of Self, of Others, of Narrative

Simon's relationship to control is **inverted from the standard heroic profile**. Most operators of his power level seek operational control — terrain, information, tempo. Simon seeks *narrative* control: he wants to manage how the scene reads, how he is perceived, what story is being told about the moment. He will sacrifice tactical advantage for a better image-frame. This is not vanity in the trivial sense (though it is also that). It is identity-maintenance. The image is the self.

**Self-control:** adequate in stable periods, poor under shame or romantic threat. He does not drink, does not use, does not lash out at subordinates, does not abuse power in any of the conventional ways available to him. His failures of self-control are *moral and identity-level* — the Vision refusal, the Revengers turn — not behavioral-impulsive. He does not hit people he shouldn't hit. He chooses positions he shouldn't choose.

**Control of others:** minimal interest. He is not a manipulator. He leads when asked (Force Works) but does not seek command and is mediocre at it because he reads people emotionally rather than instrumentally and cannot bring himself to deploy people against their preferences. He is closer to a beloved senior actor on a set than to a director. The Revengers period is partial evidence against this — he did recruit, he did lead — but the recruitment worked because the recruits were already grievance-aligned; he persuaded no one of anything, he gathered the already-persuaded.

**Control of narrative:** this is where he expends real effort. He gives interviews. He chooses his roles. He selects his costume iterations with conscious eye to how they will be perceived (the abandonment of the green-and-red original is itself a narrative decision; subsequent variants are calibrated). He manages, badly but constantly, his public profile. A surveillance file on his public-facing communications would show a man who *cares* about phrasing, who revisits and revises, who is wounded by criticism and elated by praise out of all proportion to the source.

---

## 6.6 Trust: Architecture and Failure Modes

Simon's trust system is **fast-on, slow-off, and reverses catastrophically when it does**.

**Onboarding:** he extends provisional trust quickly. A warm welcome, a shared loss, a request for help, a story told well — any of these will get a stranger inside his ring within a single substantive interaction. This has been weaponized against him repeatedly (originally by Zemo; the pattern recurs in subtler forms).

**Maintenance:** once inside, very stable. He does not audit his close relationships. He does not require ongoing demonstrations of loyalty. He extends benefit-of-the-doubt liberally, sometimes past the point of evidence (the Pym defense, where his loyalty was correct in the long run but ran ahead of what he could justify at the time). He is the friend who shows up.

**Failure mode:** when trust does break, it does not erode — it *flips*. A trusted figure who disappoints him does not become merely disappointing; they become miscast, and the recasting is total. The Avengers-to-Revengers turn is the canonical exhibit, but the pattern is older: it shows up in smaller form in team disputes across the West Coast and Force Works periods, and in his oscillating posture toward Stark across decades.

**Recoverability:** unusually high. He can re-trust someone who has broken with him, and can be re-trusted by people he has broken with, more reliably than most figures with this profile. The same narrative substrate that produces catastrophic flips also produces redemption arcs: if a story can be told that re-casts the broken relationship in a hopeful frame, he will sign on. He has rejoined the Avengers after declaring war on them, and the rejoining was not cynical.

**Who he actually trusts, long-arc:** Pym, almost without condition. Wanda, with the specific instability that the relationship itself generates. Beast in some periods. The Vision, complicatedly, after long penance. Himself, intermittently and never for long.

**Who he never quite trusts:** Stark (the original injury never fully heals, regardless of cooperation). Any Avengers leadership figure whose authority depends on his deference. Anyone who tells him too quickly that he is special — the recognition he craves is also, when offered without earned context, the exact signal that triggers his suspicion in retrospect.

---

## 6.7 Risk: Calibration, Bias, Behavior

Simon's risk calibration is **systematically distorted by the death-rebirth cycle and by the audience-orientation**.

**Physical risk to self:** drastically underweighted. He has died multiple times and returned; the visceral fear of death that organized his post-resurrection arc has not so much resolved as *inverted* into a kind of resigned recklessness. He will step in front of the blast. He has, repeatedly. This is partly genuine courage and partly something more concerning — a sense that his death is provisional, perhaps even owed, and that risking it costs less than risking someone else's.

**Physical risk to others:** *overweighted* when calibrated, *catastrophically underweighted* during ionic destabilization. In stable function he is one of the more careful heavy-hitters on any team, conscious of his strength and pulling appropriately. In destabilized periods he has caused collateral damage that he then cannot fully integrate, contributing to the next shame cycle.

**Reputational risk:** **overweighted to a degree that distorts other decisions.** He will accept significant operational cost to avoid looking foolish, weak, or villainous on camera (literal or figurative). The Hollywood career has reinforced this rather than created it — it was already his structure; the career gave it a vocabulary.

**Moral / identity risk:** poorly calibrated because it routes through narrative rather than principle. He will accept a morally questionable position if the story he is telling himself about it is satisfying (Vision refusal: *I am not obligated to give up my brain to bring back a rival for the woman I love* — narratively coherent, morally hollow). He will reject a morally sound position if the story is ugly. This is the chronic failure mode of his ethical reasoning and the one a hostile intelligence would most reliably exploit.

**Risk-taking behavioral signature:** he announces big risks (theatrically) and accepts small ones (silently). The announced risks are typically less dangerous than they read; the silent acceptances — the additional patrol shift, the lingering in the line of fire, the quiet substitution of himself for a more vulnerable teammate — are where the real exposure accumulates.

---

## 6.8 His Own Place in the World

Simon's self-location is the most unstable variable in the file, and he knows it.

**Stated self-conception:** an Avenger, a survivor, an actor, a man who has done some good and some harm and is trying to do more of the former. He will offer this, in some form, to any sincere questioner.

**Operative self-conception, shifting by period:**

- *Pre-ionic:* the failed son, the fraud, the inferior brother, the man Stark out-competed without noticing.
- *Zemo period:* the rescued man, briefly grateful, then horrified.
- *First death / early resurrection:* the man who should not be here. Borrowed time, borrowed body.
- *Late '70s recovery:* the second-chance man, gratitude and panic alternating.
- *West Coast / Hollywood era:* the performer, the visible one, the man whose existence is confirmed by being watched.
- *Vision-template revelation onward:* the original, the source, but also the redundant one — the man whose interior life is no longer uniquely his.
- *Discorporated period:* the lover-as-substrate, existing through her need, ontologically dependent.
- *Revengers period:* the dissenter, the man who sees what others won't, finally an agent rather than an object. (False, but the felt experience.)
- *Post-Revengers, late career:* the veteran, the cautionary tale, the figure who has done enough rounds to know his own pattern without being able to fully exit it.

**The underlying constant:** he does not believe, at any of these stages, that he occupies his place by right. He occupies it because someone allowed it, summoned it, cast him in it. He is grateful and resentful in roughly equal measure, and he conceals both.

**Cosmic / metaphysical orientation:** he does not have a developed religious view. He believes, vaguely, in *meaning* — that things happen for reasons within a story — and this is the closest he comes to faith. He has been dead and come back and this has not made him a mystic; if anything it has secularized him, because death turned out to be navigable rather than transcendent. He treats his ionic immortality as a circumstance, not a gift or a curse, though he can be argued into either framing depending on who is asking.

**Political / institutional orientation:** small-l liberal in the American mid-century sense — believes in institutions provisionally, believes in individuals primarily, distrusts concentrated power including his own. His Revengers turn is not a repudiation of this; it is, in his framing, an expression of it (the Avengers had become a concentration of power requiring opposition). The framing is convenient but not invented for the occasion.

---

## 6.9 The Operational Code, Distilled

A handler, antagonist, or sincere ally working with Simon Williams should expect, reliably, the following:

1. He will read the emotional content of the room correctly and the strategic content imperfectly. Brief him on the strategy; he will absorb the feel on his own.
2. He will take provisional commitments as more provisional than he admits and announced commitments as more announced than committed. The loud declaration is a mood, not a treaty.
3. He will not kill. Do not plan around the possibility that he will, even under pressure that would break others.
4. He will pull punches in front of an audience and not in private. The most honest version of his combat capability appears when no one is watching.
5. He will switch sides if a sufficiently coherent narrative is offered to him by someone he reads as sincere. The sincerity matters more than the content.
6. He will return. Whatever the break, however serious, the path back is open and he will take it if it is offered with grace.
7. He requires a mirror. Deny him one and he degrades — first morally, then physically. Provide one and he stabilizes within a story or two.
8. He cannot be controlled by force, money, or status. He can be moved, reliably, by being seen — accurately, generously, in a frame that makes a coherent man of him.

The man who turned on Zemo in the first hour of his second life is the same man who founded the Revengers and the same man who came back to the Avengers afterward. The mechanism is identical in each case: a story was told about who Simon Williams was, and Simon Williams, who does not have a self underneath the story, agreed to be him. The work of any honest assessment is to notice that the mechanism, not the position, is the man — and that the mechanism, for all its hazards, has more often than not delivered him to the side of the people he should have been on.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 14
## MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*Subject: Williams, Simon — "Wonder Man"*
*Method: enacted conduct over six decades of record, weighted over professed conduct; contradictions catalogued, not smoothed.*

---

### 14.1 The Operating Code (as enacted)

Strip away the speeches — the manifestos, the press interviews about pacifism, the on-set philosophizing, the Revengers-era jeremiads — and what remains, observable across the longitudinal record, is a code far more modest and far more consistent than the subject himself believes he holds. Reduced to its load-bearing axioms:

1. **Do not let an innocent die when you could have stood in front of them.** This is the bedrock. It is the rule he died for in *Avengers* #9, and it has never been violated, even at the apogee of the Revengers period. When his anti-Avengers ideology came into direct contact with a civilian in jeopardy, the ideology yielded. Every time.
2. **Do not kill a person who is talking to you.** Not "do not kill" — he has killed, in war, in defense, in the chaos of Kree engagements during the Force Works period. The actual rule is narrower and stranger: he will not kill someone with whom he is in conversation, in relationship, or in legible humanity. The Reaper, who is both his brother and an active mass murderer, has survived dozens of encounters that should have ended him because Simon will not be the one to do it.
3. **Stand with the broken person against the room.** Operationalized most clearly in the Pym court-martial sequence (*Avengers* #213 and following; *West Coast Avengers* #1) but visible throughout: when a teammate is in disgrace, Simon's position hardens *toward* them and *against* the consensus. It is the most reliable behavioral predictor in the file.
4. **Do not be Zemo's tool.** Articulated negatively, but it is the spine of his identity. Any time he detects that he has been instrumentalized by a charismatic operator running a longer game, he turns — late, often catastrophically late, but he turns.
5. **Earn the right to exist.** Not a moral axiom in the philosophical sense, but enacted as one: he behaves as if his continued life must be justified by service, sacrifice, or visible heroism. The performance is moral payment.

Those five rules are the *actually* operative framework. Note what is missing: no rule against lying (he lies, especially to himself), no rule against cowardice (he has fled and frozen and is honest about it), no rule against rivalry-driven sabotage (the Vision refusal exists), no consistent rule against escalating violence in defense of his self-image. The code is narrower than he claims and concentrated almost entirely on protection of others and resistance to being used.

---

### 14.2 What He Will Do

He will **take a hit meant for someone else**, automatically, without weighing it. The pattern is so reflexive in the combat record that it is properly classified as somatic ethics, not deliberation — he intercepts incoming fire the way a person flinches from a blow. The first death (Zemo, 1964), the Force Works death (1990s), and the various discorporation events are all this same behavior, scaled.

He will **lie about his own state** — physical, emotional, psychiatric — to remain operational. The post-resurrection period contains multiple instances of Simon claiming readiness he does not possess. He treats his interior life as a thing he should not burden others with, which is a moral position even when it produces poor outcomes.

He will **forgive serial offenders** in his orbit. Pym, Wanda after Disassembled, the Vision after every reconfiguration, even his brother. His threshold for re-extending trust is among the lowest in the Avengers cohort. He will frame this as fairness; it is also need.

He will **break ranks with institutional authority** when he believes a person, specifically, is being abandoned by it. He is bad at organizational loyalty in the abstract and good at personal loyalty in the particular. The Avengers as concept have never held him; specific Avengers have held him for life.

He will **perform the gesture publicly**. Apologies, declarations, renunciations, recommitments — they happen on stage, frequently with cameras present (literal cameras during the Hollywood era, the symbolic camera of teammate witness otherwise). This is not insincerity; the public performance is, for him, part of how a moral act becomes real.

He will **take ideological positions sincerely**. When he founds the Revengers, he believes the argument. He is not cynical, ever. This makes him more dangerous, not less, in his bad phases: a sincere romantic chasing a flawed thesis will go further than a cynic would dare.

He will **die again**. He has demonstrated this. The death-phobia of the post-resurrection arc never resolved into self-preservation; it resolved into a man who is terrified of dying and goes back into the fire anyway. This is the closest thing in the file to actual moral courage in the technical sense — acting against a fear that has not abated.

---

### 14.3 What He Will Not Do

He **will not kill his brother.** Across approximately forty publication years and dozens of direct confrontations with Eric, the line holds. He will subdue, contain, mourn, bury, recover, re-confront. He will not deliver the killing blow. The pattern is technically a failure of moral seriousness — Eric's continued life produces continued civilian dead — and Simon knows it. He accepts the cost rather than be the agent. The code, in this domain, is private and personal: the rule is not *do not kill* but *I, specifically, will not be the man who killed my brother*.

He **will not torture, interrogate coercively, or use his strength on a restrained person.** The negative space is conspicuous. Many of his peers have crossed this; he has not. His Class-100 strength makes the restraint significant — he is one of the few Avengers physically capable of casual lethality at the slightest miscalibration, and his discipline in this regard is near-perfect.

He **will not collaborate with Zemo, or with anyone whose pattern matches Zemo.** Once he has identified a figure as a manipulator-of-the-broken, he is immune to further recruitment by that figure. The corollary, dangerously, is that he can be recruited by *new* figures who do not match the pattern.

He **will not let Wanda be harmed in his presence.** This sits between the rules of conduct and the architecture of compulsion. It has produced moral outcomes (defense against the Reaper, defense during multiple cosmic incidents) and immoral ones (the Vision refusal, defended internally as protection of Wanda's future).

He **will not, in the long run, stay on the wrong side.** Every defection from the Avengers — Zemo, the Revengers, lesser quarrels — has been temporary. The reconciliation drive is, eventually, total. He cannot tolerate being permanently outside the room he has spent his life trying to be admitted to.

He **will not use his Hollywood platform to lie about other people.** Note the specificity. He will lie about himself (overstate, posture, image-manage), he will lie by omission about his condition, but the platform-to-defame move that the actor career would make trivially easy is absent from the record.

---

### 14.4 The Justifications (and What They Conceal)

Simon's stated reasons for his actions cluster into a small, repeated vocabulary that the file should learn to translate.

**"I had no choice."** Appears at every major decision point from the Zemo recruitment forward. Translates to: *I had a choice and the alternative cost was unbearable to me.* The Zemo deal was a choice (prison was survivable). The Vision refusal was a choice (the brain pattern donation was not lethal). The Revengers founding was a choice. The "no choice" framing is the verbal signature of a decision he is unwilling to own as preference.

**"Someone has to."** Heroic register. Translates to: *I need to be the someone, because being the someone is how I know I am here.* The motive is not impure — the act is often genuinely needed — but the framing reveals that the role-fulfillment is doing as much work as the necessity.

**"For Wanda."** Appears in defense of acts ranging from the entirely creditable (interposing himself between her and harm) to the indefensible (withholding the Vision template). Translates, in the negative cases, to: *because the alternative would diminish my standing with her, or hers with me.* The Wanda-justification is the most contaminated rhetorical instrument in his vocabulary, and the one he is least able to audit.

**"The Avengers have become..."** (Revengers-era). Translates to: *I have accumulated grievance I cannot otherwise discharge, and a thesis has appeared that licenses the discharge.* The argument is constructed *after* the affect, not before it. The tell is that the thesis evaporates the moment the affect is metabolized; he does not maintain the position once readmitted to the room.

**"I'm not the same man I was."** Continuous through the post-resurrection record. Translates to: *I am asking you to confirm that I am still a man at all.* It is a request for testimony disguised as a confession.

The pattern across all five: Simon's justifications are sincere but inverted — the stated reason is downstream of the felt need, and the felt need is almost always about location of the self in relation to others' regard.

---

### 14.5 Where the Code Is Consistent

Across sixty years of record, certain commitments hold under every stress condition tested:

- **Bystander protection.** No exception found. Not under coercion, not under ideology, not under the Revengers banner, not during the discorporation period when his very substance was uncertain. If a civilian is in line of fire, he is in front of them.
- **Refusal to be a finishing blow.** Bound up with but broader than the Reaper rule: even in the chaos of large engagements, the combat record shows him pulling strikes against downed opponents with a regularity that cannot be coincidence.
- **Loyalty to the publicly disgraced.** Tested against Pym (alleged abuser, court-martialed), Wanda (post-Disassembled), and others. Holds.
- **Eventual return.** Every exit is followed by a return. The arc is unfailing.
- **Refusal of the Zemo-pattern recruiter.** Once burned by that template, never again recruited by that template.

These are the bones of an actual ethics. They are not the ethics he describes himself as having — which is grander, more articulated, and more frequently revised — but they are the ethics he in fact has.

---

### 14.6 Where the Code Fractures

The fracture lines are precise and recurrent.

**Fracture One: The Wanda Variable.** The code's rules degrade in a roughly inverse relationship to proximity to Wanda Maximoff. At maximal distance from her (operating in deep space, in a Hollywood production, with the West Coast team during her absent periods), Simon's behavior aligns most closely with his stated ethics. At maximal proximity — particularly under romantic uncertainty — the code distorts. The Vision refusal is the canonical instance: a man who has never otherwise withheld aid from a fellow Avenger in mortal need withheld it from the Vision specifically, citing principle, while the actual variable was Wanda. He has never adequately re-examined this. When pressed, he produces fresh rationale. The fracture is permanent.

**Fracture Two: The Brother Exception.** The refusal-to-kill rule is, in the Eric case, a private indulgence with a body count attached. Every Reaper civilian-death after the second is, in some forensic sense, on Simon's ledger — a fact he half-acknowledges and cannot act upon. The code is not "do not kill" but "do not kill in ways that would destroy me," and his brother sits inside that protected interior.

**Fracture Three: The Grievance-Ideology Window.** Under sustained accumulation of unmetabolized affect — usually after a Wanda-loss, a death-and-return cycle, or a perceived dismissal by the Avengers institution — Simon becomes susceptible to constructed ideologies that license previously refused behavior. The Revengers period is the documented instance; there are minor precursors throughout. The fracture is not random: it requires a particular kind of stress accumulation and a particular kind of available thesis. Predictable, therefore preventable, by anyone close enough to read him.

**Fracture Four: Self-Disclosure and Self-Care.** The rule against burdening others with his condition produces operational lies that have endangered teammates. He has gone into combat under-recovered (post-resurrection arc), under-stabilized (post-discorporation), and under-disclosed (during the Revengers ideation, which was visible to those who knew him before he announced it). The code that says *do not be a burden* fractures the code that says *protect the people you fight beside*. He has never resolved the conflict.

**Fracture Five: The Performance Layer.** Because moral acts are, for him, partially constituted by their public legibility, his ethics distort in proportion to audience presence. Camera on: the gesture inflates, the apology lengthens, the renunciation gets a press release. Camera off: the same act is sometimes not performed at all, or is performed quieter and less completely. This is not hypocrisy in the standard sense — he is not pretending — but the witness-dependence is a genuine structural compromise of the ethics.

---

### 14.7 Diachronic Drift: How the Code Has Shifted

**Pre-transformation (Williams Industries era).** Code minimal and conventional. Obeyed law until law obstructed survival of the firm; then violated law in the form most likely to be discovered (embezzlement is a confession scheduled for later). The pre-Wonder Man Simon is morally unremarkable: a man with ordinary commitments who failed an extraordinary stress test and did not have the resources of character to refuse the fraud. The shame from this period is the substrate of everything that follows.

**Zemo recruitment and first death (1964).** First articulation of the operative code, in extremis. The turn against Zemo is the founding moral act. Note: it occurs after he has already accepted the power, infiltrated the team, and put them in danger. It is not refusal-of-evil; it is interruption-of-evil-in-progress. The pattern of late conscience, decisive when it arrives, is set here.

**Resurrection through death-phobia arc (mid-to-late 1970s).** Code in suspension. He is not making moral choices in this period so much as failing to make any choices — the freeze response dominates. When the arc resolves, the code reasserts but now carries the weight of having been failed; the post-recovery Simon is more morally vocal, partly to drown the memory.

**West Coast / Hollywood / Wanda era (mid-1980s through early 1990s).** Code most articulated, most performed, most fractured. The Vision refusal occurs here. The Pym loyalty occurs here. The same period produces his best and worst conduct because the audience pressure and the Wanda pressure are simultaneously at peak. He is, in this era, the cleanest exhibit of his own pattern: a sincere man performing sincerity, sometimes accurately and sometimes ruinously.

**Force Works and second death (mid-1990s).** Code reverts to its founding form: take the hit, die for the team. The intervening complexity drops away under combat pressure. This is, in a sense, his most morally legible period — and he spends most of it dead.

**Discorporation / Wanda-anchored existence (late 1990s–early 2000s).** Code essentially unavailable. He cannot act independently enough to choose. The ethics of an entity that exists only through another's longing are necessarily compromised; he is in this period more an object than an agent.
