The shame of having been *summoned* rather than *returned* is consequential for the next phase.

**Revengers and grievance phase (early 2010s).** Code at maximum distortion under maximum ideology. The fundamental rules (bystander protection, refusal of finishing blows) still hold, but the institutional and inter-personal layer collapses. He attacks former teammates while still refusing to kill them — the code's contradictions are completely visible in this period for anyone reading carefully. This is when he most resembles the man Zemo recruited, and he does not see it.

**Post-Revengers / late-career oscillation (mid-2010s onward).** Code now partially metabolized through repetition. He is more aware of his fracture lines than at any prior point, though awareness has not eliminated them. The pacifism phases and the rage phases alternate at shorter intervals; the gestures are smaller; the audience is less convinced. He is, in the late record, a man approaching the truth about his own ethics — that they are narrower and more personal than his rhetoric — and beginning, intermittently, to live within them rather than around them.

---

### 14.8 The Code Beneath the Code

What the file resolves to, after every layer of justification is stripped: Simon Williams's actual ethics are the ethics of a man who is trying, at every moment, to be the kind of person who would not have embezzled. Every standing rule he holds is, structurally, a corrective to 1964. He will not be bought. He will not let people down for money. He will not be the coward in the room. He will not be the man who chose himself over the institution that trusted him — except, catastrophically, when Wanda is the variable, at which point the original failure pattern reasserts and he chooses himself again, and constructs a justification afterward, and lives with the shame, and adds it to the pile, and tries again to be the kind of person who would not have done it.

The code is, therefore, both more limited and more honorable than its public version. It is the code of a man doing genuine moral work against a genuine moral injury, succeeding most of the time, failing in predictable places, and never — not in sixty years of record — abandoning the project. Whatever else the dossier concludes about him, this should stand: he is still trying, and the trying is real, and most men in his position would have stopped.

*— UATU, observing.*


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE

## Subject: Simon Williams ("Wonder Man")

---

## 6.1 Baseline Voice and Acoustic Profile

The subject's speaking voice is a trained baritone, audibly worked-on since the late-1970s migration to the West Coast and the stunt-then-acting career that followed. Recordings of pre-transformation Simon Williams (deposition transcripts from the Williams Innovations embezzlement trial, late-period civil filings) describe a higher, thinner, faster New Jersey-inflected speech — Paterson vowels, the long flat *a*, the dropped post-vocalic *r* in tired speech, and the verbal pacing of a man trying to talk his way out of an arithmetic problem. Post-ionic, the voice deepens by roughly a fifth and acquires a faint metallic resonance under emotional load, an artifact of energy-substrate vocal folds vibrating in a non-organic medium. Microphones pick up a sub-audible hum at 60–80 Hz when he is agitated; sound engineers on his film sets have routinely complained about it on the playback.

He has, by the 1990s, scrubbed the Jersey out of his speech consciously and incompletely. Under stress, fatigue, or in conversation with Eric, the vowels return within three or four sentences. This is the single most reliable forensic tell in his recorded speech: the **regression to Paterson** is involuntary and tightly correlated with affective destabilization.

Cadence is theatrical. He breathes from the diaphragm even in casual speech, projects past his interlocutor, and tends to hit final consonants harder than American conversational English requires. He has acquired what voice coaches call a "trailer voice" — the capacity to drop into a public-address register without seeming to shift posture. Teammates have noted, sometimes affectionately and sometimes not, that he "talks like he's miked."

---

## 6.2 Register Switching Across Contexts

The subject maintains at least five distinguishable communicative registers, and he switches between them with the unconscious fluency of someone whose self-cohesion depends on the switching. The registers are not masks layered over a stable core; they are the structure of the personality, expressed in language.

**Register A — "Avengers-formal."** Deployed in team briefings, public statements as a costumed operative, congressional/SHIELD testimony, and any setting where he believes the historical record is listening. Diction is elevated, sentence structure subordinated, modal verbs prominent (*we must, I would suggest, one might consider*). He uses the team's collective pronoun (*we*) more than any other Avenger of comparable tenure — measurable across the public-record transcripts. This register carries the heaviest concentration of borrowed phrases — locutions originally voiced by Captain America, the Vision, occasionally Reed Richards — repurposed without attribution. He is a magpie of authoritative speech.

**Register B — "Soundstage."** The Hollywood working voice. Faster, looser, peppered with industry shorthand (*the gag, the beat, on the day, in the can*), copious use of first names ("Phil tells me," "Janet mentioned"), and a habit of finishing other people's sentences to demonstrate engagement. Register B is where the bulk of his self-deprecating humor lives. It is also where he flirts.

**Register C — "Locker room."** Reserved for Hank Pym, Clint Barton, Bobbi Morse in the West Coast period, occasionally Ben Grimm. Profanity rises sharply (he is otherwise close to PG); contractions multiply; he allows himself to complain, which he almost never does in A or B. Register C is the only one in which he will speak ill of an absent teammate, and even then he reliably retracts within the same conversation ("ah, he's fine, he's fine, forget I said it").

**Register D — "Wanda."** A register of one addressee. Slower, quieter, the projection dropped. He uses her name disproportionately within sentences — a vocative tic that intimacy researchers flag as a marker of attachment hunger ("Wanda, I — Wanda, listen — Wanda"). Sentence fragments increase. Metaphor density spikes. He becomes, in her presence, the most verbally inefficient version of himself, which is to say the most honest.

**Register E — "Eric."** The brother voice. Flat, clipped, monosyllabic where possible. The Paterson vowels are fully reinstated. He calls Eric *Eric* — never Grim Reaper, even mid-combat — and refers to himself as *Simon*, not *Wonder Man*, in roughly nine out of ten recorded exchanges. Register E is the regression register: it is the speech of the younger brother he was before any of the rest of this happened.

The transitions between registers are themselves diagnostic. He can shift from B to A in a single breath when a camera turns on. He cannot shift cleanly *out* of E once he has dropped into it; an Eric encounter contaminates his speech for hours afterward, with Paterson vowels bleeding into the next press scrum.

---

## 6.3 Lexical Signatures and Recurrent Phrases

A concordance of his recorded speech across six decades surfaces a small set of phrases that recur with statistically anomalous frequency. These are his fingerprints.

- **"Look — "** as a sentence-opener under disagreement. Functions as a softener and a stall; buys him half a second to compose the rebuttal he has not yet thought of. Appears in roughly one in eleven of his utterances in adversarial team meetings.
- **"For what it's worth."** A pre-emptive devaluation of his own forthcoming statement, deployed when he is about to say something he believes is correct but expects to be dismissed for. The phrase concedes the dismissal before it occurs.
- **"I'm not — I'm not that guy anymore."** A self-referential denial that resurfaces in every era of his life: the embezzler, the Zemo pawn, the coward, the jealous lover, the Revenger. The repetition is the symptom; the past selves are not metabolized but renounced, sequentially, in identical syntax.
- **"What was I supposed to do?"** Rhetorical, addressed to no one in particular, deployed after morally compromised choices. The Vision-engram refusal, the Revengers turn, the Force Works decisions — all post-hoc narrated in this phrase.
- **"It's fine. I'm fine."** The doubled assertion of fineness, almost never true when uttered. Hank Pym has reportedly learned to hear it as a request.
- **"You don't have to — "** A construction he uses to pre-empt the other person's care, gratitude, or apology. It looks generous; it functions to refuse the relational debt that would obligate him to receive.
- **"Honestly?"** As a one-word interrogative preface. He uses this when he is about to be approximately half-honest. A reliable inverse-tell.

He almost never says *I love you* as a discrete utterance. The phrase appears perhaps a dozen times in his recorded life, all but two of them addressed to Wanda, and most of them buried mid-paragraph rather than offered standalone. He communicates love through declarative observations about the loved person ("You did the right thing." "You look — you look like you again.") and through the offer of physical proximity rather than speech.

---

## 6.4 Verbal Tics, Disfluencies, and Micro-Patterns

**The double-take stammer.** When surprised or contradicted, he repeats the first word of his response: "I — I don't — I don't think that's…" The stammer is performative-adjacent (he is an actor, and he knows it reads as searching) but it predates the acting career, so it is genuine in origin and instrumentalized later. Frequency rises sharply in Wanda's presence and in any conversation about the Vision.

**The self-interrupting clause.** He will begin a sentence, abort it mid-clause, and restart on a different subject, often a softer one. "I was going to — never mind. How's Cassie?" This is avoidance dressed as solicitude.

**The chuckle-before-the-hard-thing.** A short, unmusical laugh — almost a cough — that precedes any disclosure he expects to hurt him to make. Pym has identified it explicitly in conversation ("There's the laugh, Simon, just say it"). The chuckle is the audible seam between the performed self and the underlying one.

**The third-person slide.** Under high stress he will occasionally refer to himself by codename in the third person ("Wonder Man can take it"), a tic that emerges most in the death-phobia arc and again during the Revengers period. The third-person construction is the language of someone trying to make the self into an object he can look at from outside, which is to say someone whose first-person is not currently load-bearing.

**Vocative overuse.** He uses his interlocutor's name within the first sentence of an exchange far more often than baseline. It reads as warmth; it functions as a self-orienting device — naming the person opposite him to confirm where the conversation is happening and who he is supposed to be inside it.

**Trailing ellipsis.** Sentences left unfinished, particularly when the natural completion would commit him to a position. "I just thought maybe we could…" He lets the listener finish, and then agrees or disagrees with their completion rather than his own.

**The reformulating apology.** When he apologizes, he restates the offense in his own words before the *sorry* — "I shouldn't have said that to you, I know it landed wrong, I'm sorry." This is genuine and a useful tell: the length of the restatement scales with the size of the underlying shame.

---

## 6.5 Rhetorical Patterns

Simon's rhetoric is **narrative before it is propositional.** He persuades by telling stories — often about himself — in which the moral is implicit. When forced into argument, his structure is recognizable: he opens with a concession to the opposing view ("You're not wrong about — "), pivots on a personal anecdote ("but when I was — "), and lands on a value-claim presented as obvious ("and you can't tell me that's not worth something"). The argumentative weakness is the pivot: the anecdote rarely entails the conclusion, but the emotional cadence carries the listener past the gap.

He is **rhetorically vulnerable to symmetry.** Any argument structured to mirror the form of his own self-narrative — *you were once X, now you must Y* — lands harder than it should. Zemo used this to recruit him originally; he used it on himself to justify the Revengers. He is aware of the vulnerability and does not know how to defend against it.

His **public speech** (interviews, premieres, the rare team-spokesperson moment) is competent and slightly over-prepared. He works from beats. He has been observed mouthing his next sentence while the interviewer is still asking the question — the muscle memory of an actor with lines.

His **conflict speech** has a recognizable escalation ladder: irony → moral framing → personal disclosure → grievance enumeration → ultimatum → withdrawal. He almost never reaches the ultimatum stage with people he loves; he reaches it quickly with institutions.

He is **uncharacteristically poor at small talk** for someone who works in entertainment. He defaults either to the prepared (industry shop) or the disclosing (the unbidden personal admission). The middle band — weather, sports, polite nothing — is not in his repertoire. Anyone he sits next to at a function gets either a monologue about a stunt rig or, two drinks in, the embezzlement.

---

## 6.6 Deflection and Defensive Language

The subject deflects through five characteristic moves, all linguistically detectable.

**Deflection by self-deprecation.** "Yeah, well, what do I know, I'm just the guy who — " followed by the most damning self-summary available ("got my own brother killed, got my company stolen, got my brain copied"). The move forecloses criticism by performing it more harshly than the interlocutor would; it also recruits sympathy. It is so reliably effective that he has come to depend on it, and several teammates over the years have stopped pretending to be moved.

**Deflection by humor.** A one-liner deployed at the precise moment a more serious response is being requested. The joke is usually genre-aware — a reference to his own celebrity, his death count, his costume — and functions to relocate the conversation onto safer ground. Pym, Barton, and Carol Danvers have each, in different decades, called him on this in nearly identical words: *Simon, knock it off.*

**Deflection by reframe-to-principle.** When pressed on a specific decision, he elevates the discussion to abstract values ("the question is really about what we're for"), where his rhetorical strengths and his moral self-image are both stronger. This is the engine of the Revengers manifesto: a specific grievance laundered through generalization.

**Deflection by physical exit.** When language fails him he simply leaves the room, often mid-sentence. The unfinished sentence is the linguistic residue. He almost always returns within a day with a reformulated position; the exit is a regulation strategy, not a severance.

**Deflection by attribution to the ionic condition.** "It's — the form is unstable today, I — let me — " offered when the actual instability is affective. He has used the body as an excuse for the mind for at least twenty in-story years.

---

## 6.7 The Language of Love

He does not say it; he describes around it.

To Wanda his speech in private is dense with **attentive specificity** — he notices and names what she is wearing, the particular tea she has made, the song that was playing the first time, a freckle. The cataloguing is the love-language. He remembers, and he tells her he remembers. He uses her name as punctuation. He gives her, repeatedly, the same compliment in slightly different phrasings, as if the search for the right wording were itself a gift. When she is sad, his sentences shorten and he asks small questions — *what do you want, what would help, is this okay* — without filling the silence between them.

To Hank Pym, love is expressed through **the refusal to leave.** Pym in his worst weeks heard from Simon every day, often by phone, often consisting of nothing but *I'm here, do you need anything, I'll call tomorrow.* The relentlessness is the message.

To teammates broadly, affection is expressed through **physical idiom in speech** — *brother, partner, my man* — and through the willingness to take a hit verbally as well as physically. He will absorb a teammate's bad mood without retaliating and then make a joke that lets them off the hook.

To his brother, love is expressed through **refusal to stop addressing him by his name.** Every Grim Reaper encounter, Simon says *Eric.* The naming is the love; the brother knows it; the brother hates it; the naming continues.

To audiences, love (such as it is) is expressed through **the line read** — a small theatrical generosity, an extra beat given to the other actor, a willingness to be upstaged. Co-stars describe him as easy on set.

---

## 6.8 The Language of Threat

He threatens badly. It is among the most useful intelligence facts in this file.

His threats are theatrical — overwritten, often quoted from his own films or from comic-book conventions he has internalized ("you really don't want to do this," "walk away, kid, while you still can"). The phrasings are borrowed; the menace is performed; opponents who know him well do not take them seriously, and they are correct not to.

His **actual** dangerousness in language presents differently and quietly. When Simon is about to do something genuinely violent, he becomes **shorter, lower, and more polite.** The honorifics return. The contractions vanish. "I'd like you to step away from her, please." Subordinates of any rival organization who have learned to read this — there are a few — describe the politeness as the warning. It is the only register in which he is not performing, and it is therefore the only one in which his stated intent and his behavioral intent align.

He almost never threatens by escalation; he threatens by stating a fact in the conditional. "If you do that, I'll have to stop you." The verb *have to* is load-bearing — it places the agency on the opponent and absolves him of choice, which is also how he describes most of his life's compromised acts. The grammar of his threats and the grammar of his rationalizations are the same grammar.

---

## 6.9 The Language of Grief

Grief in this subject is **somatic before verbal.** The ionic form destabilizes first; the words follow late and clumsily.

Verbally, he grieves in **circumlocution.** He does not name the dead. He refers to "what happened," "after — after everything," "since…" The trailing ellipsis is, in grief, near-constant. Asked directly about Eric's death, his sentences fragment within three or four words and he changes the subject; the question can be reopened weeks later and he will be slightly more capable, then more, then eventually able to name the brother by name in past tense. The work is slow and visible.

He grieves Vision-related losses with a particular **defensive crispness** — short sentences, factual, no metaphor — because the grief is contaminated by guilt and the guilt is intolerable. The crispness is the wall.

He grieves Wanda losses (the various separations, the *Disassembled* break, every withdrawal) by **talking too much.** Hank Pym's phone records from those periods, if they existed in compileable form, would show calls of unusual length, in which Simon revisits the relationship from increasingly oblique angles, looking for a frame in which it survives. The verbosity is the symptom; in his other griefs he goes quiet.

He grieves his own deaths — and this is the strange one, but it is in the record — by **narrating them.** Post-resurrection, in the Englehart/Michelinie period and again after each subsequent return, he tells the story of his most recent death to anyone who will sit still. The retellings are formulaic and the formula evolves over weeks until it stabilizes into a version he can live with. This is functional, in the way that any trauma narrative is functional, and it is also exhausting to the people around him, and he knows it, and he does it anyway, because the alternative is to hold the experience wordless.

---

## 6.10 Tells: A Forensic Summary

For any analyst, handler, or interlocutor needing to read the subject in real time, the following indicators are reliable across decades.

1. **Paterson vowels returning** → affective destabilization in progress. Time to a behaviorally significant event: minutes to hours.
2. **Third-person self-reference ("Wonder Man can…")** → identity-coherence under strain. Combat decisions made in this register should be reviewed.
3. **The pre-disclosure chuckle** → he is about to tell you the truth, and it costs him. Do not interrupt.
4. **Doubled "I'm fine. It's fine."** → he is not. The doubling is the request.
5. **Excessive use of the interlocutor's first name** → he is seeking orientation, not connection.
6. **Sudden politeness and shortened sentences in a hostile context** → imminent action. Treat as the warning it is.
7. **Reframing a specific question into a principled abstraction** → the specific answer is one he does not wish to give. Re-ask the specific.
8. **Trailing ellipsis on a name** → grief that has not been worked through. Note which name.
9. **Mid-sentence physical exit** → regulation, not severance. Expect return within 24 hours with a revised position.
10. **Borrowed phrasing from a recognized authority figure (Captain America cadences, Vision sentence structures)** → he is leaning on a template because his own register feels insufficient. The position he is articulating is not stably his own and is subject to revision under pressure.

The unifying principle of all of the above: **Simon Williams talks more, and more variously, the less stably he knows who is talking.** The volume and the register-switching are inversely correlated with self-cohesion. When he is well, he is briefer, quieter, funnier, and more himself. When he is unwell, he is everywhere in the room, in every voice he has ever borrowed, looking — through speech — for the one that will hold.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Format: GIVEN [stimulus / situation] → EXPECT [predicted behavior, with mechanism and confidence]. Confidence reported as LOW / MOD / HIGH / VERY HIGH, reflecting evidentiary weight from canon plus structural inference. Predictions cover the unobserved 98% of Subject's life — the hours between panels.*

---

## 1. MORNINGS, WAKING, AND THE FIRST HOUR

**GIVEN** Subject wakes alone in his own residence on a non-mission day → **EXPECT** a delay of 30–90 seconds before rising, during which he performs an unconscious somatic check — flexing fingers, watching the faint ionic shimmer under the skin of the back of his hand, confirming that he has held form through sleep. He does not require sleep biologically; he sleeps because the ritual reassures him he is contiguous with the person who lay down. (**HIGH** — direct extrapolation from form-instability arcs and identity-coherence deficit.)

**GIVEN** Subject wakes next to a romantic partner → **EXPECT** the somatic check is suppressed and replaced by an immediate orientation toward the partner — looking at her, listening for her breathing, often touching her shoulder or hair before she is awake. The mirror is present; the self-check is unnecessary. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject wakes from a dream of his own death or of the catatonic interval → **EXPECT** he stays in bed an extra 10–20 minutes, speaks aloud (to himself, to a pet, to the room) some banal verifying sentence — the day's date, an appointment, a line he is learning — then rises and immediately puts on music or a podcast. Silence is the trigger; sound is the chosen anchor. (**MOD-HIGH** — derived from post-resurrection arc patterns of intrusive imagery.)

**GIVEN** the morning's first mirror → **EXPECT** a long look. Two to four seconds, then a smile he practices and discards, then a second neutral look. He is checking the face for the man he remembers being and tuning the public version for the day. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** breakfast offered socially → **EXPECT** he accepts and performs eating with evident pleasure — coffee, toast, eggs — though he derives no nutritional benefit. The performance of ordinary humanity is its own reward; refusing food in company would single him out as the energy-thing and not the man. He eats more, and more demonstratively, in company than alone. (**HIGH** — directly inferable from persona-borrowing and the gap between ionic physiology and lived identity.)

**GIVEN** breakfast alone → **EXPECT** coffee only, often forgotten halfway through, while he reads scripts, scrolls trades, or runs lines under his breath. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

---

## 2. GROOMING, DRESS, AND THE BODY AS PROJECT

**GIVEN** Subject preparing for a public appearance (premiere, talk show, convention panel) → **EXPECT** a preparation window 2–3x longer than the appearance warrants. Specifically: hair worked over repeatedly even though it sets identically each time; multiple wardrobe rejections; a final selection that is one register more flamboyant than what a peer would wear in the same context. The red-and-green costume era is the load-bearing canonical evidence that his taste tilts toward visibility over restraint. (**VERY HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject preparing for a private dinner with one or two close friends → **EXPECT** the opposite — chosen quickly, often a single dark t-shirt and jeans, with the inverse signaling: *I trust you enough to be unperformed.* The understatement is itself a gift. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject catches sight of his own reflection unexpectedly (storefront glass, dark window, polished elevator) → **EXPECT** a half-second arrest of motion, then resumed walking. Frequency: many times per day. He is not vain in the simple sense; he is checking for continuity. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a photograph taken of him by a stranger → **EXPECT** he asks, casually, to see it. He almost always asks. He smiles when he sees it. The photograph confirms the ionic body has registered on a sensor as the man he means to be. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a bad photograph of himself surfaces online → **EXPECT** outsized hurt disproportionate to the stimulus, suppressed in conversation, processed alone — and a small behavioral adjustment for the next two weeks (different angle of approach to cameras, different hair part, a new jacket). (**MOD**.)

**GIVEN** shaving → **EXPECT** he still shaves, daily, despite ionic stasis rendering hair growth slow-to-nil. The ritual is the point. Same razor brand for years. Same direction. He has shaved this face through three of his own deaths. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 3. SPEECH, HUMOR, AND CONVERSATIONAL TELLS

**GIVEN** Subject in any group of three or more → **EXPECT** he speaks within the first thirty seconds, usually a joke, usually self-deprecating-but-flattering (a joke whose surface is at his own expense but whose subtext positions him as the kind of man who can joke at his own expense). This is the West Coast bravado pattern weaponized as social entry. (**VERY HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject in a one-on-one with a person he trusts → **EXPECT** the volume drops, the cadence slows, the jokes thin out. He is capable of presence and uses it sparingly because it costs him. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject is asked a direct question about his feelings → **EXPECT** a 1–2 second delay (uncharacteristic for him), then either (a) a deflecting line delivered with practiced timing, or (b) — if the questioner is trusted — an answer that is one register more honest than required, followed by a closing joke that rescinds it. He gives feeling, then takes it back. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject is paid a compliment → **EXPECT** he accepts it visibly (smile, slight head tilt, "thank you"), then within thirty seconds redirects the compliment to a third party present or absent. The acceptance is genuine; the redirection is shame-management. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject is criticized in public → **EXPECT** a smile, agreement, a self-amplifying joke ("yeah, and I'm balding too"). Internally: registered, weighed, retained. He will revisit the criticism alone, often. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject is criticized in private by someone whose regard he values → **EXPECT** immediate over-correction. He will apologize twice, propose a remediation, ask if the remediation is sufficient. The pattern repeats with Pym, with Wanda, with team leaders. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Subject is contradicted on a fact he is sure of → **EXPECT** he yields rather than presses, even when right, unless the topic is one of his three or four invested domains (acting craft, the Wanda-Vision history, the ethics of his own past choices). On invested topics he will dig in disproportionately. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** any conversational reference to Tony Stark, the Vision, or his brother → **EXPECT** a micro-expression — a tightening of the mouth, a slight delay before the next sentence — followed by either a deflecting joke or an unusually generous, performed-magnanimous statement about the named party. The generosity is the giveaway. (**VERY HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** someone tells him a story about themselves → **EXPECT** active, performed listening: eye contact, nods, follow-up questions. He is good at this and has worked at it. Then a 50/50 chance of a counter-story positioning his own experience. (**MOD**.)

---

## 4. SOLITUDE, DOWNTIME, AND PRIVATE HABITS

**GIVEN** Subject has an unscheduled evening alone → **EXPECT**: he does not stay alone. He calls someone. If no one answers, he goes out — a bar he doesn't drink at, a screening, a gym, a walk on a pier where strangers will recognize him. The absence of mirrors is the threat. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he genuinely cannot go out (storm, illness in the household, voluntary retreat) → **EXPECT** he watches his own old work, claims he is doing notes for a part, watches it twice. The footage is a stable reference of who he was on a Tuesday in 2009. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he wants to relax → **EXPECT** novels, not nonfiction; classic Hollywood biographies; scripts he has been sent. He reads quickly. He has a low patience for analytic prose; high patience for narrative. (Direct from cognitive-style profile.) (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** the residence — characterize → **EXPECT**: clean, photogenic, somewhat impersonal in the living areas (as if staged); intensely personal in one private room (an office or den), where the walls hold framed personal photographs heavy on the Avengers years and on Wanda — *displayed but not centered*, arranged so they can be plausibly explained as casual. Books in the office, scripts on the desk, a single piece of memorabilia from his father's company kept in a drawer, not on a shelf. (**MOD-HIGH** — inferred from shame-substrate around origin plus persona-management.)

**GIVEN** he is asked to host a dinner → **EXPECT** he accepts, over-caters, hires help while pretending he didn't, and tells a self-deprecating story about an actor's catering disaster to defuse the over-preparation. (**MOD**.)

---

## 5. EATING, DRINKING, AND CONSUMPTION

**GIVEN** any restaurant → **EXPECT** he is known there or wants to be known there. He tips conspicuously, learns the staff's names within two visits, returns. He prefers being a regular somewhere to being anonymous everywhere. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** alcohol offered socially → **EXPECT** he accepts the glass, holds it, drinks performatively, does not finish. The canon's noted absence of substance use sustains: he will not allow loss of control. The held glass is camouflage. (**HIGH** — directly from sober-in-actor-milieu observation.)

**GIVEN** he is pressed about the held drink → **EXPECT** a smooth line — "early call," "trying to dry out for a part," "doctor's orders" — never the real answer (that he does not metabolize it usefully and does not trust himself to lose any further control of his interior). (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** offers of recreational drugs in industry contexts → **EXPECT** refusal, smiling, often with a joke that protects the offerer's dignity. He has no contempt for users; he has terror for himself. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** caffeine → **EXPECT** consumed liberally and performatively. The ritual of coffee is a humanizing prop. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

---

## 6. EXERCISE, TRAINING, AND THE GYM

**GIVEN** he goes to a gym → **EXPECT** he goes to a gym. This is the key paradox: he is Class-100 strong and does not require physical training, yet he trains regularly. He lifts moderate weights to high rep counts, runs on treadmills he could outpace by a factor of fifty, attends boxing classes. Mechanism: the gym is somatic anchoring — felt exertion in a body whose default state has no resistance is one of the few reliable proofs he is *in* a body. He sweats deliberately. (**HIGH** — high-confidence inference from the somatized-affect pattern.)

**GIVEN** he is sparring with a normal human trainer → **EXPECT** he is exquisitely careful, scaled down to a credible amateur fighter's range, drops "tells" to let the trainer score, takes hits with visible reaction. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is sparring with a superhuman teammate → **EXPECT** he holds back roughly 70% of capacity and is consistently surprised when out-performed. The under-trust of his own power, noted in the personality workup, is operational here. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 7. ROUTES, ROUTINES, AND SPATIAL HABITS

**GIVEN** he drives → **EXPECT** he drives himself, prefers convertibles or visibly expensive coupes, takes scenic routes between two points when time permits, varies the route on consecutive days less from countersurveillance instinct than from boredom and self-narration ("today I take the canyon"). (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he flies (as Wonder Man, under his own power, not commercial) → **EXPECT** he prefers low altitudes over populated areas where he can be seen and high altitudes over open water where he cannot. The two settings serve different needs — visibility and decompression. (**MOD**.)

**GIVEN** he enters any room → **EXPECT** within ten seconds he has identified the exits, the highest-status person, the most-attractive person, and the person most likely to recognize him. The first is residual from Avengers training; the second and third are dispositional; the fourth is occupational. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar room with no one in it → **EXPECT** he gravitates to the window and stands at it. Not for tactical reasons. He likes being framed by light. (**MOD**.)

**GIVEN** he is offered a seat → **EXPECT** he chooses one that places him in the visual center of the group and oriented toward the room's primary light source. He does this without thinking. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

---

## 8. PHONES, SOCIAL MEDIA, AND DIGITAL HYGIENE

**GIVEN** his phone — characterize → **EXPECT** notifications mostly silenced; agent and publicist on a permitted list; Avengers comm in a separate, never-silenced app. He checks his own mentions on social media more often than he admits, less often than his publicist does. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a negative review or hostile thread surfaces → **EXPECT** he reads it once, screenshots it (mechanism: revisits in private later), does not respond. He is too media-trained to engage; too thin-skinned to ignore. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a fan message of unusual sincerity → **EXPECT** he replies, often at length, often in the small hours, sometimes regrets it. The sincere mirror is irresistible to him. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he posts → **EXPECT** the posts skew toward: workout shots framed as humor, set photos with crew (never above-the-line talent he is rivalrous with), team appearances with the Avengers tagged correctly and self-effacingly, a quarterly long-form earnest post about a cause that is read by close friends as a tell about his current emotional state. (**MOD**.)

**GIVEN** he is asked about a controversial public matter → **EXPECT** vague, decent, non-committal language, unless the matter touches one of his three invested domains (mental health stigma, criminal-justice second chances, the ethics of superhuman conduct), in which case the answer becomes specific, heartfelt, and longer than the interviewer wanted. The second-chances stake is the embezzlement, undisguised. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 9. MONEY

**GIVEN** disposable income → **EXPECT** spent visibly on: the home, the car, clothes for public appearance, restaurants, generous gifts. Spent invisibly on: a financial planner he over-trusts; quiet recurring donations to prisoner-reentry organizations and to mental-health nonprofits; a stipend to one or two old contacts from his father's company or his prison stint whom no one has met. (**MOD-HIGH** — the embezzlement substrate predicts both visible competence and private restitution behaviors.)

**GIVEN** a financial decision under stress → **EXPECT** poor. He defers to the planner, signs what is put in front of him, has been taken advantage of more than once and does not discuss it. (**MOD**.)

**GIVEN** he is asked for money by an old contact → **EXPECT** he gives, with shame on both sides papered over by a joke. He is a soft mark for old debts. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 10. ANIMALS, CHILDREN, AND THE UNTHREATENING

**GIVEN** a dog → **EXPECT** immediate, unforced, full attention. The dog does not require him to perform. He kneels readily. He talks to it. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he owns a pet → **EXPECT** a dog rather than a cat (he wants to be greeted), medium-sized, often a rescue (the second-chances script). He talks to it more than he talks to most people. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a child → **EXPECT** he is good with children up to about age ten — playful, silly, willing to be the buffoon. With adolescents he stiffens, because adolescents see through performance and he knows it. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** an elderly fan → **EXPECT** disproportionate warmth and time given. Substitute-parent dynamics are live, particularly with men of his father's generation. (**MOD**.)

---

## 11. RELATIONSHIPS, DATING, AND THE WANDA-SHADOW

**GIVEN** he is single and dating casually → **EXPECT** he dates frequently, charmingly, shallowly; partners are commonly other public figures or industry-adjacent; relationships last 3–9 months on a recurring rhythm; he ends them as gently as he can with a half-honest reason and stays on cordial terms. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a partner attempts to deepen the relationship beyond ~9 months → **EXPECT** he panics quietly, becomes scheduling-elusive, picks a manageable fight that he can apologize for in a way that paradoxically closes the relationship. The Wanda-attachment makes serious alternatives unconsciously intolerable. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Wanda enters or re-enters his orbit in any capacity → **EXPECT** every other relational priority bends. He cancels, reschedules, appears wherever she will be, performs casual encounter. Current partners notice. (**VERY HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** Wanda is reported to be in a relationship with another → **EXPECT** a several-day decompensation visible to close friends as withdrawal, sharper humor, more visible exercise, occasionally a small ionic flare under stress (a flicker, easily missed, when something is mentioned). (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is in conversation about the Vision → **EXPECT** scrupulous, almost forensic fairness; over-credit to the Vision; a quality of self-supervision in the speech. He is being heard by an internal Wanda. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 12. FRIENDSHIP AND THE LOYALTY-TO-THE-BROKEN PATTERN

**GIVEN** a friend in crisis (legal, psychiatric, professional collapse) → **EXPECT** Subject shows up. Physically, in person, repeatedly, without being asked twice. This is the Pym pattern and it is one of his most stable behaviors. He is better in others' crises than in his own. (**VERY HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a friend in steady success and stability → **EXPECT** lower contact frequency, occasional warmth, no neglect but no urgency. He is not jealous of stable friends; he is simply less drawn to them. He requires being needed. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a teammate has been publicly disgraced → **EXPECT** Subject visits, calls, and is one of the first to make a public statement of qualified support, often before he should. The original failure makes him reflexively unwilling to abandon the disgraced. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** an estranged friend reaches out → **EXPECT** he meets, immediately, often suggesting the time and place himself. He does not let estrangements harden if he can help it. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 13. AUTHORITY, INSTITUTIONS, AND TEAMS

**GIVEN** Subject is on a team with a clear leader he respects (Cap, Pym in good periods, Rogers-type figures) → **EXPECT** compliant, often supportive, will accept assignments below his power level without protest. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is on a team with a leader he does not respect → **EXPECT** subtle undermining: stage-whisper jokes, late arrivals, generous compliance in operations but ideological needling in debriefs. Eventually, a public break. The Revengers turn is the load-bearing canon — institutional grievance metastasizes when leadership credibility fails. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is offered leadership → **EXPECT** he accepts, performs the role with visible effort, second-guesses his own decisions in private, leans on a deputy he trusts, and is relieved when the role ends. Force Works is the precedent. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** police, federal, or government questioning → **EXPECT** cooperative, lawyered, polite, donates time later to a related charity. The criminal record is the live wire; he wants to be — wants to be *seen* to be — on the institution's side. (**HIGH**.)

---

## 14. STRANGERS AND THE PUBLIC

**GIVEN** an autograph request → **EXPECT** granted, with a 2–4 sentence conversation he initiates ("where are you from? — first time in town?"), a personalized inscription, a held smile for the photo. He is genuinely energized by these encounters. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is approached by someone visibly mentally unwell in public → **EXPECT** he does not flinch, does not summon security except in clear threat, gives time and attention. The shame substrate around his own identity-coherence deficit produces unusual tolerance. (**MOD-HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** he is approached by someone hostile, accusing him of past association with villains → **EXPECT** he absorbs it. Does not argue. May say "you're not wrong." Walks away rather than defends. Later, alone, processes it for hours. (**HIGH**.)

**GIVEN** a fan presents him with a piece of his own merchandise from a specific past era (e.g., 1980s costume) → **EXPECT** delight on the surface, complicated affect underneath; he autographs the older item warmly and the more recent one mechanically. The past versions are the proofs of continuity. (**MOD**.)

---

## 15. SLEEP, NIGHT, AND THE SMALL HOURS

**GIVEN** he sleeps → **EXPECT** he sleeps 4–6 hours, not because he needs more but because lying awake invites the intrusive material. He prefers sleeping with low ambient sound: white noise, low TV, an old film he has seen many times. Silence is the trigger. (


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*An operational forecast of Simon Williams under acute stress. Each prediction is GIVEN → EXPECT, with substantiation drawn from the canonical record (Avengers #9, the Englehart/Michelinie post-resurrection arc, the Englehart/Byrne West Coast era through VisionQuest, the Force Works and Busiek runs, the Bendis-era Revengers arc, and subsequent Remender/solo material). Forecasts are calibrated to the substrate established in §3–5: insecure-preoccupied attachment, dissociative-spectrum identity instability, vulnerable narcissistic features, somatized affect (ionic form responds to feeling), and a shame core organized around the original embezzlement.*

---

## A. THE COMBAT-CRISIS BAND

### A.1 — Death-Proximate Threat

**GIVEN:** an immediate threat capable of killing him — sustained energy attack, reality-warp targeting his coherence, a weapon explicitly framed as "ionic-disruptor" or analogous.

**EXPECT:** a measurable first-beat hesitation. Not the freeze of the post-resurrection arc (that has remitted as syndrome) but a sub-second flinch, often masked by a quip or a wider-than-necessary opening swing. Pupils — when he has pupils — will read as fixed-distance; the gaze defocuses for a fraction of a second as the intrusive memory of his first death cues. He will then overcompensate by charging rather than maneuvering, because passive defense is the position he cannot tolerate (it replicates the helpless-dying body-position). If the threat persists beyond ~90 seconds of engagement, expect ionic flare: visible luminosity-spike at the shoulders and jawline, slight loss of edge-definition at the fingertips. This is somatic leak, not power-up. He will not name it. Teammates familiar with him (Iron Man, Beast, Wanda) will recognize it and adjust.

### A.2 — A Teammate Dies In Front of Him

**GIVEN:** an Avenger or West Coast peer is killed in the engagement, particularly by a method resembling his own first death (massive trauma, instantaneous, no recovery window).

**EXPECT:** initial composure for the duration of the fight — performance carries him — followed by acute decompensation within 6–18 hours. He will not sleep (he does not need to, which removes the natural circuit-breaker). He will be found at the site, or at the morgue, or repeatedly re-watching footage. He will speak about the deceased in the present tense for 24–72 hours. If pressed to debrief he will deflect into a story about himself ("when I died, I —") and then catch himself, and the catching is the most reliable diagnostic — a small wince, a hand to the back of the neck, the line "sorry, this isn't about me." It is about him. It is always about him. This is not malignant narcissism; it is the only template he has for processing death.

### A.3 — Captured, Restrained, Powerless

**GIVEN:** he is rendered immobile — power-nullifier, containment field, sufficient mystical binding.

**EXPECT:** the worst presentation in his repertoire. Restraint replicates the prison cell (pre-Zemo) AND the inert-corpse interval AND the discorporated state simultaneously — three of his foundational traumas stacked. Expect rapid breathing despite no metabolic need (vestigial behavior), verbal escalation moving from bravado ("you know this won't hold me") through bargaining ("look, whatever you want —") to a kind of pleading he will later be unable to remember clearly. If the captor names him "Simon" he will respond; if the captor calls him "Wonder Man" with contempt he will get quiet. The quiet is more dangerous than the talking. Probability of an ill-considered deal with the captor — information, a favor, a future obligation — rises sharply past the 4-hour mark and approaches near-certainty past 24. He has been a man recruited from a cell before. The script is grooved.

### A.4 — Civilian Death He Could Have Prevented

**GIVEN:** a bystander dies within his reach during an engagement.

**EXPECT:** 48–72 hours of public visibility followed by 1–3 weeks of withdrawal. The public window is performative — statements, appearances at the funeral if appropriate, possibly a press interview in which he says the right things with too much polish. The withdrawal is the real event: he will not answer Avengers comms, will be in his Los Angeles property or an analog, will rewatch his own films (the early ones; the bad ones), and will draft and not send a resignation. He will accept being talked out of resignation by exactly one person — historically Wanda, in her absence Pym, in their absence Beast or whoever currently functions as the trusted mirror. He cannot self-soothe. He requires the mirror.

---

## B. THE BETRAYAL BAND

### B.1 — Betrayal By An Avenger

**GIVEN:** a current or former Avenger is revealed to have manipulated, deceived, or weaponized him.

**EXPECT:** disproportionate reaction relative to the betrayal's objective magnitude. The Avengers are the institution that vindicated his turn against Zemo — they are the proof that switching sides was the right thing. A betrayal from inside that frame retroactively destabilizes the foundational good act of his life. Expect, in sequence: (1) public minimization ("we'll work it out"); (2) private rumination, days to weeks; (3) a sudden, articulate, surprisingly well-organized grievance position that recruits other malcontents. The Revengers (*New Avengers Annual* #1, 2011) is the template, not an aberration. He is forecastable to repeat this structure whenever an institutional betrayal pierces the Avengers-as-redemption frame. The intellectualization — "they are a destabilizing force on reality" — will be sincere to him in the moment and embarrassing to him in retrospect.

### B.2 — Betrayal By Wanda

**GIVEN:** Wanda chooses against him, deceives him, or — most acutely — chooses the Vision, a reconstituted Vision, or any successor figure.

**EXPECT:** the worst-case decompensation in the entire profile. Ionic destabilization is essentially guaranteed within 24–96 hours. Form flares, partial dispersion, possible involuntary discorporation episodes lasting minutes to hours. He will not attack her — this is one of the firm bright lines, derived from §5's moral floor — but he will become unreliable in every other domain. Expect: a grand gesture (a sacrifice attempt, a vow of pacifism, a public renunciation), followed by retraction, followed by silence. If the betrayal is framed by Wanda as "you were never really mine / I was never really yours," expect a months-long disappearance. He has done some version of this before. He will do it again. The substrate (§3: existence is mirror-dependent on her regard) cannot be reasoned out of him.

### B.3 — Betrayal By His Own Brother

**GIVEN:** Eric Williams resurfaces — Reaper-form or otherwise — and commits an atrocity Simon could plausibly have prevented or whose victim is someone Simon cares for.

**EXPECT:** the sibling enmeshment scripted in §1 reactivating in full. Simon will refuse to kill Eric, regardless of provocation. He will refuse to let other Avengers kill Eric. He will physically interpose. After the immediate crisis, he will retrieve Eric's body if dead, attempt rehabilitation if alive, and absorb a degree of personal guilt that no observer would assign him. He cannot bury this brother cleanly because Eric is the proof of the family wound — the Williams family produced one obvious failure (Simon, by the original metric) and one obvious monster (Eric, by any metric), and Simon's heroism is in part the argument that the family was not damned. Eric's continued existence is necessary to that argument; Eric's death forecloses it. He will mourn the Reaper as if mourning himself.

### B.4 — Betrayal By A Director, Producer, or Hollywood Patron

**GIVEN:** he is publicly fired, recast, replaced by CGI, or has a film he committed to taken from him.

**EXPECT:** outsized reaction badly disguised as professionalism. The Hollywood career is genuine sublimation (§3) — it is the channel through which the performance-of-self has socially-sanctioned outlet. Cutting that channel does not just wound vanity; it removes a regulator. Expect: a magnanimous public statement, a much less magnanimous round of phone calls to representation, and a 1–3 week vanity-injury period during which he will accept inappropriate roles (a villain in a project beneath his level; a cameo as himself in something cynical) to reassert visibility. He will also be unusually present at Avengers functions during this window — the second mirror substitutes when the first goes dark.

### B.5 — A Rival Claims the Wonder Man Identity

**GIVEN:** a duplicate, a successor, a legacy character, or a hostile impostor adopts the name and image.

**EXPECT:** he will not respond from strength. He will respond from the suspicion he has carried since the Vision template revelation — that the name and the role are detachable from him, that "Wonder Man" is a costume any sufficiently ionic energy-being could wear, that he is the original of nothing. Expect either (a) abrupt name-abandonment and a months-long civilian period, or (b) a televised confrontation that goes worse than he expected. The middle path — quiet legal/Avengers-mediated resolution — is the least likely because it does not address the underlying threat, which is metaphysical rather than legal.

---

## C. THE TEMPTATION BAND

### C.1 — Offered Power By A Patron

**GIVEN:** a figure of charisma and apparent generosity offers Simon an upgrade, a stabilization, a "cure" for ionic drift, or restoration of a lost capability.

**EXPECT:** longer hesitation than a more centered hero would require. He will not say yes immediately; the Zemo memory (§1) is alive enough that a direct repeat of the script is detectable to him. But he will not say no immediately either, and the duration of the not-saying-no is the operational variable. If the patron is articulate, frames the offer in terms of stability or worthiness rather than dominance, and is not visibly malevolent, expect him to accept some lesser version of the offer — a partial collaboration, a trial, a "let me think about it" that functions as soft acceptance. He is vulnerable to charismatic reframers. The defense against this is not warning him about the patron; it is restoring an alternate mirror (Wanda, Pym, the team) before the patron's offer becomes the primary source of being-seen.

### C.2 — Offered Restoration of Wanda

**GIVEN:** any entity — cosmic, infernal, technological — offers to give him a stable, choosing, present Wanda.

**EXPECT:** the single highest-probability ethical lapse in his future. He will say no the first time. He will say no the second time. The third iteration, particularly if framed as her choice rather than his ("she wants this; she's only waiting for you to allow it"), is the failure point. He will not torch a city for her. He will, however, withhold information from the Avengers, lie to teammates by omission, and decline to prevent a smaller harm if preventing it would foreclose the offer. The Vision-refusal arc (*West Coast Avengers* #42–45) is the floor model: jealousy rationalized as caution. The ceiling is worse. Anyone using this lever on him is using the most reliable lever that exists.

### C.3 — Offered Erasure / Oblivion

**GIVEN:** he is offered, by a credible source, the end of consciousness — final death, dissolution, the option not to reconstitute.

**EXPECT:** he will be tempted, and he will refuse, and the refusal will cost him visibly for weeks afterward. The temptation is real because the post-resurrection life has been, by his own internal accounting, a series of fragmentations. The refusal is reliable because (a) the moral floor (§5) holds that suicide-by-cosmic-offer is an abandonment of the people who would mourn him, and (b) Wanda is in the world. The cost is a depressive interval during which he will be sober, quiet, unusually present in small kindnesses, and prone to writing things down — letters, will-type documents, recorded statements — that he does not send. These documents, if ever surfaced, are the most honest material in the file.

### C.4 — Offered Leadership

**GIVEN:** he is offered command of a team, a faction, a movement.

**EXPECT:** he will accept, he will perform the role with surface competence, and he will underperform the role substantively. The Force Works leadership is the canonical exhibit. Leadership requires tolerating the team's anger at the leader; Simon cannot tolerate being the rejection-target, because the leader-position structurally generates the conditional-regard scenario that scripted his childhood. He will compensate by being too consultative, too eager to be liked, too prone to the grand gesture in lieu of the difficult call. Expect resignation within 8–18 months of taking any such position, framed as principle, actually exhaustion.

### C.5 — Offered an Audience

**GIVEN:** a media opportunity of unusual scale — talk show, awards platform, congressional testimony, livestreamed press.

**EXPECT:** he will accept and he will say more than he intended. The mirror is too large to look away from. Expect at least one quotable line that his publicist did not authorize, framed in his own narrative ("I died once, you know —" or some equivalent), and a follow-on news cycle in which he is required to clarify. He is not a careless interview by intent; he is a careless interview by structure. The audience pulls performance from him faster than judgment can govern it.

---

## D. THE WOUND BAND — Direct Touches on the Shame Core

### D.1 — Reference to the Embezzlement

**GIVEN:** any actor — journalist, antagonist, casual acquaintance — references the original Williams Innovations fraud, the conviction, or the prison sentence.

**EXPECT:** a momentary stillness, a controlled exhalation, and a deflection that lands too quickly to be unrehearsed. He has rehearsed it. The rehearsed line varies but resolves to "I paid for that, and I've spent my life trying to be worth more than that." If the reference is sustained — a piece of investigative journalism, a documentary, a court proceeding — expect 2–6 weeks of disturbance: reduced public appearances, a notable uptick in heroic visibility (overcompensation), and at least one private conversation with whichever current mirror is operative in which he asks some version of "am I still that guy? Was I ever not?" The questioner will say no. He will not be reassured. The wound does not heal because it is the foundation; healing it would require dismantling the structure built on it.

### D.2 — Comparison to Stark

**GIVEN:** he is compared, favorably or unfavorably, to Tony Stark.

**EXPECT:** the most reliable micro-tell in the file. He looks down and to the left, briefly. He smiles. He says something gracious about Stark. The graciousness is real and the wound is also real; both at once. Unfavorable comparisons cue rumination lasting hours; favorable comparisons cue suspicion lasting days ("they only said that because Stark wasn't in the room"). He cannot metabolize being measured against Stark because Stark is the man whose company destroyed his father's, who succeeded at the role Simon failed at, and who — to add the unbearable inch — became a hero too. There is no axis on which Simon outranks Stark by the metric Simon was raised on. He has built an entire alternate-metric life and the Stark comparison collapses it back to the original ruler.

### D.3 — Comparison to The Vision

**GIVEN:** he is told, in any register, that the Vision was "more Simon than Simon," or that Wanda's love for the Vision was love for Simon's template, or that the Vision was the better man.

**EXPECT:** he will not respond in the moment. He will leave the room within a defensible interval. He will be unavailable for 12–72 hours. He will return composed and will reference the exchange exactly once, obliquely, weeks later. This wound is the deepest functional one because it cannot be argued with — the Vision *was* built from his patterns, and Wanda *did* love the Vision, and the question of whether she loved the original or the copy is unanswerable. The Vision-refusal in VisionQuest is the only act of his life he cannot redeem, because the redemption — donating the patterns, restoring the Vision — would foreclose the possibility of Wanda. He chose, and the choice is permanent, and he knows it.

### D.4 — Comparison to His Brother

**GIVEN:** anyone — antagonist or ally — frames Simon and Eric as "two sides of the same coin," "products of the same family," "destined for each other."

**EXPECT:** measured rage. Not the bravado-rage of the West Coast persona, the quieter kind. He will object precisely, articulately, and with too much heat. The objection is necessary because the comparison is partially true and he knows it: both Williams sons were inadequate to the father, both turned to crime, both transformed themselves into combat-bodies through external means, both could not let the other go. Simon's heroism is the argument that the comparison is false. Forcing the comparison forces him to defend the argument, and the defense costs him.

### D.5 — The "Are You Really Simon?" Question

**GIVEN:** the metaphysical question — whether the post-ionic, post-resurrection, post-discorporation, post-template entity is still Simon Williams of Paterson, NJ.

**EXPECT:** the question that breaks him cleanest. He has no answer. There is no answer. Asked in good faith, he will engage philosophically, perform openness, and destabilize over the following week — small ionic flares, sleep-substitute behavior (long drives, long swims), unusual phone calls to old contacts as if to verify the continuity of his social existence. Asked in bad faith by an antagonist who has clearly studied him, the question is a weapon and lands as one. Form-instability can be induced almost on demand by a sufficiently surgical version of this challenge. He should not be left alone after exposure to it. The mirror, again, is the only intervention; someone who knew him before — or who insists, with conviction, that the continuity holds — restores cohesion in a way internal resources cannot.

### D.6 — Public Exposure of a Past Failure

**GIVEN:** the Vision-refusal, the Revengers, the Force Works deaths, or another publicly-documented failure resurfaces in the news cycle, an academic study, a documentary, or a hostile actor's leak.

**EXPECT:** confession-prone behavior. He will, within days, give an interview or make a statement in which he says more than his advisors want him to say. He will frame the failure honestly. He will also frame it in a narrative arc with him as the protagonist learning, which will read to some viewers as self-serving and to others as moving. Both readings are correct. After the confession he will be unusually serviceable for 1–3 months — taking unglamorous missions, doing community work, attending team functions he would normally skip. The confession is sincere; the post-confession service is sincere; the underlying shame is undischarged and will reactivate at the next reference.

---

## E. THE COMPOUND-EVENT BAND

### E.1 — Wanda + Brother Simultaneously

**GIVEN:** an event involving Wanda (death, possession, hostility) AND Eric simultaneously.

**EXPECT:** the worst aggregate decompensation forecastable. The two organizing relationships of his life crisis at once. Expect ionic instability sufficient to require containment, judgment-impairment sufficient to require supervision, and a probable grand-gesture attempt (sacrifice, surrender, ultimatum) within 72 hours. He should not be the lead operator on the engagement. He will insist on being the lead operator. The insistence should be overridden by whoever has the standing to override him — historically Captain America, occasionally Pym, in the modern era a small handful of others.

### E.2 — Death + Audience

**GIVEN:** he dies, or is widely believed to have died, in a publicly visible event.

**EXPECT:** the resurrection — and one is statistically likely, per §2 — will be poorly managed. He will return to a public that has already mourned him, eulogized him, and assigned meaning to his death. Returning collapses that meaning. Expect: a complicated re-entry, public confusion about which version of him has returned, at least one piece of commentary suggesting the returned entity is not "really" Simon (cuing D.5), and a 3–9 month period of identity-recalibration during which his work is uneven. He will give an interview about the experience that he will later regret. He will write a memoir or treatment that he will not publish. He will be, for the duration, both more famous and less coherent than usual.

### E.3 — Betrayal + Shame-Touch

**GIVEN:** a betrayal by a trusted figure who, in the act of betraying, references the original embezzlement or the Vision-refusal as justification ("we never really trusted you because —").

**EXPECT:** the conditions for a second Revengers-pattern event. He will not act immediately. He will go quiet, he will assemble a justification framework over weeks to months, and he will eventually take a position against an institution he formerly served. The position will be articulate, partially correct, and tactically catastrophic. The intervention window is during the quiet period; once he has assembled the framework, he is committed to it for the duration of its internal coherence. The framework collapses only when an alternate mirror — almost always Wanda or a Wanda-substitute — calls him back to a different self. He will then renounce the position with the same sincerity he held it, and the renunciation will be genuine, and the susceptibility to a third iteration will remain.

---

## F. RESIDUAL FORECAST — The Throughline

Across every band above, the single most reliable prediction is this: Simon Williams under sufficient stress will do something visible, large, narratively framed, and partially regretted, in service of being seen as the man he is afraid he is not. The act will be heroic as often as it is harmful — he has died for others more than once and meant it each time (§5) — but the structure is the same in both directions. He cannot do the small, quiet, sustained thing as reliably as he can do the large gesture, because the small thing is not witnessed, and unwitnessed action does not register on his internal accounting as having occurred.

The handler, ally, or therapist who understands this manages him by ensuring the small things are seen — by him, by a mirror, by a record — so that the large gesture is not the only available proof of self. This is the operational implication of the entire profile. He needs witnesses for the ordinary, or he will manufacture occasions for the extraordinary, and the extraordinary occasions are where he is most dangerous to himself and to others.

The wound does not close. The forecast assumes it never will. The model is built on the assumption that the wound is the engine, and the engine is the man, and the man — with all his fragmentation and all his sincerity — is, on the balance of his life, worth keeping in the field.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM
## Subject: Simon Williams / Wonder Man

*Orientation note: This compendium is constructed for protective and benevolent-handler use — to know where the man can be reached, where he can be steadied, and where, in the wrong hands, he can be turned. Every lever documented here has been pulled in canon, often more than once. The patterns are stable enough to predict, granular enough to time.*

---

## I. THE FOUNDATIONAL WOUNDS (Strata)

Before tactics, the substrate. Four wounds lie underneath every lever; nearly all subsequent pressure points are local expressions of one of these.

**Wound 1 — The Inadequate Heir.** Sanford Williams's company, lost; Eric Williams's dominance, conceded; Tony Stark's market, surrendered. The original embezzlement was not greed; it was a son scrambling to preserve the appearance that he had not failed his father. This wound is the deepest because it predates the ionic body and therefore cannot be repaired by anything the ionic body achieves. Any heroism is, internally, a delayed audit on whether he would have measured up if he'd been left alone.

**Wound 2 — The Coerced Villain.** Zemo bought him, costumed him, aimed him. Simon's first appearance as a "hero" was as a trojan horse he himself had agreed to be. He turned on the betrayal, but he had agreed to the betrayal first. He cannot tell the story of his origin without telling the story of his complicity.

**Wound 3 — The Dead Man Walking.** He died and woke up. The interval between is a hole in his autobiography. Every subsequent death — and there have been several — re-perforates it. The body has been reconstituted; the continuity has not.

**Wound 4 — The Borrowed Self.** His brain patterns built the Vision. His powers were given by an enemy. His face is a screen-actor's. His ongoing existence has, in some periods, depended on Wanda's calling. There is no layer of his identity that originated entirely in him, and he knows it.

Every lever below routes back to one or more of these four.

---

## II. APPROACH PROTOCOLS — HOW TO REACH HIM

### 1. The opening register

Address him by first name early. *Simon* lands; *Williams* is what the warden said; *Wonder Man* is what the call-sheet says; *Mr. Williams* is what the prosecutor said. The first name is the part of him that nobody has ever rewritten, and using it signals — without his having to ask — that you are speaking to the man rather than the asset.

### 2. The seating and staging

He calibrates rooms cinematically. He will read sight-lines, lighting, and exits the way an actor reads a set. To put him at ease: do not stage the meeting. Sit at an angle rather than across; ambient light rather than overhead; no recording devices visible (he will perform to them whether he means to or not). Avoid mirrors in his eyeline — not for vanity reasons but because mirrors invite him to check whether he is still solid, and the question, once posed, is destabilizing.

### 3. The opening minute

He scans for whether you have read him correctly. The wrong opening is *I'm a fan of your work* (he hears: you have only seen the persona). The wrong opening is *I read the file* (he hears: you have only seen the case). The right opening acknowledges that there are several Simons and that you do not assume you know which one is in the room. *I'm glad you came in. How are you arriving today?* — almost clinical, but it gives him permission to choose his register rather than guess yours.

### 4. The conversational floor

He is verbally agile and will fill silence with quips when uncertain. Do not punish the quips; do not reward them either. Receive them flatly, then return to the substantive thread. The quips will thin within ten minutes if they are neither praised nor scolded. Underneath them is the actual man, who is more articulate and more careful than he lets people see.

### 5. The trust accelerants

- Naming Hank Pym as someone you respect — *without* a "despite everything" caveat — opens him faster than any other reference. Pym is the proof-text that Simon's loyalty is real; honoring Pym honors that proof.
- Acknowledging that the Avengers have not always handled him well. He does not require you to agree with the Revengers; he requires you not to pretend that nothing was ever done to him.
- Treating the acting career as a genuine vocation rather than a costume break. He has thought about craft; ask him about it once and listen.

### 6. The trust killers

- Calling the ionic form a "condition," a "gift," or "your power-set." It is his body. Refer to it as such.
- Comparing him favorably to the Vision. He will smile and never trust you again.
- Asking what it was like to die. He will answer; he will not return.
- Bringing up the embezzlement before he does. If he raises it, you may follow. If you raise it, you have told him you are running a case.

---

## III. CALMING PROTOCOLS — HOW TO STEADY HIM

### 1. Recognizing decompensation in progress

Early signs, in approximate order of escalation:

1. **Verbal density increases.** Quip rate rises; sentences shorten. He is regulating with talk.
2. **Tactile self-checking.** Touches his own forearm, the back of his neck, his sternum. He is confirming form. The gesture is unconscious and reliable.
3. **Eye-color saturation deepens.** The ionic red intensifies; this is involuntary and precedes any verbal admission of distress by several minutes.
4. **Heat signature rises** at the hands and along the jawline. Detectable to touch; readable visually as a faint shimmer in cold air.
5. **Postural stiffening, then theatricality.** Stands when he need not; declaims when he could simply speak.
6. **Edge-blur at the silhouette** — the outline of his body softens against the background. This is the last stable warning; flares follow within minutes.

### 2. The grounding sequence

If captured early (stages 1–3), the steadying intervention is simple and does not require physical contact:

- **Lower your own volume.** He matches.
- **Lengthen your own sentences.** He matches.
- **Sit, if you are standing.** He will sit.
- **Refer to a third thing** — a specific object in the room, a small concrete fact, a shared memory of a person you both know. Pull his attention out of the recursive interior loop and onto a stable external referent. The third thing reconstitutes the field he can locate himself in.

### 3. The advanced grounding

If captured at stages 4–6 (somatic destabilization underway):

- **Do not touch him without warning.** Heat is real and he cannot always modulate it; more importantly, an unexpected touch confirms the unreality fear (someone is verifying whether he is solid; therefore he might not be).
- **Name what is happening, neutrally.** *Your hands are warm. Your edges are softening. You are still here.* The third sentence is the operative one; the first two earn the right to say it.
- **Anchor him in chosen identity, not powers.** Not *you're Wonder Man, you can handle this.* Rather: *you're the one who stood with Hank when nobody else did.* Powers are borrowed; that act was his.
- **If Wanda is safe, available, and willing**, her voice over a line will reconstitute him faster than any other intervention. This is operationally true and ethically fraught; see §VII.

### 4. The aftercare

Post-flare, he will be ashamed. The shame is itself a destabilizer; do not leave him in it alone. The correct posture is matter-of-fact: a glass of water, a remark about the room, a question about something unrelated. Treat the episode the way one treats a friend's nosebleed — acknowledged, cleaned up, not made into a chapter. He will be grateful in a way he cannot say.

---

## IV. PERSUASION VECTORS — HOW TO MOVE HIM

### 1. The narrative frame

Simon thinks in stories with himself as protagonist whose worth is being adjudicated. To persuade him toward an action, situate the action inside a story whose moral center he can occupy. *We need you to do X* lands weakly. *This is the kind of thing the man who turned on Zemo would do* lands hard — perhaps too hard; it can be used cynically and he will eventually notice. The honest version is to describe the situation in narrative terms and let him cast himself.

### 2. The loyalty channel

He is movable by the suffering of specific persons more reliably than by abstract stakes. *Thousands will die* is statistical and he will engage it intellectually. *This one person, whom you know, will be left alone* is operational and he will move. Name the person; give the person a face; let him imagine the absence his presence prevents.

### 3. The redemption ledger

Every act of help is, internally, a credit against the original criminal failure. He is not fully aware that he is keeping this ledger, but he is. Framing an ask as *this is the kind of help that would not have been possible if you had not become what you are* converts the ionic body from a curse to an instrument and converts the original failure into the precondition of the present good. Use sparingly; it is potent and partially manipulative.

### 4. What does not work

- Appeals to status, rank, or formal authority. He has been outranked by everyone his whole life and stopped responding to it years ago.
- Appeals to money. Wealth is not a lever; he has had it, lost it, regained it, and does not organize around it.
- Threats of exposure. There is nothing he has done that has not already been published in some form; the worst is already in the open.
- Flattery about his power. He distrusts it because he distrusts the power; the praise lands as evidence you have not understood.

### 5. What works against him (to be guarded, not used)

- Reframing his hesitation as cowardice. He will move to disprove it, often into a fight he should have declined. Antagonists have used this; the post-resurrection death-phobia arc is the textbook case.
- Implying he is less real than the Vision. He will overcompensate, often into the precise behavior he has sworn to avoid.
- Suggesting Wanda would have preferred a different version of him. The injury is so deep that he will act, and the action will be regrettable.

---

## V. PROVOCATION TRIGGERS — WHAT BREAKS HIM

A complete inventory of the buttons. Documented here so that allies know what to avoid and protectors know what to watch for.

### 1. The comparison triad

**Stark.** Mentioning Stark's industrial success in proximity to Williams Innovations activates the original wound. He will absorb a single reference; sustained or pointed comparisons produce visible affect within minutes.

**The Vision.** Any framing that treats the Vision as the "real" Simon, the "improved" Simon, or the version Wanda chose. He has decades of practice masking the reaction; the mask is not airtight.

**Eric / the Grim Reaper.** The brother is the deepest of the three because the rivalry is constitutive — Simon cannot be Simon without being the inadequate younger brother. Even posthumous references to Eric reach him.

### 2. The fraud channel

Any implication that the heroic identity is a costume over the criminal. Phrasing like *people forget where you came from* will be received as a threat whether one is intended or not. The embezzlement is not the secret; the live wire is the suggestion that the embezzlement is the truth and the rest is performance.

### 3. The ontological challenge

Direct questions about whether he is the original man — *are you the same Simon Williams who* — destabilize disproportionately. He has no good answer; the question, posed seriously, forces him to confront the absence of one. Use of this question by adversaries is documented (in his own internal monologue across multiple Englehart/Byrne issues) to produce hours of subsequent dysfunction.

### 4. The Wanda variables

The full set:
- Her safety in doubt: high motivation, low judgment. He will move toward her at the expense of every other consideration.
- Her affection withdrawn or directed elsewhere: protracted depressive-spectrum decompensation, eventually expressing as grievance.
- Her stability in doubt: he organizes a crusade. The Revengers arc is the cleanest example.
- Her presence in a scene without acknowledgment of him: a small wound but a chronic one; accumulates.

### 5. The audience channel

Public ridicule reaches him in a way private criticism does not. A bad press cycle around the acting career produces measurable behavioral changes — louder costumes, larger gestures, ill-advised statements. Adversaries with media access have more leverage on him than adversaries with weapons.

### 6. The death-adjacent
