Imagery, mention, or threat of dissolution, discorporation, the gap, the dark, the silence between deaths. The post-resurrection arc is the proof-text; the sensitization is permanent. Even oblique references — *you've been quiet, where did you go* — can produce intrusive memory.

### 7. The conscience trap

He cannot be talked into killing — but he can be talked into a fight whose only resolution is killing, and then he will be destroyed by the result. Adversaries who maneuver him into a binary between "kill or be defeated" exploit a real structural vulnerability. The Reaper used this for years.

---

## VI. PREDICTION MODELS — WHAT HE WILL DO

### 1. Under acute physical threat

He will engage, hesitate at the decisive moment, recover, and prevail more often than not — but the hesitation is reliable and timeable. Adversaries who know about it have approximately one to two seconds of asymmetric advantage at the inflection point of any fight. Allies should position to cover the gap.

### 2. Under accusation of moral failure

Predictable sequence: (1) defensive quip, (2) verbose self-justification, (3) silence, (4) days or weeks of withdrawal, (5) ostentatious corrective act. The corrective act is sincere but often disproportionate — he overpays the debt because he does not know how to pay it exactly. Protectors should intercept between stages 4 and 5.

### 3. Under loss of Wanda

He will not retaliate against Wanda; he will retaliate against whatever framework he holds responsible for her loss. After the original Vision triangulation, the framework was himself (the Vision-template refusal, the guilt). After Disassembled and the long arc following, the framework became the Avengers (the Revengers). The displacement is reliable; predict the direction by identifying which framework he can plausibly blame.

### 4. Under prolonged stability

He becomes restless. Long quiet periods produce minor self-sabotage — bad scripts accepted, public statements regretted, romantic entanglements pursued and dropped. He is not built for peace; the substrate is too anxious. Protective management of long stable periods is more important than crisis intervention; the crises are predictable but the slow drift is where the next crisis is seeded.

### 5. Under offered redemption by a charismatic figure

Highest-risk scenario. He is precisely the kind of man who can be re-recruited by a Zemo-equivalent — anyone who offers him a story in which his powers serve a clear moral purpose and his existence is finally vindicated. He has the discernment to refuse the obvious version; he is vulnerable to a sophisticated one. Watch for new mentors, new ideologies, new framings of his history. The Revengers were a self-recruitment along these lines; an external recruiter with similar narrative gifts is the worst-case scenario.

### 6. Under offered self-knowledge

If a figure approaches him with a credible account of who he actually is — not as praise, not as accusation, but as a careful reading — he will at first resist and then attach with intensity. This is the lever a therapist could use ethically and a manipulator could use catastrophically. The signature of the manipulative version is that the account is too flattering, arrives too quickly, and asks for something soon after.

---

## VII. THE WANDA VECTOR — DEDICATED SECTION

She is too large a variable to scatter through other sections.

**The structure.** Wanda is, in his interior architecture, the only reliable mirror. He does not love her as one of several primary relationships; he loves her as the relational object around which the others are arranged. This is not healthy and he half-knows it; he has tried to work around it and has not succeeded.

**The operational implications.** Anyone who can route a message through Wanda has more access to Simon than anyone who cannot. Anyone who threatens Wanda has more leverage on Simon than any other threat. Anyone who claims her affection without his — including, historically, the Vision — produces in him a slow, structural injury that surfaces in unpredictable downstream behavior.

**The protective protocols.** 
- Wanda should never be used as a tool to move him, even in good causes. The use is too potent to remain ethical for long. The temptation, for handlers, is severe; the discipline against it must be deliberate.
- Wanda should be kept informed of his condition, not because she owes him anything, but because she is the only person whose voice can predictably reconstitute him in extremis. This is a fact, not an obligation. She is entitled to decline; he is entitled to a contingency that does not depend on her.
- He should be helped, slowly and across years, to develop a second anchor — Pym, when Pym is well; the work, when the work is real; the team, when the team has earned it. The goal is not to replace her but to ensure he does not literally cease to exist if she is unavailable. The Busiek-era discorporation is the warning that this is not metaphorical.

**The risk profile.** If Wanda is ever turned against him by an adversary — convinced of a false account of his conduct, manipulated into a public rejection — the resulting decompensation would likely be the worst event in his clinical history. Mitigation requires that her communications with him be, to the extent ethical, verifiable as actually hers. He has been fooled by impostors before; he is more vulnerable to a Wanda-shaped lie than to any other category of deception.

---

## VIII. THE BROTHER VECTOR

Eric is dead, often, and rarely stays dead. The relationship is therefore live whether or not the brother is presently alive.

**The active leverage** — used historically by the Grim Reaper and available to any sufficiently informed antagonist:
- Framing Simon as the soulless one. Eric's "you're not really my brother, you're a thing wearing his face" is the precise ontological challenge described above, delivered by the one person whose accusation Simon cannot dismiss.
- Demanding Simon prove his humanity by killing. The bind: refusing proves nothing, complying destroys the identity being proven.
- Holding Avengers hostage to a fraternal demand. Simon will negotiate when he should not; will delay when he should act; will hesitate at the decisive moment more reliably here than anywhere else.

**The protective protocols.**
- Do not let Simon handle Eric alone, ever, regardless of how confident he sounds.
- Do not let Simon be the one to deliver the killing blow if it comes to that. He will recover from grief; he will not recover from being the one. Other Avengers should pre-arrange to absorb the act if it becomes unavoidable.
- After every Reaper incident, mandatory decompression with a trusted figure (Pym, when possible; Wanda, when appropriate). The pattern of Simon disappearing alone after these encounters has produced two of his worst subsequent decisions.

---

## IX. THE PERFORMANCE VECTOR

The acting career is, on balance, healthy — a real sublimation of grandiosity into a structured craft. But it carries specific vulnerabilities.

**The screen-self bleed.** Sustained performance of a role produces, in him, transient adoption of its affect. Long shoots leave residues. Handlers and friends should monitor what he is currently filming; a violent role produces a more volatile Simon for the duration. Romantic roles produce a more vulnerable one.

**The public-image dependence.** Press cycles, reviews, social-media chatter. He claims to ignore them; he reads them. A coordinated reputational attack would reach him within hours and degrade him within days. Information-environment protection is a real operational concern.

**The audience as ersatz parent.** A full house, a good review, a fan's sincere recognition — these reach him in the parental register that Sanford Williams never filled. Cynical actors (literal or figurative) who manufacture this attention can recruit him with it. Healthy associates who provide steady, modest, honest recognition are doing genuine clinical work whether they know it or not.

---

## X. CONTAINMENT PROTOCOLS (Worst Case)

In the event of catastrophic destabilization — uncontrolled ionic discharge, ideological turn into hostile action, identity collapse:

1. **Do not lead with force.** He has died enough times to be unimpressed and unwell enough to be unpredictable.
2. **Establish an audio channel before a visual one.** A familiar voice — Wanda's if available, Pym's as a strong second, Beast's as a third — reaches him through the noise of his own form.
3. **Name him, not the alias.** *Simon* repeatedly, calmly, until response. This may take minutes.
4. **Anchor with concrete memory, not principle.** *Remember the diner on the lot, the one with the bad coffee, where Hank told you* — specifics he cannot have rehearsed for. The specifics pull him back into a self continuous with the one in the memory.
5. **Containment, not capture.** A space he can dissipate in safely; a perimeter that does not feel like a cage. Cages confirm the worst story he tells himself.
6. **Wait.** Almost every Simon Williams crisis has resolved itself, eventually, into return and apology. Patience is itself a tactic.

---

## XI. THE PROTECTIVE BOTTOM LINE

He is a profoundly accessible man. Almost everything in this compendium can be used against him by someone willing to study him for an afternoon. The fact that he has not been ruined more often than he has is a testament to two things: a genuine moral floor that asserts itself at the last possible moment, and the steady presence of a small number of people — Pym chief among them, Wanda inevitably, the Avengers institutionally if imperfectly — who have refused, over decades, to use the levers they could pull.

The protective task is not to seal the vulnerabilities. They cannot be sealed; they are constitutive. The task is to ensure that the people in proximity to him are the kind who will not pull, that the people who would pull are kept out of proximity, and that when he destabilizes — and he will, again — there is a voice he trusts on the line and a room he can re-form in without being seen by anyone who will publish what they saw.

He is, in the end, a man whose existence has been written by other hands so many times that the kindest thing one can do is to let him, for stretches, write a sentence himself. Most of the leverage in this file consists of refraining.

— UATU


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — Simon Williams / Wonder Man

*The positive side of the ledger. Compiled in the spirit of total understanding: what this man has, what he can do, what has kept him on the side of the angels across sixty years of in-universe pressure that has broken people with sturdier foundations. Read against the rest of the file, the ledger is larger than the deficits suggest — which is itself the central fact about him.*

---

## 1. THE MORAL FLOOR

The single most important asset in the entire file, and the one most often underestimated by hostile observers because it is quiet, is that Simon Williams has a moral floor he has never crossed and, on the available evidence, *cannot* cross.

**The Zemo turn (Avengers #9) is the founding datum.** A man who had been failed by his father's shadow, surpassed by his brother, ruined by Stark, humiliated in court, imprisoned, and then offered godhood by the man who had defeated the Avengers — turned on his benefactor inside a single afternoon. He had no reason to. The Avengers were strangers to him; Zemo had given him a body that would not die. He flipped because the operation required him to be the kind of person he could not stand to be. This is the entire character in one act, and it has held for six decades of escalating provocation.

**Sub-data points reinforcing the floor:**

- Across roughly twenty years of in-story conflict with the Grim Reaper — a brother who has murdered innocents, raised the dead, and tortured Simon personally — Simon has refused to kill him. The refusal is sustained against fatigue, against tactical sense, against the urging of teammates. When Eric finally dies, Simon buries him.
- During the Hank Pym disgrace arc, when Pym had been court-martialed, divorced, and abandoned by virtually every reasonable colleague, Simon stayed. The friendship had no upside; staying cost him standing. He stayed anyway.
- Repeated, documented willingness to die: the original Zemo sacrifice, the Kree action in the Force Works run, multiple lesser instances. Each was meant. He is not a man who performs sacrifice; he performs many things, but not that.
- The reluctance to kill is *generalized*, not Wanda-adjacent or brother-adjacent. Across his entire combat record, kills are vanishingly rare and consistently followed by visible distress.

The technical name for this asset is conscience. The relevant operational fact is that it is *automatic* — not a value he has to remember in the moment, but a structural feature that asserts itself even when the rest of him is compromised. When Simon Williams is at his worst — the Revengers period, the Vision refusal — he is still operating from a sincere (mistaken) moral argument, not from indifference. The floor does not lift.

## 2. THE CAPACITY FOR SHAME

This sounds like a deficit and is in fact the second largest asset on the page.

Simon is exquisitely vulnerable to shame. He carries the original embezzlement live, decades after it should have faded; he carries the Vision refusal as a permanent splinter; he came back to the Avengers from the Revengers in part because he could not metabolize what he had done. From a surveillance-and-understanding standpoint, this is the precondition for everything good about him. Subjects without functional shame do not return, do not apologize, do not repair. Simon returns. Simon apologizes — clumsily, often after the damage is done, but genuinely. Simon repairs.

The shame is also *granular*. He does not feel a generalized "I am bad" cloud in the manner of a depressive subject; he feels specific shames attached to specific acts and specific people, and he can be moved by being shown the specific act. This makes him reachable by anyone — Wanda, Pym, an audience, a therapist who never sees him — who can name the thing accurately. Vague moralizing slides off; specific recognition lands.

## 3. RETURN AND REPAIR — THE NON-PERMANENT DEFECTION PATTERN

Across the entire career, *every* defection has been temporary.

- Zemo: hours.
- The Revengers crusade: a publication arc, then return.
- Each ideological turn in the Remender and post-Remender period: oscillation, not commitment.
- Every romantic withdrawal from Wanda and re-approach: cyclical, not terminal.

This pattern is durable and predictive. Simon does not have the constitution for permanent enmity. He can be radicalized briefly; he cannot stay radicalized. The same identity-instability that makes him vulnerable to bad reframing makes him equally vulnerable to good reframing, and the moral floor ensures the eventual direction of drift. As an asset, this means he is essentially impossible to lose permanently. As a tactical fact, it means any handler or ally can write off a Simon defection on a clock measured in weeks-to-months, not years.

## 4. PHYSICAL CAPABILITY — THE INSTRUMENT

The body is, by any honest accounting, one of the more formidable instruments on the planet. The ledger here is undersold in his own self-presentation, which is part of why opponents miscalibrate.

- **Strength:** sustained Class-100 capability — the strict upper tier of unaugmented metahuman lift. Demonstrated against the Hulk, against the Wrecking Crew, against Kree warships. He underperforms this ceiling routinely because he does not fully trust the body; the ceiling is nonetheless real.
- **Durability:** functionally invulnerable to conventional and most unconventional force. He has walked out of detonations, orbital reentry-class impacts, and direct beam weapons.
- **Flight:** developed post-resurrection, fully under conscious control, sustainable indefinitely.
- **Metabolism:** no requirement for food, water, oxygen, or sleep. Operationally this is enormous — no logistical tail, no environmental constraint, no biological clock degrading performance.
- **Lifespan:** indefinite. Demonstrated across multiple in-universe decades without aging.
- **Reconstitution:** documented across multiple death events. The body comes back. The instrument is, in the literal sense, hard to destroy.
- **Ionic discharge:** late-career capability — direct energy projection, area effect, with destructive potential well beyond the strength baseline. Underused, because Simon dislikes the implications of it (it is the most visibly "not-human" thing he does).

The asset is the body; the meta-asset is that he treats it cautiously and ethically. A subject with this instrument and a worse conscience would be a planetary problem. Simon is not a planetary problem.

## 5. COMBAT EXPERIENCE — SIXTY YEARS OF SCHOOLING

The dossier should not underweight that this man has been in the field, at the high end, since 1964 (in-universe time-compressed but operationally comparable to a multi-decade veteran). He has fought:

- The Masters of Evil in multiple incarnations.
- The Wrecking Crew, the Lethal Legion, Ultron in several iterations, Kang, the Kree, the Skrulls, Galactus-adjacent threats, the Grim Reaper's animated dead.
- His own teammates, under various manipulations and during the Revengers period.
- A long roster of street-level and cosmic-level opposition.

He has fought as a solo, as an Avenger (East and West), as a Force Works principal, and as the leader of his own faction. He has worked under Cap's command, under Iron Man's, under Hawkeye's (West Coast), and under his own. The tactical vocabulary is enormous, even if his preferred mode (front-line bruiser with selective restraint) is narrower.

He has also been schooled in performance combat by the Hollywood career — choreography, sight-line awareness, hit-the-mark precision. This shows up in the field as a fighter who is unusually *legible*, who can be coordinated with at a glance, who instinctively occupies camera-front positions in a melee. The legibility is a team asset; it makes him an easy partner to fight beside.

## 6. THE HOLLYWOOD CAREER AS GENUINE SUBLIMATION

Treated correctly, the acting career is one of his healthier compensatory structures. It accomplishes several real things at once:

- **Channels grandiosity** into a socially sanctioned outlet. The exhibitionism that would otherwise show up as costume vanity and combat showboating is partly burned off on set.
- **Provides identity scaffolding.** A role is a temporary self with clear edges. For a subject whose self-cohesion is the central deficit, a script is a stabilizer. He knows who he is when he knows what he is supposed to say.
- **Generates income and lifestyle independence from the Avengers payroll / Stark patronage.** He is one of very few Avengers who does not financially depend on the team or on a wealthy teammate. The autonomy is real and load-bearing for self-respect.
- **Creates a non-superhero peer set.** Crew, agents, fellow performers — relationships that do not require him to be Wonder Man. The texture of normal sociality is preserved.
- **Public-facing track record of competence** outside the costume. He has been on screen, on time, hitting marks, for years. The professional reliability is documented and durable.
- **Direct rehearsal of the invulnerable persona** — performing it daily, in controlled circumstances, with feedback. This is, accidentally, a kind of exposure therapy for the death-phobia.

The career is brittle in some directions (vanity, image-management) but it is, in the asset column, real work that has held.

## 7. THE RELATIONAL ASSETS

Despite the relational deficits cataloged elsewhere, Simon has, by veteran-superhero standards, an unusually rich and durable bench of human attachments.

**Wanda Maximoff** — even granting all the complications, she has loved him, returned to him, summoned him from non-existence, and remained a stable referent across forty years of in-universe time. Whatever else this relationship is, it is also an enormous reservoir of regard from one of the most powerful beings in the setting. She has called him back from dissipation more than once. As an asset in the strict sense: he has someone who will not let him not-exist.

**Hank Pym** — the friendship has held through Pym's worst periods and Simon's. It is reciprocal: Pym has reciprocated the loyalty in Simon's bad periods. It is one of the few relationships in either man's life characterized by mutual non-judgment.

**The Vision** — even through the rivalry, even through the engram refusal, there is a relationship here that has survived being literally impossible. They are family, in the only sense the word admits. Over time, the relationship has been re-established with caveats. The capacity to maintain it at all, given the structural ugliness, is itself a strength.

**Eric / Grim Reaper** — paradoxically, an asset. The refusal to abandon his brother, even at the cost of repeated personal danger, is a moral data point that organizes the rest of his self-image. He gets to be the brother who tried. This is psychologically load-bearing.

**The Avengers, as institution** — he has been a member of the East, the West, the Mighty, and adjacent rosters. Even after the Revengers, they took him back. The institution functions for him as a family-of-origin replacement and an anchoring social structure. He has somewhere to return to.

**Beast, Tigra, Hawkeye, Cap, the Wasp** — second-tier friendships of substantial duration. The Tigra connection in particular has been periodically romantic and consistently warm. He is not a man without friends.

The pattern: he has more relational capital than a fragile-identity subject usually retains, because the loyalty mechanism is one of his stablest features and other people respond to it.

## 8. INTELLIGENCE, LEGIBLE AND LATERAL

He is not Stark and does not pretend to be — but the original Williams Innovations inheritance presupposes that he had the technical literacy to attempt running an industrial firm. He failed at *competing with Stark*, which is not the same as being non-functional. Inside the Avengers, he reads tactical situations adequately, holds command credibly in Force Works (whatever the run's quality), and processes briefings without difficulty.

His more interesting cognitive asset is **narrative intelligence** — he understands stories, characters, dramatic structure, audience response. This is a real and useful form of cognition. In a Hollywood meeting, in a press appearance, in a public-relations crisis for the team, in reading the emotional shape of an opponent's grievance — he is unusually good. It is the same faculty that makes him vulnerable to bad framings; it is also the faculty that lets him connect with a frightened civilian, a wavering teammate, an estranged brother, in language they recognize.

He is **emotionally literate** about other people in a way many of his strongest teammates are not. He sees when Pym is collapsing. He sees when Wanda is being managed. He sees the human moment in a crisis. This is rare in the cohort.

## 9. THE PERFORMER'S TOOLKIT

Discrete capabilities accumulated from the acting career and durable across contexts:

- Voice control — projection, register, pacing — usable in command, de-escalation, public address.
- Physical poise and blocking instinct — knows where his body is in a space and how it is being read.
- Memorization and recall under pressure — he can hold a brief verbatim.
- Cold-read capability — he reads a room.
- Public-speaking comfort — press conferences, hearings, civilian-facing crises.
- Camera awareness — knows how the moment will look. This is double-edged but as an asset is real: superhero work is partly public theater, and he is one of the few practitioners who understands this consciously.

## 10. RESILIENCE STRUCTURES

The dossier should be honest that Simon's resilience is *unusual* given the load he has carried. The list of catastrophes — repeated deaths, identity dissolution, the loss of his brother, the loss of Wanda twice, the Revengers shame, the discorporation period, the engram-template realization — would have ended most subjects. He is still in the field, still functional, still on the side he started on.

Mechanisms underlying that:

- **Sublimation through work.** Acting gigs, Avengers duty, the routine of being looked at competently doing something. He uses scheduled performance as a stabilizer.
- **Humor as containment.** The quipping is a real regulator. It allows affect to discharge in small increments instead of accumulating to flare-threshold.
- **Capacity for solitude when needed.** Despite the dependency profile, he can absorb stretches alone (the discorporation period, between-projects downtime). The solitude is anxious but tolerable.
- **Aesthetic anchoring.** He has taste — in scripts, in company, in costume, in domestic environment. Aesthetic preferences are a low-cost self-locating mechanism for a fragile identity, and he uses them.
- **Body as ritual.** Even without metabolic need, he keeps routines — sleep approximation, gym appearances, meals taken socially — that hold the human shape together by behavior. The performance of normal life is itself a stabilizer.
- **Mirrors curated, not avoided.** He has assembled — consciously or not — a set of regular reflectors (Wanda, Pym, his agent, a few crew, certain teammates) who give him back a stable image. Functionally, an outpatient support system.
- **Reachability.** He answers when called. He can be talked to. He can be talked *down*. This is itself a resilience asset because it means the rest of the world can intervene in his crises.

## 11. SOBRIETY

Across the entire canon, in a milieu (Hollywood plus superhero PTSD) that would predict heavy substance involvement, the record is conspicuously clean. Whether the ionic metabolism precludes intoxication or he chooses abstinence is partially ambiguous; functionally, he is sober. This removes an enormous class of failure modes that would otherwise be live: there are no benders, no DUIs, no enabling relationships built around use, no withdrawal-driven decisions. For a subject of his profile this is a quietly massive asset.

## 12. FINANCIAL AND LOGISTICAL INDEPENDENCE

He owns property in Los Angeles. He has agent representation, a working career, residuals, public Q-rating. He is not a financial dependent of the Avengers or of any patron. He can pay his own way through a bad year. He has a phone people answer. He can get on a plane, or fly under his own power. For a superhero subject this baseline is less universal than one might assume, and it underwrites his capacity to make moral choices that cost him standing — he can afford to.

## 13. THE ASSET THAT IS THE SUM OF THE OTHERS

If the file had to name the single overarching resilience factor, it is this: **Simon Williams is a man whom decent people consistently choose to help.**

He gets called back from dissipation. He gets covered for in his worst hours. He gets re-admitted to teams that should not re-admit him. He gets forgiven by people who do not need to forgive him. Wanda summons him. Pym stays close. The Avengers reopen the door. Crew rehire him. Audiences keep buying tickets.

This is not luck and it is not charm in the manipulative sense. It is the cumulative return on the moral floor, the genuine loyalty, the capacity for shame, the reachability, and the sincerity. Other people recognize, correctly, that he is worth the effort. The recognition is the asset that has kept him alive — in every available sense of the word — through a sequence of trials that the file's deficit columns suggest should have ended him several times over.

The man underneath the borrowed identities is, on the evidence, a person other people want to keep in the world. That is, by any reasonable accounting, the most durable resource he has.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

## Simon Williams / Wonder Man

---

## 1. The Master Pattern

Simon Williams does not break the way most superhumans break. He does not snap into rage, dissociate into a fugue, or retreat into catatonia in the dramatic single-event sense — though he has done all three at least once. What he does, structurally and repeatedly across sixty years of canon, is **dissolve at the seams of a borrowed self**. His decompensations are not eruptions from a stable core; they are the failures of a held performance. When the costume of the moment — son, brother, hero, lover, stuntman, ideologue — can no longer be sustained against contradictory evidence, the man underneath does not emerge. There is no man underneath in the conventional sense; there is ionic energy in a human-shaped habit, and the habit slips.

The decompensation pattern is therefore best understood as **a cascading loss of cohesion across three coupled systems** that, in a less unusual subject, would be independent variables: somatic integrity (does the body hold its form), identity coherence (does the self hold its story), and moral orientation (does the conscience hold its line). In Simon these three are mechanically linked. Affect loads onto identity; identity loads onto ionic stability; ionic instability loads back onto affect through the terror of dissolution. The loop is closed and reinforcing. Once it begins, it will run until an external mirror intervenes — most reliably Wanda, secondarily a peer whose regard he cannot dismiss (Pym, the Beast in certain runs, occasionally Steve Rogers), tertiarily an audience.

This is the master pattern. The remainder of this section maps its stages, its precipitants, its historical exhibits, and its predictable forms.

---

## 2. The Standard Escalation Curve

Across the documentary record, Simon's decompensation follows a recognizable five-stage curve. It is not always completed; in healthier periods he arrests at stage two and self-corrects. In the worst-documented episodes (the Vision refusal, the Revengers founding, the post-Force Works discorporation) he traverses all five.

### Stage One — Mirror Disturbance

Some figure whose regard organizes him changes posture toward him. The change need not be dramatic; the system is exquisitely tuned. Wanda chooses the Vision over him. The Avengers convene without inviting him. A director recasts a part. A reviewer mocks a performance. Eric, in some incarnation, returns and accuses him of having "no soul." Tony Stark, in any room, exists.

The subjective experience at this stage is **a flicker of the embezzlement-self** — the original failed-son, surpassed-brother, exposed-fraud configuration that predates everything ionic. It is not consciously identified as such. What Simon notices is a sudden over-attention to how he is being perceived in the room, a slight delay in his own reactions, a heightened awareness of his costume, his voice, his standing.

**Observable tells at Stage One:**
- Increased self-referential speech; jokes that test the room.
- A specific habit of touching the costume's chest emblem or, in civilian dress, smoothing the lapel — a checking gesture for whether the outer presentation is still in place.
- Slight elevation of vocal performance; lines delivered as though for an audience that isn't there.
- Brief, recoverable hesitations in combat — a half-beat of looking around before engaging.
- In ionic terms: faint, transient brightening of the eyes, undetectable to non-instrumented observers.

### Stage Two — Performance Inflation

If the mirror disturbance is not repaired within a short interval — hours to days — Simon begins to **compensate by overproducing the persona currently on offer**. The vain Hollywood-action affect intensifies. The one-liners get louder and worse. He volunteers for missions in registers slightly above his actual willingness. He picks fights with low-tier opposition he can decisively beat, generating visible wins for himself in the team's sight. He may give interviews, sit for photographs, accept an endorsement he would otherwise decline. In civilian register, he over-invests in the acting career: takes a marginal role, throws a party, calls a press agent.

This stage is **highly functional from the outside**. Teammates routinely mistake it for confidence; the public reads it as charm. The subject himself reads it as recovery. It is not. It is the system loading more demand onto an already-strained mirror.

**Observable tells at Stage Two:**
- Verbal density up; pauses down.
- Increased physical occupation of space — wider stances, broader gestures, taking the central position in formations and group photographs.
- Reduced tolerance for being interrupted, particularly by the Vision, by Stark, or by anyone speaking with technical authority he does not share.
- Combat performance trends grandiose — finishing moves, called shots, throwing villains into camera-friendly geometry. A pattern noted by Hawkeye on multiple occasions in the West Coast period.
- Sleep, insofar as ionic physiology requires the analog of rest, becomes restless or skipped entirely. He paces. He rewatches his own film work — a documented private habit from the West Coast residency.

### Stage Three — Moral Reframing

This is the critical inflection. The decompensation becomes dangerous at the point where Simon begins to **construct a story** that explains the mirror's withdrawal as the mirror's fault rather than his inadequacy. The narrative gift that makes him a sincere romantic in stable periods becomes a defense mechanism under load: he is constitutionally a man who thinks in stories, and under threat he writes himself a better one.

The Vision refusal is the textbook exhibit. Wanda chooses to attempt to restore the Vision, which is to say she withdraws from Simon precisely after he believed himself chosen. Within the interval of that decompensation, he constructs the rationale: it would be unwise to donate the brain patterns; the resulting being would be a confusion; better for everyone if the Vision remains as he is. The rationale has surface coherence. It is also, transparently to every other adult present, jealousy. Simon does not see this. He cannot see it, because seeing it would return him to Stage One.

The Revengers founding is the same mechanism at institutional scale. The Avengers have failed, in his reading, to prevent or address the cascading reality-distortions surrounding Wanda. His exclusion from the inner decision-making (mirror disturbance) and his sense of unique investment in Wanda's outcome (mirror history) get reframed into an ethical position: the Avengers themselves are the destabilizing force; opposing them is the moral act.

**Observable tells at Stage Three:**
- Sudden articulacy on a topic he has previously addressed casually. He acquires positions.
- Use of categorical language ("the Avengers are," "the Vision can't be," "Wanda would never") where he previously used contingent language.
- Reduced laughter. The bravado of Stage Two thins into earnestness.
- Increased private writing or rehearsing — manifestos, in the Revengers case; speeches and declarations in earlier instances. He has been known to draft and discard.
- Avoidance of the specific persons whose regard he is rewriting his story against. He stops calling Wanda. He stops attending Avengers functions. He goes to ground in the desert house, or the Hollywood condo, depending on era.

### Stage Four — Action Under the New Frame

Simon now acts on the reframed position. The act is the catastrophe of the cycle. Refuses the brain patterns. Assembles the Revengers and attacks the mansion. Goes public with the ideological denunciation. In earlier eras: freezes at the critical moment in combat (death-phobia exhibit), or sacrifices himself in a gesture that is partly heroism and partly an exit from a situation he cannot otherwise resolve.

The Stage Four act is **always presented by Simon, to himself, as necessity**. The verbal markers are consistent across decades: *I had to. There was no choice. Someone had to say it. If not me, who.* He is not lying; he experiences the act as compelled. The defense is intellectualization in service of action — the rationale is real to him in the instant, even when, weeks later, he cannot reconstruct why it seemed sufficient.

**Observable tells at Stage Four:**
- Ionic flares synchronized to the moments of decision. The body broadcasts what the man will not yet say.
- A specific facial set documented across multiple artists' interpretations: jaw forward, mouth slightly open, eyes wide rather than narrowed — the look of a man performing certainty he does not feel.
- Rapid speech, often with rehearsed phrasing. He delivers prepared lines as though improvising.
- Inability to tolerate dissent in the moment. Teammates or opponents who try to argue him down are dismissed, sometimes physically.

### Stage Five — Form Failure

The cost of the Stage Four act is somatic and identity-level collapse. The ionic body, already strained, **loses cohesion**. In the early canon this presented as catatonia or death (the original ionic instability, the Force Works sacrifice). In later canon — after the discorporation arc retrained the body to dissipate rather than die — it presents as flares, partial dissolution, periods of energy-form existence, and reconstitution under the influence of an organizing observer, almost always Wanda.

The psychological correlate is the same dissolution at the level of self-story. He cannot maintain the rationale he just acted on. He cannot maintain the prior rationale either. He cannot retrieve a stable account of who he is, what he believes, what he was trying to do. There is documented, repeated dialogue in this state — across multiple writers — of Simon asking variants of *who am I, am I real, was that me*. The question is not rhetorical.

Recovery from Stage Five requires external reconstitution. He cannot self-rescue from this depth. A trusted mirror must address him by name, with continuity, and hold the address steady for the interval required for the form to re-cohere.

---

## 3. The Specific Precipitants

The decompensation cycle is reliably triggered by a small, well-characterized set of inputs. Any single one is sufficient under load; combinations are nearly always sufficient.

**Comparison to the three referents.** Stark, the Vision, and Eric Williams. Any explicit comparison in his presence — even casual, even favorable to him — activates the inadequacy script. The Vision case is the most exquisite: the Vision *is* a comparison to himself, the better-articulated version of his own brain patterns. Co-presence with the Vision is chronically destabilizing and Simon manages it across decades by a learned, brittle politesse that costs him visibly.

**Wanda variables.** Her absence, her presence with another, her crisis, her indifference, her unconscious need (the discorporation period). The variable is undirected; any change in her state propagates. This is the single most powerful input in the system and the most frequently exploited by canon writers when a Simon-story is desired.

**Confrontation with the embezzlement-history.** Direct reference — a journalist, an old acquaintance, a villain who has done research — produces a documented physiological reaction: brief ionic dimming, vocal pitch drop, an almost imperceptible step backward. He recovers within seconds but the rest of the conversation is conducted from a destabilized baseline.

**Public mockery.** Reviewers, comedians, social-media sentiment in modern eras. The actor-self is genuinely sublimative when reception is positive; when negative, the sublimation reverses and the underlying shame floods the costume.

**Threat of permanent death.** Not death itself — he has accepted death heroically multiple times — but the credible threat of *final* death, the version that does not resurrect. Specific antagonists who have invoked this (certain cosmic-tier opponents, certain magic-users) produce Stage One to Stage Three escalation within minutes.

**Being trusted with another's vulnerability.** Counterintuitive but documented: when Pym, in his lowest period, leaned on Simon's loyalty, Simon's *baseline* functioning improved markedly — but if the trusted person's vulnerability is then revealed to be a manipulation or a pretext, the betrayal-load on his system is disproportionate. He does not handle being used by people he has chosen to protect.

**Forced choice between two regards.** Wanda or the Avengers. The team or his brother. The role or the man. He does not metabolize forced choices well; he tends to defer, then act, then regret, in a compressed cycle that produces some of his worst decisions.

---

## 4. Failure-Mode Typology

The escalation curve produces, in the historical record, a small number of recognizable terminal forms. They are not mutually exclusive; he has manifested several in combination.

### 4.1 The Freeze

The pure death-phobia presentation. Documented primarily in the post-resurrection mid-to-late 1970s arc, with recurrences under specific threat conditions thereafter. Simon, in combat or imminent combat, locks. He sees the action; he cannot generate the motor output. The body, ionically capable of more than the situation demands, simply does not move. Teammates initially read this as cowardice and are not entirely wrong on the phenomenology, though wrong on the etiology. The freeze can last seconds or minutes; in extreme cases he has been physically removed from a battlefield by Vision or Thor.

The freeze recurs as a residual pattern. Even in his most confident eras, there are moments — usually involving energy weapons or threats of disintegration — when the body delays. He has learned to mask it with a quip or a deliberate stance shift. The mask works on most observers.

### 4.2 The Sacrifice Exit

Simon's most morally legible failure mode and the one he is most likely to reach for under pressures he cannot otherwise resolve. When the decompensation curve threatens Stage Three reframing but a battlefield is available, he will instead choose the heroic death — leap into the explosion, hold the energy, absorb the blast. The Force Works sacrifice is the archetype.

This must be assessed carefully. It is not exclusively pathological. He has died for genuine cause, with full lucidity, more than once, and the moral floor that produces these acts is real. But the pattern is also a known route out of intolerable internal states: the gesture resolves the identity question (he is a hero, definitionally, in the act of dying as one), resolves the relational question (the mirrors will mourn him, will regret him, will see him), and resolves the somatic question (the form fails on his terms rather than at someone else's hands). It is a perfectionist's suicide that is also, genuinely, a rescue. Both readings are correct simultaneously and they reinforce each other.

The post-resurrection era has complicated this exit — he knows, now, that he will come back, which both lowers the cost and changes the meaning. There is documented ambivalence in the later runs about whether his sacrifices "count" the way they used to. He raises this himself, in conversation with Pym and with Wanda, in different decades.

### 4.3 The Ideological Turn

The Revengers presentation, with antecedents in smaller scale across earlier eras. Simon constructs a categorical position — usually moral, sometimes political — that licenses behavior his prior self would have refused, and acts on it with the conviction of a man who has finally seen clearly. The position is not delusional; it has real referents (the Avengers' decisions had real costs; Wanda's destabilization was a real harm). The pathology is in the **load-bearing** of the position: it is doing work that the position cannot honestly do, namely converting his personal grievance into a public good.

The ideological turn is his most dangerous failure mode because it is the one that hurts others. The freeze hurts the mission; the sacrifice hurts him; the form-failure hurts him and frightens witnesses. The ideological turn hurts allies, in their persons and in their reputations, and is the most difficult to unwind, because the act of unwinding requires Simon to acknowledge that the position was a defense, which returns him directly to Stage One.

He has, to his credit and consistent with the substrate of decency, performed exactly this unwinding more than once. The Revengers period ended with apology and partial return. The pattern is forgivable in principle and has been forgiven in practice. It is also, as of the most recent canon, not yet exhausted.

### 4.4 Discorporation

The somatic terminal form. The body fails to hold shape. He becomes ionic energy without geometry — sometimes a glow, sometimes a voice, sometimes a presence felt by Wanda before it is seen. This is the most distinctive failure mode of the subject and arguably the most diagnostic: it is the literal exhibition of what is psychologically true about him, that he requires an organizing observer to exist as a coherent self.

The discorporation can be partial (flares, localized dissolution, an arm fading) or complete (the post-Force Works state, in which he was effectively dispersed). Reconstitution is reliably triggered by Wanda's attention; less reliably by other strong attentional sources. He has, in some periods, been able to reconstitute himself by an act of will, and the development of this capacity represents the most significant clinical improvement in his profile. It is not stable. Under sufficient load it still fails.

### 4.5 The Quiet Collapse

The least documented but most behaviorally diagnostic in stable periods. Simon, between crises, can be observed to experience small, contained decompensations that do not progress past Stage One or Two but recur with high frequency. He goes silent for a day. He cancels appointments. He sits in the screening room of whichever residence he currently occupies and runs old footage. He calls Wanda and hangs up before she answers. He works out for hours against the heavy bag in the West Coast facility, or its successor. He memorizes new material — scripts, poetry, occasionally Pym's old papers — which functions as a substitute substrate when his own self-story is thin.

These quiet collapses are the baseline of his life and the file should not understate their frequency. He is decompensating, in small doses, much of the time. He has built a functional life around managing the dosage.

---

## 5. What the Collapse Looks Like, in the Room

A trained observer in his presence during a full Stage Three-to-Five decompensation would note, in approximate order:

The voice changes register first. The performed warmth thins; the vocal placement moves higher in the chest; the cadence becomes more declarative, less responsive. He stops asking questions. He stops finishing other people's sentences with the easy banter that characterizes his stable presentation.

The eyes brighten. This is involuntary and increases roughly with affective load. In his stable state the ionic glow is suppressed to near-human appearance; in decompensation the suppression fails and the eyes read as lit from within, sometimes flickering. He is aware of this and dislikes it; in modern eras he has been known to wear tinted lenses in civilian contexts during high-load periods.

The skin temperature rises perceptibly to anyone close enough to register it. Witnesses who have embraced or restrained him during these episodes describe heat — not painful, but unmistakable, in the range of a low fever.

He occupies space differently. The expansive Stage Two posture compresses into something more guarded. He turns slightly away from the room. He stands with the dominant side back. He stops touching people, including those he habitually touches — Pym's shoulder, Wanda's hand, the Beast's arm in the runs where they were close.

Speech content shifts from narrative to declarative. He stops telling stories about himself. He starts asserting positions about others. The shift is one of the most reliable verbal markers in the file.

Motor control of fine gestures degrades subtly. A glass set down too hard. A page turned too sharply. A door closed with a touch more force than the situation requires. He is not breaking things; he is moving with the affect-loaded slightly-excessive force of a man whose body is no longer perfectly calibrated to the world it is in.

Under sufficient further load, the ionic flares become visible. Discharges at the hands, the shoulders, the back. The hair, in artists' renderings, lifts slightly. Heat distortion in the air around him. At this point any competent observer should disengage him from the situation, because the next failure point is form integrity, and form integrity loss in his presence is dangerous to bystanders as well as to him.

The terminal state, when reached, is one of three: the freeze (motor lock, eyes still open, no response), the act (the Stage Four catastrophe, performed with rehearsed certainty), or the dissolution (form failure, partial or complete, often accompanied by a final spoken phrase that is later difficult for witnesses to remember accurately).

---

## 6. Recovery Conditions

Simon's recovery profile is, structurally, the most hopeful feature of his presentation. He is not a permanent defector from any position, any team, or any relationship. He returns. The return is sometimes humiliating to him and difficult for those who must accept it, but it is reliable.

Recovery requires, at minimum: **time off the front line** (combat exposure prolongs decompensation), **a stable mirror** (Wanda is most effective; Pym is next; a trusted teammate willing to address him by his given name and his history will do), **distance from the precipitating comparison** (he cannot recover in Stark's company, in the Vision's company, or — in the bad periods — in his brother's), and **a low-stakes performative outlet** (acting work, training, even cooking, in some runs — channels for the persona that do not require him to defend a position).

Recovery is faster when **shame is met with continuity rather than absolution**. He does not need to be told he was right; he needs to be told he is still here, still known, still expected at the next briefing. The Avengers, at their best as an institution, have understood this about him and provided it. At their worst they have either over-forgiven (which fails to address the act) or under-forgiven (which compounds the shame and prolongs the cycle). The middle posture — *we know what you did; we know why; we want you back; do not do it again* — is what he requires, and it is the posture that several long-tenured teammates have learned, by trial and error, to provide.

Recovery is never complete. The substrate — the embezzlement-self, the death-phobia, the Vision-template question, the Wanda-dependence — is permanent. What changes across the historical record is not the substrate but the latency: how quickly he detects Stage One, how often he arrests at Stage Two, how rarely he reaches Stage Four. The trend, over decades, is mildly favorable. He is, by any reasonable measure, more stable in his recent decades than in his middle ones. The improvements are real and they are bought at the cost of a man who has done enormous internal work and continues to do it, mostly in private, mostly without credit, against a constitutional disadvantage that no amount of work will resolve.

The dossier records, for the avoidance of doubt, that this is itself a heroism — distinct from the heroism of the costume, and arguably more substantial. The man who manages a chronic identity-coherence deficit at the level Simon Williams manages his, while continuing to function in the most demanding theater of operations on the planet, while continuing to show up for the people he loves, while continuing to refuse, on principle, to become what was done to him — that man is doing something every day that does not have a name in the literature, because the literature does not, generally, have subjects like him to study.

The failure modes are real. They will recur. They will, in some future iteration of the cycle, cost him or someone near him something he cannot replace. This is the prediction the file is obligated to make.

The recoveries are also real. They will also recur. This is the prediction the file is permitted to make alongside it.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — SIMON WILLIAMS / WONDER MAN
## Section 6: Trajectory & Forward Assessment

---

### 6.0 Framing

A forward assessment on this subject is unusually tractable because the underlying pattern is unusually stable. Simon Williams's external life looks chaotic — career pivots, deaths, resurrections, ideological turns, costume changes, team affiliations re-shuffled every eighteen to thirty-six months — but the *generative grammar* underneath is consistent across six decades of record. He is a man who, when his mirror cracks, fragments; when a new mirror is presented, he reassembles around it; and who has now run this cycle enough times that each iteration leaves the substrate more sensitized and less elastic. Trajectory is not a question of *whether* he will cycle again. He will. The questions are: *which mirror, how violently the seam tears, and whether anyone is present to catch the reassembly.*

What follows is organized into: the dominant trend lines (what is already in motion); the medium-horizon fork points (the next five to fifteen years of subjective time, where the road actually branches); the structural open questions (the ones he himself cannot answer and that will, unanswered, drive the next decompensation); the growth pathway (specific, achievable, and almost never offered to him); the catastrophe pathway (specific, achievable, and offered to him constantly); and the indicators a handler/therapist/teammate should track to know which road he is on at any given week.

---

### 6.1 The Dominant Trend Lines (Already in Motion)

**Progressive somatic destabilization.** Each death-and-return cycle has produced a body that holds its shape with less native cohesion. Early Wonder Man was simply *very strong and very durable.* Post-Force-Works Simon was a discorporated energy field that required another consciousness to anchor him into form. Post-Bendis Simon is solid by default but flares, disperses, and reconstitutes under emotional load — the body has become an EEG readout of the affect. The direction of travel is clear: the threshold for somatic destabilization is dropping, not rising. He is twenty years from a presentation in which sustained heroism in a high-stress combat environment is no longer physically reliable, because the load that produces dispersion is now ordinary rather than extraordinary. He will not notice this himself until it humiliates him in public.

**Declining cycle-time between ideological reversals.** The Zemo-to-Avengers reversal took one issue. The Avengers-to-Revengers reversal took roughly four publication decades. The post-Revengers re-integration was faster. The pacifism/aggression oscillations of the late Remender period are inside a single arc. The amplitude is not diminishing — the *frequency* is increasing. This is the signature of a stress system that no longer reconsolidates between insults; each new reframing arrives before the prior one has settled. Without intervention this trend converges on what looks like rapid-cycling moral inconsistency — to outside observers, *unreliability*; internally, an inability to locate ground.

**Hollywood-career drift toward self-parody and then toward retirement.** The acting work, originally a healthy sublimation, has aged into a brittle, self-aware late-career posture. He is increasingly cast as himself, in projects *about* him, which collapses the distinction between performance and life that was the entire therapeutic value of the sublimation. The next phase — already glimpsed in the most recent solo material — is the celebrity-memoir/celebrity-documentary phase, in which the performance is *autobiography*. This is dangerous: it requires him to articulate a coherent self for public consumption when no such coherent self exists, and it incentivizes him to commit publicly to whichever provisional self is most narratively satisfying that quarter.

**Slow attrition of the stabilizing relationships.** Pym's availability and bandwidth have decreased across decades. Wanda has moved through partnerships, motherhood-arcs, X-affiliation, and her own decompensations and recoveries — her capacity to function as Simon's mirror is structurally lower than it was, and her own work requires that it remain so. The Vision exists in iterations Simon did not contribute to. Beast's moral coordinates have warped. The Avengers as institution has churned so heavily that the version that *knows* Simon, contextually, is mostly gone. He is, in the slow background, losing the people whose continuity defined his.

**Brother-shaped vacancy.** Eric is dead, mostly, mostly. The Grim Reaper recurs in attenuated forms (clone, revenant, ionic echo, narrative invocation). Simon has never developed a peer-male relationship that is not haunted by Eric — the rivalry-and-rescue gestalt is the only template he has for fraternity. The vacancy is unfilled and is likely to be filled, at some point, by a figure who *resembles* Eric structurally (older, dominant, morally inverted, demanding Simon's loyalty against his judgment). This is the single most predictable manipulation surface on the subject.

---

### 6.2 Medium-Horizon Fork Points

The next decade-plus of Simon Williams's life will be decided at a small number of identifiable junctures. Each is foreseeable; each is, in principle, navigable.

**Fork A — The Next Death.** There will be one. The pattern is established. The question is *whose hand and in service of what.* A death-in-sacrifice for a teammate (the historical mode) returns him through the now-familiar mechanism — diminished, more fragile, but recognizably himself. A death-by-dissolution under his own ionic flare (the trend mode) returns him, if at all, as something that has to relearn it is Simon. A death engineered by an antagonist who *understands* the template-transfer history (a successor to Ultron, a salvaged Zemo project, a Reaper-derivative) risks return as a substrate that someone else is *writing on.* Probability ordering: sacrifice > flare > engineered. Severity ordering: engineered > flare > sacrifice. The fork point is whether anyone close to him has done the work of pre-arranging an anchor — a person, a recording, a ritual — that the reconstituting Simon can use to find his way back to *being Simon* rather than being a fresh template.

**Fork B — The Wanda Question, Re-Asked.** Wanda's life will, periodically, produce moments in which she is unattached, in distress, and within his orbit. At each such moment Simon will face the same choice he has faced four or five times already: pursue, or stand down. Pursuit, even successful pursuit, has historically produced the worst version of him — the version that withheld brain patterns from a dying friend. Standing down is the growth move and is the move he has, to date, never quite managed without external pressure. The fork is not *will she be available* (she will, eventually); the fork is *has he done enough self-work in the intervening time to recognize that his love for her is partly his need for her as the only stable mirror he has ever had, and to decline the role of mirror-husband on those grounds.*

**Fork C — The Mentor Offer.** Simon is now, by tenure, an elder. Younger powered figures will increasingly approach him for guidance, training, and the use of his name. He has never been a mentor. He has been mentored — badly (Zemo), well (Pym), inconsistently (Cap). The fork is whether he accepts a sustained mentor role, which would be the single most generative act available to him (it would force him to articulate values to a student and thereby commit to them in himself), or whether he ducks it because mentoring requires a stable self he does not believe he has. The likeliest failure mode here is the *celebrity mentor* — he accepts the role for the image of having accepted it, and disengages when the actual work begins.

**Fork D — The Project-About-Himself.** The biopic, the memoir, the documentary, the limited series. He will be offered one. He will almost certainly say yes. The fork is whether he engages it as a *reckoning* (in which case it could function as exposure therapy and public accountability for the Vision refusal, the Revengers, the embezzlement) or as a *rehabilitation* (in which case it codifies a sanitized narrative that he will then have to defend against contradicting reality, accelerating the splitting tendencies). The signal to watch is whether the project has a writer or director who is willing to make him uncomfortable. If everyone on set works for him, it is the bad version.

**Fork E — The Ideological Recruitment.** Someone will, again, approach Simon with a coherent grievance-narrative that explains his pain, names a culpable party, and offers him a corrective role. The Revengers was the first mature iteration; it will not be the last. The recruiter need not be malevolent — a sincere movement (anti-superhuman regulation, post-Krakoa species politics, AI-rights advocacy given his Vision-template entanglement) could capture him just as effectively. The fork is whether, at the recruitment moment, he has a peer present whom he trusts enough to say *let me think about this for a week.* He has historically not bought himself that week. Whether he buys himself that week next time is the single most useful predictor of the following decade.

**Fork F — The Template Question, Forced.** At some point, an event will require him to either *donate* engrams (to restore a Vision-successor, to seed a new synthezoid, to rescue a fragmenting ally) or *refuse* them. The original refusal is the unhealed wound. The opportunity for repair is real but the form it will take is almost certainly degraded — it will not be a clean repeat of the Vision dilemma; it will be a messier case where the right answer is not obvious. The fork is whether he uses it to discharge old guilt (in which case he may donate when he shouldn't) or whether he engages it as a present-tense ethical problem (in which case he might, finally, act as an adult about his own substance).

---

### 6.3 The Open Structural Questions

These are the questions Simon cannot answer about himself, has not been asked clearly by anyone qualified to press them, and which will — left open — continue to drive the cycle.

**Is he the same man.** The pre-Zemo Simon Williams was an organic human with a criminal record, a dead father, a brother he feared, and a failed company. The current entity shares memories with that man and a continuous (if interrupted) narrative identity, but the substrate is energy, the personality has been copied and instanced elsewhere, and the body has been reconstituted from dispersed states more than once. He does not know whether he is *Simon* or whether he is a *very good ongoing impression of Simon* that has, by sheer continuity of performance, earned the name. He cannot resolve this analytically. It can only be resolved relationally — by a sustained other who treats him as continuous and whom he trusts enough to believe.

**What does he want when Wanda is not the answer.** He has organized his interior life around her presence or absence for so long that he has not seriously asked what he would pursue if she were simply unavailable in a settled, non-tragic way. Career? Mentorship? Solitude? A different partner? He does not know. The avoidance of this question is the principal block on his individuation.

**What does he believe.** The Revengers position was wrong but it was the most coherent ideological statement he has ever made about anything other than his own grievances. Since recanting, he has not assembled a replacement worldview. The pacifism phases are reactive, not founded. He does not have a *politics*, an *ethics*, or a *theology* he can articulate without prompting. For a man whose name is *Wonder*, this is a striking absence. Until he assembles one, every charismatic ideologue who approaches him will have an open door.

**What is owed for the Vision refusal.** He has never made restitution. The Vision, in his various iterations, has not asked for it. Wanda has not asked for it. Simon has not offered it. The debt is unpaid and he knows it. Unpaid debts of this kind do not metabolize on their own; they re-present, often in the form of self-sabotage at moments of incipient happiness. He will undermine his own good periods, mildly, until this is addressed.

**Whether the brother is finished.** Eric is dead in the sense that matters legally; he is not finished in the sense that matters psychologically. Simon has never had a conversation, with anyone, in which he said clearly what his brother was to him and what his brother's death made him. Until he does, every dominant-male figure who enters his orbit will be auditioning for the role.

---

### 6.4 The Growth Pathway

A specific and unromantic account of what would actually move this subject forward. It is not what is usually offered to superhumans of his standing; it is what would work.

**A sustained, non-Avengers therapeutic relationship.** Weekly, years, with a clinician who is not impressed by him. The treatment frame should be trauma-informed, attachment-focused, and tolerant of the dissociative-spectrum identity work. He will perform for the therapist for the first six to twelve months; the work begins when he stops. The clinician must be someone who can survive his ionic flares without flinching, which constrains the pool but does not empty it. This is the single highest-leverage intervention available.

**An articulated values document, written by him, revised annually.** A literal artifact: a few pages, in his own words, of what he believes and why. Not for publication. The discipline of writing it would force the integration he has avoided. The annual revision would let him see his own drift and, crucially, *own* it rather than enact it unconsciously.

**A reparative act toward the Vision.** Not a grand gesture. Something small, sustained, and useful — a standing offer of engrams in any future emergency, formalized; a public correction of the historical record where he has minimized his role; a private conversation with whichever Vision is current in which he says, without softening, *what I did was wrong and the reason was jealousy.* The act matters less than the speaking.

**A mentee, taken seriously.** Not a sidekick. A younger powered person, ideally one with their own identity-coherence issues, whom Simon commits to for a multi-year arc. The therapeutic value runs in his direction more than the mentee's. He cannot remain incoherent while modeling coherence; the role would force assembly.

**A romantic relationship that is not Wanda.** Not as substitution. As *practice* — practice at being loved by someone who is not also his cosmological anchor. Any partner who can tolerate the volatility and is not seeking to fix him would suffice. The criterion is that *she does not need to be his mirror* and that *he does not need her to be.* He has, to date, not had this experience as an adult.

**A retirement plan for the body.** A pre-arranged protocol for what is to be done if his form destabilizes catastrophically — who is to be called, what anchor (recording, person, ritual) is to be presented, what consent he has given in advance for what kinds of reconstitution. The act of *making the plan* is half the value: it requires him to take seriously that he is mortal in the ways that matter and to specify a continuous self worth recovering.

None of these are dramatic. All of them are available. He has, to date, attempted none of them systematically.

---

### 6.5 The Catastrophe Pathway

Equally specific. What it looks like when he goes the other way — and he is, on the current trend, slightly more likely to go this way than the other.

**The capture cascade.** A charismatic figure (a former antagonist rebranded as a reformer, a movement leader, a synthetic successor to the Vision) offers him a comprehensive narrative explaining his pain, naming the Avengers (or Stark-successors, or human institutions, or organic life itself) as the problem, and giving him a role. He accepts within a week, without consultation. The first acts are speeches and public gestures. The middle acts are sabotage. The final act is direct violence against former teammates. Unlike the Revengers, this iteration would be harder to walk back because the cycle-time has shortened and the witnesses-who-knew-him-before have thinned.

**The dissolution event.** A combat or emotional crisis at a moment of low cohesion produces a dispersion he cannot self-reconstitute. He persists as a diffuse ionic field — conscious, distressed, unable to act. Recovery requires another consciousness to anchor him; if Wanda is unavailable or unwilling, recovery may take years or be partial. The Simon who reconstitutes may be missing affect, missing memory, or missing the moral floor that has, until now, always held.

**The substrate hijack.** Following a death or dispersion, his engrams or ionic pattern are used by an antagonist as the template for something else — a synthezoid, a weapon, a doppelganger — that walks the world wearing his name. He returns to find himself preceded by a counterfeit, and the question *am I real* receives, finally, a publicly contested answer. This is the worst psychological outcome on the board and is technically achievable by multiple existing actors in the milieu.

**The public unmasking.** The biopic/memoir project goes badly. Old footage, classified records, or a hostile journalist surfaces the embezzlement, the Vision refusal, the Revengers manifesto, and Zemo's original recruitment in a single integrated narrative aimed at the public. He cannot defend it because the facts are correct. The career collapses; the parasocial mirror that has stabilized him collapses with it; he retreats, drinks (newly, late, badly — the ionic metabolism notwithstanding, he will try), or accepts the first capture offer he is made.

**The brother-shaped figure.** A new dominant-male presence enters his life — possibly a Reaper-successor, possibly something more ambiguous, possibly someone he himself has unknowingly created by his prolonged refusal to grieve Eric — and Simon attaches to the rivalry-and-rescue gestalt with the same helpless intensity he showed his actual brother. Whichever way this plays (he tries to save the figure; he tries to defeat the figure; he becomes the figure's instrument), it eats years.

**The slow fade.** Least dramatic, most likely. No catastrophic event. He simply continues to oscillate, with diminishing amplitude in the moral signal and increasing amplitude in the affective noise; he takes fewer roles; he is invited to fewer missions; he becomes a figure who is *around*, who *was important once*, who flares occasionally and is quietly stabilized by whichever junior teammate is on call. He is not destroyed. He is attenuated until the difference between him and his absence is small.

---

### 6.6 Indicators to Track

For any handler, teammate, partner, or clinician monitoring the subject, the following are the load-bearing signals. None require unusual access; most are visible to anyone in regular contact.

**Speech patterns.** Increased use of the third-person ("Wonder Man would..."), increased rehearsed-soundbite quality in casual conversation, and reduction in unprompted self-deprecation are all signals of persona-thickening — he is performing a self because the underlying one is thin. Conversely, return of dry self-mockery, return of references to the embezzlement era, and willingness to be quiet in a room are signals of integration.

**Costume and grooming.** Reversion to the most theatrical costume iterations correlates with low cohesion. Settled, simpler dress correlates with stability. Attention to facial-hair styling that tracks current screen-roles indicates the performance/life seam is collapsing.

**Ionic baseline.** Visible luminosity at rest, micro-flares during ordinary conversation, perceptible warmth at arm's length — all indicate the somatic-affective load is high and the threshold is dropping. A clinician should be summoned before a mission is undertaken.

**Wanda-references per week.** Above a personal baseline (which a longitudinal handler can establish), it predicts a Wanda-adjacent decompensation within roughly two months. Below baseline, often, paradoxically, the same — sustained avoidance of mention indicates active suppression.

**Engagement with mentees / juniors.** Sustained, mundane, slightly bored mentoring activity is the strongest positive indicator available. Performative mentoring (photo ops, public statements, no follow-up) is a negative indicator and predicts a capture-cascade attempt within twelve to eighteen months.

**Sleep / downtime behavior.** He does not biologically require sleep, but his behavior in the unstructured hours is diagnostic. Reading, watching others' work, calling old teammates, walking — stable. Endless rewatching of his own films, drafting unsent letters to Wanda, scripting public statements he has not been asked for — unstable.

**Response to criticism.** A measured response, including a willingness to sit with the criticism overnight, is the single best indicator of present cohesion. Immediate counter-narrative, public rebuttal, or theatrical concession ("you're right, I'm a monster") in equal measure indicate the shame substrate is hot and an episode is near.

**Contact with Pym.** Maintained contact, even infrequent, is protective. Lapse of contact for more than several months is correlated with subsequent poor decisions. He uses Pym, whether he knows it or not, as an external superego that he trusts because it has been broken and survived.

---

### 6.7 Synthesis

The trajectory of Simon Williams is not tragic and it is not triumphal. It is *open*, in a way that few subjects of this depth and tenure remain open. He is too sincere to be lost and too fragmented to be safe. He is, after sixty years of record, still capable of growth and still capable of catastrophe, and the gap between them is narrower than his public persona suggests and wider than his private despair admits.

The single sentence that should sit at the top of any forward-looking file on him is this: *he is a man waiting to be assembled, who keeps trying to assemble himself in front of a mirror, and the next person who hands him a mirror — for good or ill — will write the next decade.* The interventions that work are slow, unglamorous, relational, and require a sustained other who is not impressed. The catastrophes that loom are fast, narratively satisfying, offered to him frequently, and require only that he say yes once.

He has, historically, said yes to the wrong thing about once per decade. He has, historically, said yes to the right thing about once per decade. The base rate is not encouraging and is not damning. The job of anyone who cares about him — and the implicit job of this file — is to ensure that, at the next fork, the right offer is in the room and the wrong offer is not the only one being made.

Watcher's note: the subject is worth the trouble. He has died for others repeatedly and meant it each time. Files of this depth are usually written about people who do not deserve them. This one does.
